# 庚道集

**Collected Alchemical Methods of Geng Dao**

**Title:** *Geng Dao Ji* (*Collected Alchemical Methods of Geng Dao*). Author unknown. According to Chen Guofu’s research, the elixir methods recorded herein were mostly composed by Tang and Song dynasty practitioners, with a few later additions from the Yuan and Ming dynasties. The text compiles over twenty external alchemical formulas and instructions, rich in content. In nine fascicles.

**Source:** *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongshen* Section, *Zhongshu* Category.

---

**Fascicle One**

**Method for Nurturing Cinnabar with Arsenic in a Sealed Vessel**

Take half a catty of pure, stone-free arsenic, crushed to the size of mung beans—this is best. Divide into portions of two taels each, wrap in white paper, and place inside a coarse cloth bag.

Harvest *xiaku* grass in season, dry it in the sun, burn to ash, and steep in boiling water to extract a thick infusion. Suspend the infusion in a porcelain jar with a false bottom and boil. Frequently replenish the liquid. After five or six days, the cloth bag will gradually lighten as the infusion thickens. Test over fire: if smoke appears, the process is complete.

Then boil the medicine in the infusion. By the seventh or eighth day, the medicine will dissolve into the liquid. If a small residue remains, it is merely mineral dregs—no need to consume it entirely.

Transfer the medicinal infusion to another jar and simmer slowly until it dries into a dark brown mass—this is the "subdued" state. Dry thoroughly over a slow fire, ensuring no moisture remains, then place in the crucible, seal tightly, and set in an ash basin. Apply a top fire of one and a half taels, positioned one and a half *cun* away, and nurture for three days. Gradually increase to two taels and nurture for three seven-day periods.

Inspect the sealed vessel—if undisturbed, continue nurturing until the thirty-fifth day. Upon opening, if the contents appear ashen white with a watery sheen on top, the elixir is complete. Test by burning: if smoke persists, the spirit has not yet departed. Crush with an iron spoon, add milk, reseal, and nurture for another month.

Upon reopening, if the elixir is yellow and gradually dries without moisture, burn again over fire. If it melts without smoke, the death is complete—but not yet true death. Repeat the previous method, sealing and nurturing for another month. When the medicine becomes white and lustrous, burning like stone without melting, it has truly died. The frost-like ash has been nurtured away, leaving only the pure, dead essence of the mineral.

Crush into rice-sized grains for storage. This method is peerless—no other compares. The oral instructions and manual techniques are all herein.

---

**Method for Boiling and Nurturing Cinnabar**

Take two taels of fine cinnabar, pound with *yuxing* grass and rice vinegar to extract the juice, and boil in a suspended vessel for seven *fu* periods. Remove, wrap the cinnabar in coarse grass, place in a sealed vessel or jar, and seal tightly. Apply a slow fire for one firing cycle. Alternatively, use a water jar beneath—this is even better.

Take the cinnabar, pound with the aforementioned coarse grass to form a storage vessel, place one tael inside, and nurture with top fire aligned to the *mao* and *you* directions for three *fu* periods. Remove, wrap the cinnabar in *Kunlun* paper, attach dead alum to the body, place in the mother vessel, and seal for nurturing for four seven-day periods. Increase the top fire to one and a half taels, then stop at two taels. When the days are complete, the cinnabar is subdued.

Use the vessel to nurture the body, then proceed to nurture powdered frost.

---

**Powder Method**

Beat two to four *sheng* of material—this is optimal. Take four taels of powdered frost, hard as crystal, and shape into small pieces. First wrap in white paper, then place in a dense silk bag. Boil in an infusion of lotus leaf ash for five *fu* periods.

Next, boil in the juice of *juxue* grass (a five-topped grass) and *jiandao* grass (water chestnut) for one *fu* period. Affix genuine silver foil to the body, or wrap the powder in silver foil, and place in a vessel with dead cinnabar. Forge a divine chamber from pure silver, first lining the bottom with cinnabar, then layering the powder, followed by another layer of cinnabar. Repeat the layering, then cover the top with dead cinnabar. Seal with mud and dry thoroughly. Place inside a vessel with dead arsenic, sealing as before.

Apply a top fire of two taels and nurture for seven seven-day periods. Test by burning: if no smoke appears, the process is complete. If not, nurture an additional *qian* to transmute one tael into top-grade treasure.

If the cinnabar vessel loses potency over time, remove the powdered frost and cinnabar together, grind with milk into a *qian* of powder, and transmute one tael. Then prepare a new vessel according to the above method—this is wondrous and divine. Do not treat it lightly.

---

**General Vessel Methods**

The divine chamber within the vessel should be forged thickly—do not make it thin.

Take one catty of white alum (not *mingfan*), pound, and steep in a thick infusion of wheat straw ash, one large cupful. Place in a porcelain vessel and drip-cook the alum until the liquid evaporates and the alum turns to water. Dry slowly over fire.

Then place the alum in a porcelain jar, seal tightly, and dry. Set in an ash basin, apply a top fire of two taels, and nurture for three *fu* periods. Remove and use as needed.

**Black Donkey Juice** (also called *mumi* or paper mulberry juice): Divide eight taels into four portions and grind into coarse powder. Wrap each two-tael portion first in two layers of white paper, then in coarse cloth, and suspend in grass juice. Boil in four small jars, covering the mouths with paper. Replenish the liquid as it dries. Frequently lift and agitate the cloth bags to facilitate dissolution. If a small residue remains, collect it and transfer to another jar to simmer. When three to five parts have dried, pour the liquid back and continue simmering until fully dry. Dry slowly over fire, break the jar, and combine the residue with the previously undissolved medicine. Grind finely.

Initially, eight taels of medicine will yield an increased weight when combined with frost. Seal and nurture in a vessel, opening once a month. After three to four months, the frost will have nurtured away the ash, leaving only the original medicine, snow-white and subdued.

For the aforementioned *xiaku* grass ash infusion: line the bottom of a wicker sieve with a layer of paper, pour the ash, and drip the liquid slowly. Collect in a clean porcelain vessel, let settle, and decant the clear liquid into another vessel. Repeat the settling process, retaining only the clear liquid and discarding the ash residue. This is the proper method for boiling medicine.

For all eight minerals, thorough boiling, refining, nurturing, and subduing are required before reversing the fire’s work. Only after prolonged processing do they die. Alum can be steeped and rinsed to sprout buds, which are then used to make rinsing vessels. The buds are rinsed again, sprouted anew, and this process is repeated until nine transformations are complete. Only then can the vessel be used to nurture cinnabar and mercury for medicinal consumption.

**Method for Calcining Cinnabar**
Take one *liang* of bright cinnabar and place it in a small crucible, approximately one *liang* in capacity. Add the cinnabar, then seal the mouth with *geng* (refined lead or tin), ensuring no gaps, and secure tightly. Place this within a clay crucible, then set a water-filled *ding* (tripod vessel) atop it, its copper base resting upon the *geng*. Fill the outer vessel with water and seal it tightly. Dry thoroughly. Calcine with twelve *jin* of fuel for about a day, then allow to cool. The mercury within the cinnabar will volatilize and condense upon the *geng*, appearing white and dry. Remove it, then repeat the calcination process as before. After several cycles, approximately four *liang* of dry mercury may be obtained, which can be cast into vessels to nurture the Three Yellows and other medicines, all of which will be subdued.

**Nine-Transformation Method for Boiling Arsenic Powder**
**Method for Boiling Powder**
Take *da huang* (rhubarb), *wu bei zi* (gallnut), *shan zhi* (gardenia), *chuan jiao* (Sichuan pepper), and *xi xin* (asarum), along with ginger juice, honey, and thick rice vinegar. Boil them together with water for a full day until the mixture turns black, which is the proper standard. Once dry, calcine again—this method is extraordinary. Know that this is the immortal’s art, left for alchemists as a foundational practice.

The above method uses *da huang*, *wu bei zi*, *shan zhi zi*, *chuan jiao*, and *xi xin*, ground into a coarse powder. Then, take two bowls each of fresh ginger juice, honey, and rice vinegar, mix with water, and suspend the powder in a cloth bag to boil for a day until the *fen shuang* (arsenic frost) turns black. Collect the powder separately, then calcine it with arsenic.

**Method for Boiling Arsenic**
*He zi* (chebulic myrobalan) and *yuan zhi* (polygala) are weighed,
*Di fu* (broom cypress), *niu xi* (achyranthes), and *ku shen* (sophora),
*Zhi mu* (anemarrhena), *qiang hua* (wolfsbane), and *da ji* (euphorbia)—
Steep them in river water, boiled to perfection.
Enclose in a silk pouch, the mysterious womb method,
Day and night, gently apply even heat.
Aiding the great medicine, none compare,
Transformation upon transformation, the Great Vehicle unfolds.

The above method uses equal parts of *he zi*, *yuan zhi*, *di fu zi*, *du niu xi*, *ku shen*, *zhi mu*, *qiang hua*, and *da ji*, ground coarsely and mixed with arsenic. Place them in a silk bag and boil in river water for a day and night. Remove, dry in an ash box, then grind into powder.

**Method for Calcining Arsenic Powder**
Bury a lamp dish level with the ground,
First wipe the interior with *hai zhi* (pig fat).
Lay *yin mu* (silver mother) as desired at the bottom,
Then arrange the boiled powder evenly upon it.
Place the boiled arsenic atop the powder,
Three parts powder to five parts arsenic by weight.
Mix *di fu* ash with *che qian zi* (plantain seed),
Layer them by weight atop the arsenic.
Seal all gaps beneath the dish,
Then apply mature fire, spreading it evenly.
Calcine with a three-*jin* fire’s force,
Remove one *jin* of fuel, cover the medicine with ash.

The above method uses a lamp dish buried in the earth. First, lightly burn *hai zhi* within it, then add *yin mu sha* (silver mother sand) or *yin mu* powder as desired. Next, place the *fen shuang* (arsenic frost), then the boiled arsenic atop it, covering the *fen shuang*. Above this, use three ingredients: *di fu*, *che qian zi* ash, and herbal powder, piled atop the arsenic. Apply three *jin* of mature fire, reducing it by two *jin*, then withdraw the fire and cover with cold ash. Once cool, separate the arsenic and powder, storing each apart. Repeat this process three times before use.

When arsenic and powder are calcined to spiritual efficacy,
The fields’ crops are already sown.
They say it guards the poor scholar,
And indeed, this is clearly so.
It can transmute red silver into treasure,
Fit to craft vessels of refinement.
The powder can transform red substances,
The arsenic can nurture the silver’s body.

The above method explains: If following the transmutation process in sequence, at this stage, great accomplishment is possible. First, take *lu* (green pigment) to refine red silver, transforming it into an infant, which is then bathed in the Jade Pool three times. After feeding it the Heavenly Mother’s milk three times, the red color is shed. The Heavenly Mother’s milk is the arsenic atop the vessel. For one *liang* of red substance, use one *qian* and a half of Heavenly Mother’s milk, applying it three times. Once the infant has shed its garments, use the White Snow Divine Elixir to guide it into the immortal realm, where it becomes celestial bone. The White Snow Divine Elixir is *fen shuang*. Apply it in three stages: first, let the infant return to the mother, consume the Heavenly Milk, and transform with the mother. Then, bathe it again in the Jade Pool to purify it. Apply the Divine Elixir three times, then briefly use *chu shan qian* (lead from the mountain’s depths) and *lao shuang* (aged frost) to refine its form, naturally forging a great vessel.

If using *da qi shuang* (great seven-frost grains), the highest grade is pure; half-pure is middling; *xiao san qi* (small three-seven) is the lowest. This is but a rough outline of the greater work—use your discretion. The powder serves as a vessel, the *chang nü* (ever-maiden) as the infant, and the household’s greater work is the *san qi mu sha* (three-seven mother cinnabar). If using arsenic as the vessel, nurture the White Snow as the Divine Elixir. Once the elixir is complete, transformations are endless. The arsenic vessel also becomes a great medicine, and the spiritual cinnabar and mother cinnabar together form the great vessel.

First transformation: Arsenic vessel nurtures *zhu ling* (vermilion spirit).
Second transformation: Within *zhu ling*, cinnabar forms spontaneously.
Third transformation: Within cinnabar, nurture *jiao gong sha* (mercury sand), which is the sand that responds to heaven and earth’s darkness.
Fourth transformation: Within mercury sand, nurture *yu xiao qiong zhi* (jade laughter, jasper branches).
Fifth transformation: Within *yu xiao*, cinnabar is refined anew.
Sixth transformation: Take half a *jin* or one *jin* and sixteen *liang* of cinnabar, aligning with the celestial pattern. Place the divine treasure within the cinnabar, nurturing four *liang* of it as the great work’s endless cycle.
For the great elixir, mix with *chu* juice (paper mulberry), form into pills the size of *tong* seeds (tung tree seeds). One pill extends life; one pill dries mercury.
Seventh transformation: Within the divine chamber, nurture one *liang* of *ci xiong* (male and female) as the great medicine, which transforms into the Gold Mother. Its form shifts from white to red, then returns to luminous red. This red *geng* (lead) is the return to the original source.

Eighth transformation: Within cinnabar, nurture the male and female to cultivate *geng*. Take eight *liang* of cinnabar to nurture two *liang* of male and female; after forty-nine days, four *liang* are achieved. Combine the embryo with *geng* and nurture it within the divine chamber. When the days are complete, the medicine is obtained—one *qian* can transmute cinnabar-silver into red *geng*.

Ninth transformation: Use the male and female as the crucible; the cinnabar-male is called the Great Elixir Medicine. Take one *liang* each of cinnabar, male, and female, place them within the former male-female crucible, and nurture them in the *geng* divine chamber. After forty-nine days, use one *jin* of the former medicine as the crucible—this is the great wonder, completing the celestial pattern. Form into pills with *chu* juice, the size of *wutong* seeds. One pill can dry ten *liang* of mercury, producing superior *geng*.

The firing regimen is as follows, now appended again:
For the first through fourth transformations, apply fire once daily, two *liang* each morning and evening. On the third day, add one *liang*, making three *liang*. From the third to the sixth day, increase by one *liang* again, making four *liang*. The fire’s intensity should be moderated to maturity; if the heat is excessive, adjust gradually—this is optimal. The ash may be raised without hindrance.
For the fifth through seventh transformations, follow the usual method. After seven days, replace with four *liang* of mature fire daily, ensuring no deficiency, though it need not reach five *liang*.
For the Great Medicine’s forty-nine-day cycle, proceed gradually, without applying five *liang* of fire; thereafter, the same applies.

*The Precious Formula for the Golden Elixir and Great Medicine of Master Wen Zhen*
Dong Qi’s Culaishan Retired Elder, Cui Fang Huishu, styled Master Wen Zhen, compiled this formula for the Great Elixir Medicine, with a postscript following the *Bencao*. Here, extraneous methods are omitted, and only the most extraordinary are recorded, to be elaborated in a separate compilation, preserving their renown.
Written by Mengxuan Resident of the Wuji Hall in the Quande Abbey of Nanyue, during the Zhongyuan Festival of the Jiazi year of the Shaoxing reign.

In the Qingli reign’s guiwei year, Fang was appointed to Hunan, where he pacified the Yao and Liao tribes of Jingxi Cave and governed the northeastern precincts of Wugang County, three hundred *li* distant from Changsha. At that time, the former chief minister Liu Chongzhi governed Tanzhou and summoned Fang to oversee construction, whereupon Fang moved his family to reside at the Green Robe Temple. One day, a local man named Li Bi visited—aged around seventy, his complexion ruddy and youthful—who discoursed extensively on elixir arts. He then bestowed upon Fang the method for the Cinnabar Elixir of the Perfected Lord Wei. Upon examining its procedures, Fang found no discrepancies, though its hidden subtleties remained obscure. Bi urged him again: "You should undertake this." The method employed two parts sulphur to eight parts mercury, placed in the water-and-fire crucible and refined through nine cycles, whereupon it would naturally coalesce. Though Fang had official duties, he often found leisure. Following the method, he performed the nine cycles, yet the result was mere quicksilver. He questioned Bi, who had no answer. Fang pondered deeply: the method was profoundly ingenious, but without grasping the immortals’ secret instructions, success was impossible.

Later, while stationed on garrison duty, he journeyed to Mount Heng and paid homage to Master Yangsu Lan, seeking enlightenment. Master Lan said: "This method is exceedingly refined and most easily executed. Yet you have not mastered the immortal classics, hence the disparity between sulphur and mercury. In the first cycle, add two *liang* of sulphur; by the sixth cycle, gradually reduce it, and in the seventh cycle, add no sulphur at all. For sulphur is the utmost yang, and mercury the utmost yin. Each time they are stir-fried and sealed in the crucible, fire is applied until halted. Only by the seventh cycle does the mercury cease to volatilize, thus achieving subjugation. After nine cycles, transfer it to an external furnace for nurturing, following distinct fire regimens, then calcine to remove the sulphur, leaving the mercury as a solitary essence to form the elixir treasure."

Fang then understood Li Bi’s words and bowed in gratitude. From Master Lan’s instructions, every preparation he undertook thereafter met with precision. This elixir, in its highest use, grants eternal life; in its middle use, aids others; and in its lowest, enriches one’s household. The key lies in holding a generous heart and eschewing greed—thus is the Dao accomplished.

Disciple Cui Fang of Daliang respectfully records this.
Eulogy to the Perfected Lord Wei, annotated by Lan Zizhen.

Refine the cinnabar according to ancient methods: two parts sulphur to eight parts mercury, stir-fried to form "green gold." Then grind it finely before placing it in the water-and-fire crucible for calcination. Initially, the ratio of two to eight governs the union of Heaven and Earth—its meaning is noted above. On the second day, do not alter the Celestial Origin; stir-fry and refine eight times, following the same method as before. Only then is it called the "divine achievement with full cycles." From the first to the seventh, it becomes "spirit sand." For the third cycle, halve the sulphur: use one tael. In the fourth, the solitary yang must not be scattered—when stir-frying with the same amount of sulphur, ensure no loss, and gather it meticulously. For the fifth, do not add to the three parts: use seven mace and five candareens of sulphur, applied beneath the furnace. In the sixth, not even half a grain should be recklessly released: use half a tael of sulphur. By the seventh, it is confined within the "fire dwelling"; after seven transformations, it turns red and becomes green—this is the "wood within fire." It is also said: "The dragon emerges from within the fire." After being captured and subdued by sulphur seven times, it can no longer ascend, and thus is tamed by fire to form the treasure. In the eighth, the celestial soul must not be allowed to dissipate—the green gold solidifies, leaving no free mercury. The ninth is called the "returning elixir" or "reverted yang": after nine cycles, the yin reverts to yang nature. The dead who consume it will revive.

After the green gold forms the elixir, place a single grain upon a crane’s crown. Have dozens of skilled archers shoot at it from fifty paces away, yet none will strike it all day. This elixir greatly extends human life and restores departed souls. Each of the nine stir-frying cycles demands meticulous care. The fire regimen uses five catties throughout, from the first to the ninth cycle. For the fifth cycle, discard the key and fan the fire, using a total of forty-five catties of charcoal. Nurture the spirit sand to resist fire: with each refining to the third cycle, its color becomes exquisite. Then incorporate this sand into the nine-cycle green gold and nurture it further, so that it resists fire and becomes a treasure. Only with the "golden lord" can fruition be achieved.

Once fire resistance is complete, take lead and refine it in the "flower pool." Use one tael of "river chariot" to two taels of lead—a lead-to-sand ratio of two to one. Refine it until it gleams like snow, then it is ready. After the elixir is completed, use what you have gained to offer thanks to Heaven and Earth, aiding the orphaned, impoverished, and afflicted. Practice kindness without greed. Thus shall you escape the dust of the mortal world and avoid sinking into oblivion. By bestowing blessings upon all beings and establishing merit and virtue, Heaven will protect you, granting long life and ascension to the Golden Gates, where you shall wander and feast in the Jade Capital.

*Method for the Cold Grove Jade Tree and Gushing Spring Vault*
First, prepare the spirit sand...

Two taels of superior sulfur and eight taels of mercury are ground together until thoroughly blended. Place them in a ceramic water-and-fire crucible, seal the crucible’s mouth with purified clay, and secure it with iron wire. Position water and charcoal above the crucible, then apply a ring of fire around it to refine the spirit sand. When the water atop the crucible has evaporated to five shallow cups and no sound emerges from within, the process is complete. Withdraw the fire, remove the spirit sand, and split it into dice-shaped lumps.

Grind equal parts Sichuan peppercorn, white atractylodes, Sichuan aconite, and arisaema into fine powder—enough to coat the aforementioned spirit sand lumps. Place the sand in a raw silk pouch, tie it securely, and suspend it in a large sand bowl filled with aged rice vinegar using bamboo skewers, ensuring the pouch does not touch the bottom. Boil the vinegar until dry, then remove the pouch. Gently pat the spirit sand dry with soft cloth, and when slightly damp, coat it with iron filings for bodily application. Store it securely.

Prepare an airtight Xinzhou sandalwood box. Take the finest silver filings or beads, spread a layer of silver beads at the bottom, then arrange the spirit sand lumps like lotus seedpods atop them. Cover with another layer of silver beads. If any spirit sand remains, add another layer of silver beads above the empty space, then cover the sand lumps again. Once the top and bottom are fully layered, place a round piece of Kunlun paper (dyed with high-quality ink) over the contents and sprinkle a small amount of table salt on it.

Seal the box’s opening with water-mixed white kaolin, secure it with iron wire, and fashion a loop at the top for lifting. Coat the exterior of the box with a uniform layer of clay, roughly one fen thick, pressing firmly to prevent cracks. Allow it to dry in the shade.

Prepare a large sugar jar large enough to hold the sandalwood box. Fill it nine-tenths full with temple paper-money ash that has been fired until glowing red. First, add half the ash, then place the box inside, and cover it completely with the remaining ash.

Cut high-quality white charcoal into three-inch segments, weigh them, and ignite until glowing red. Place them in the jar, keeping them three to four cun from the box’s top. Nurture the fire for five days:
- On the first day, use four taels of charcoal.
- On the second day, use five taels.

On the third day, use six taels of charcoal.
On the fourth day, use seven taels.
On the fifth day, use eight taels.
After five days are complete, remove the numinous cinnabar and continue nurturing it.

The firing regimen requires adding charcoal only at dawn each day, continuing until the following dawn. This aligns with the sun’s celestial movement, embodying the natural subtlety of withdrawal and replenishment. Those who do not understand this—adding charcoal at dawn and dusk—disrupt the workings of creation, severing the root of Heaven and Earth’s generative power and losing the origin of yin-yang transformation, thus leading to failure.

The method: for every four taels of silver pearl, nurture one tael of numinous cinnabar. When accumulated in sufficient quantity, remove the mother (residue), using only the already-nurtured numinous cinnabar ground into powder. Again, use four taels to nurture one tael. For unnurtured cinnabar, wait until five days have passed and a surplus is obtained, then take four taels of this numinous cinnabar powder, pour it over one tael of mercury, seal it at the center, and apply the firing regimen as before to secure it. After the nurturing period is complete, sprouts will naturally emerge, which are to be plucked as they grow.

This charcoal must be the fine white charcoal from Luzicibiao in Jiande County, Yanzhou—only that which, when struck like a deer’s leg, does not break is superior. Charcoal from other places is unsuitable.

[...] lotus-form.

The "Two-Eight Numinous Cinnabar" Method

Take two taels of finely ground sulfur paste and eight taels of mercury—only the white variety is to be used; black mercury is unsuitable. Place these two ingredients together in a mortar, gradually add half a cup of rice vinegar, and grind them evenly into a fine mixture. Pour this into an iron pan, first coating the pan with sesame oil. Stir continuously over a slow fire until it forms cinnabar grains. Return it to the mortar and grind finely again. Then pour it back into the iron pan, stir continuously over a slow fire until it forms grains once more, and this is called "Green-Gold Head." Grind it finely again, place it in a crucible, and cover it with a *jian* bowl filled with water. Take two taels of red halloysite, two taels of calcined glauberite, and half a tael of calcined lead oxide, grind them evenly, and mix with rice vinegar to form a paste. Seal the crucible’s seams with this paste, bind it securely with thick iron wire, and attach two iron wire loops for threading the iron firing rod. Place it over a slow fire to dry, adding a bit more powder as needed. Then gradually apply a layer of *guan* clay, drying each layer before adding the next. When sealing, the fire must not be too fierce, lest the medicine escape. Once the seal is over an inch thick, it can withstand the firing. Then place it in the furnace, with the iron firing rod standing outside the furnace and a horizontal iron rod on either side to suspend the water-fire cauldron. Fill the water cauldron with water, replenishing as it evaporates. Begin with a small amount of charcoal, gradually increasing to eight catties, but only fill to the midpoint of the water-fire cauldron. Pack the charcoal tightly to prevent the escape of fire qi. If the ashes accumulate, remove the charcoal and repack it tightly. If flames appear, cover the wind holes with cloth. When the charcoal is spent—or when five cups of water remain—remove the water-fire cauldron and place it in another furnace to cool. First remove all the *guan* clay, then the iron wires, then the water cauldron. Use the back of a knife to break the lower segment of the fire cauldron, then lightly tap the upper segment to retrieve the medicine. Pick out the ashes and grind the medicine until no sound is heard.

If further refinement is desired, add one tael of raw sulfur to ten taels of numinous cinnabar, along with the Green-Gold Head, which is optimal. Then grind them together finely and seal as before. For the *guan* clay, use fine yellow clay mixed with paper fiber and four taels of salt, kneaded with water the day before. Prepare the water-fire cauldron with sufficient water, and use the paper-fiber salt clay to form a rim and base, piercing six or seven small holes before drying. Without these holes, the cauldron may float and not sit firmly. After adding the medicine, seal the small holes with the sealing paste, level the base, and seal the seams. Use three taels of red halloysite ground into fine powder and mixed with rice vinegar for sealing. Use charcoal without bark, cut into three-inch pieces, totaling about sixteen catties. Prepare three iron wires, three iron firing rods, half a cup of rice vinegar, a small amount of sesame oil, and five cups of water before placing it in the furnace.

**Sealing and Calcining Method**
First grind the sulfur extremely fine before adding the mercury, grinding together from *mao* (5–7 a.m.) to *you* (5–7 p.m.), or from *chen* (7–9 a.m.) to *xu* (7–9 p.m.), until they are thoroughly combined and no mercury globules remain. Do not pause even briefly, for if you stop, it may take two or three days to recombine. When placing the mixture in the crucible, warm it slightly first, and heat the crucible as well. Use a two-to-eight salt-clay mixture to seal the crucible’s opening: eight parts salt to two parts clay, mixed with good vinegar and pounded thousands of times. Seal the furnace tightly in seven layers, and once the seal is dry, begin the firing. Start with four bowls of base fire, ensuring no ghostly flames arise. Gradually add fire until it reaches the midpoint of the crucible. Another sealing method involves adding a small amount of needle-like iron filings to red halloysite, mixed with *guan* clay and vinegar, which is excellent. Another calcining method involves placing the water-fire cauldron in the furnace as usual and calcining for one *fu* period (twelve hours). For the second refinement, add sulfur; by the third refinement, omit the water cauldron and place a ceramic vessel beneath it to cover the water cauldron, applying top fire for calcining. This method is uniquely effective, embodying the principles of *jiji* (completion) and *weiji* (incompletion). This formula was transmitted by Chen Benren of Tiantai; it is most wondrous and must be kept secret, not recklessly disclosed.

**Hua-Chi (Flower Pool) Method**
Mix lime with oyster-shell lime, knead with hot water to form a dish, and place the "Golden Duke" (mercury) with the extracted numinous cinnabar. Heat them together until white, and the treasure is complete.

**Mercury-Washing Method**
Rub the mercury with rice until the rice turns white. Then rub it with rush pith until the pith no longer blackens.

**Refined Mercury Method**
Take transparent cinnabar, regardless of size, grind it into powder, and mix it evenly with charcoal powder and glutinous rice water. Place it in a crucible, and use an iron rod to shape it into a honeycomb-like structure, allowing it to dry. Prepare another pot, bury it in the ground, and fill it with water to eight-tenths capacity. Place the crucible with the dried cinnabar on top of the buried water pot, seal the seams tightly with paper-fiber clay, and dry it over a fire. Use five catties of charcoal, igniting the fire from the top. When the crucible turns red-hot, remove the charcoal. Once cool, retrieve the refined mercury from the buried water pot. From one tael of ordinary cinnabar, only eight *fen* of mercury is obtained.

**Fire-Taming Cinnabar**
Take four taels of cinnabar and boil it in a cup of rice vinegar until dry. Coat the cinnabar with ink and vinegar, place it in a bag made of fine silk, and tie it tightly. Grind egg white with ink and coat the silk bag, allowing it to dry. Grind the kernel of a green silkworm cocoon into powder, mix it with honey, and knead the cinnabar into a firm ball. Place it in a sand container, lining the bottom with chopped *guanzhu* leaves (green silkworm cocoon leaves).

Then place the cinnabar inside, cover it with another layer of *guanzhu* leaves, and seal the seams of the container with liver-mixed clay. Bind the container crosswise with iron wire and let it dry. Extract juice from daylily roots and mix it with clay to thoroughly seal all joints.

Arrange ashes around the base of the container, leaving only the top exposed, and encircle it with a single layer of charcoal. Ignite a fire from the top until the container is thoroughly heated.

**Method for Polishing Cinnabar to a Gold-like Luster**
Apply a paste of iron oxide powder mixed with water, let it sit overnight, then polish it repeatedly with several layers of silk until the cinnabar gleams like gold.

**Method for Polishing Cinnabar to a Silver-like Luster**
Grind mercury, *Centella asiatica* (Indian pennywort), and fresh brick dust together into a fine powder. Dry the mercury, then use this mixture to polish the cinnabar until it resembles silver. Alternatively, mix thin alum and white alum powder for polishing.

*End of Volume One of the* Gengdao Collection

**Moon Osmanthus Longevity Elixir**
**Method for Nurturing the Great Cinnabar Elixir with Fire**

Crush four taels of elixir base. Extract one tael of true mercury from cinnabar, and add a small amount of gold and silver filings. First, seal a water-fire crucible with Six-One Clay and dry it over a fire. Next, bathe the elixir base in well-drawn water and place it inside the crucible. Then, mix one tael of true mercury with the gold and silver filings, and pour it over the elixir base in the crucible. Place the water crucible atop the furnace, first sealing the seams with paper strips. Then, apply Six-One Clay to the entire assembly, dry it thoroughly, and ensure it is tightly sealed without gaps.

Select a room and prepare the furnace according to the prescribed method, using clean paper ash. First, warm the furnace with fire, then place an iron tripod inside. Position the elixir crucible atop the tripod, ensuring it is level and stable. Separately, weigh four taels of flaming charcoal and arrange it around the crucible, adjusting the fire’s proximity and height to match the elixir. After the fire has warmed the crucible, cover it with ashes. Fill the water crucible with warm water, checking it frequently to prevent it from drying out.

Daily at the *mao* (5–7 a.m.) and *you* (5–7 p.m.) hours, add fire and replenish water as before, ensuring the timing is never missed. After nurturing the fire for half a month, open the crucible to add more mercury, reseal it, and continue the process. After the fourth cycle of nurturing and adding mercury, the total weight of the elixir base and mercury will be eight taels. Add two more taels of mercury—this is the ancient method known as "four additions, one supplement." Some practitioners open the crucible every seven days, but this risks incomplete mercury absorption, weakening the mother elixir and hindering success. For elixirs nurtured to over ten taels, the crucible may be opened once a month or after forty-nine days, though this is not strictly required.

Once the elixir base reaches over one catty, do not add more mercury. Continue nurturing the fire for three months until the elixir base solidifies and turns golden. Then open the crucible, grind the elixir, and select the hardest, mercury-free portions for later consumption. The remainder is treated as before: mercury is poured over it, and the fire is nurtured—this is called the "elixir mother." Mother and child elixirs mutually generate and sustain each other, making their use inexhaustible.

**Method for Extracting Mercury**
Use eight taels of cinnabar (or five to seven taels, as the quantity is not strictly fixed), five taels of charcoal powder, and one tael of honey. First, seal a crucible or earthen pot with clay and dry it over a fire. Then, mix the cinnabar and charcoal powder with honey water, knead it into a paste, and pack it tightly into the crucible. Seal the crucible’s mouth with a clay disc and dry it. Pierce five to seven holes in the disc. Next, dig a pit and place a large basin filled with water inside. Invert the cinnabar crucible onto the water basin, ensuring a snug fit, and seal the seams with Six-One Clay to ensure airtightness. Coat the ground around the setup with coarse clay to prevent water and fire from interacting violently.

Ignite twenty catties of charcoal from the top and burn it thoroughly. Add ten to twenty more catties of charcoal from morning to evening, carefully regulating the fire to avoid excess or insufficiency. The next day, once the crucible has cooled, open it to retrieve the cinnabar, which will have transformed into true mercury in the water basin. Scoop it out and dry it over a fire. If the cinnabar is of good quality, each tael yields seven to eight *qian* of mercury; if poor, only half is obtained. The remaining cinnabar residue can be found in the charcoal basin, though it is no longer useful. The extracted mercury is the essence of the cinnabar.

In all fire-based methods, the key lies in carefully regulating the fire—neither too much nor too little—to avoid success or failure. This is transmitted orally and mastered through practice.

**Method for Nurturing the Yellow Sprout**
Before nurturing the elixir base, prepare the upper water and lower fire crucibles by mixing equal parts yellow earth and fine sand with paper fiber to form a clay. Seal the crucibles with this mixture and dry them in the sun. Place the elixir base inside the fire crucible. Before sealing the top, pour four *qian* of prepared mercury over each tael of elixir base, then cover it with the water crucible. Seal the seams with the previously prepared paper-fiber clay. Apply clay from the water crucible downward to form a gourd-like shape, no thicker than three *fen*.

Dry the setup over a fire. If the elixir base is hard and gray, grind it into small pieces first.

**Method for Nurturing Fire**
Use a large-mouthed, small earthen jar filled with paper ash (which should clump within five to seven days—unlike straw or cogon grass ash). Place an iron tripod inside the jar (not too tall) and position the elixir crucible atop it, ensuring stability. Fill the upper crucible with water, but not to the brim. Weigh long, red-hot charcoal pieces (about four to five *cun* each) and arrange them in four sections. Begin the fire at the *mao* hour (5–7 a.m.), replacing the old charcoal at the *you* hour (5–7 p.m.). At *mao*, place the charcoal north-south; at *you*, place it east-west.

Before adding charcoal, cover the water crucible with a tile, then stir the ash with a fire poker to evenly distribute the heat before placing the charcoal. Remove the tile afterward.

When adding water, always use a kettle to heat it to the same temperature as the water in the crucible before pouring. The water crucible must never run dry.

Every seven days, open the crucible to replenish mercury. If the elixir is abundant later on, the interval need not be fixed—once every half-month or month will suffice.

If the elixir head readily absorbs mercury and free mercury is scarce, the medicine is potent. When the mercury is fully incorporated, open the crucible to retrieve it; further refinement follows.

If absorption is slow and free mercury remains abundant, with little "jade forest and jasper trees," another method applies.

**Later Stage Formula for the Yellow Sprout Great Elixir**
The Yellow Sprout elixir head is refined with utmost precision by immortals and sages. The marvel of water and fire in harmony, the clear interplay of yin and yang—adding mercury and nurturing the fire follows the way a mother nurtures her child.

If too much mercury is added, the quantity may seem sufficient, but the mother grows weak and the child timid, unable to withstand the fire. Ingesting it yields no benefit, for the mercury will flee at the slightest heat.

Better to use slightly less than the prescribed weight, adhering to the proper timing and fire management. Nurture it over time without adding more mercury, maintaining the fire for years.

When ready for use, select the hardest portions from within, grind them to the size of mung beans, and place them in a crucible. Set a water vessel above it, and each day surround it with mature fire until the crucible and elixir head glow red inside and out. Sweep away the mercury condensation from the water vessel’s base once daily. Only when the mercury settles after intense heating is it ready.

To retrieve the elixir, place it in a bag of boiled silk and suspend it inside a sand jar. Add four to five *liang* of finely chopped licorice and simmer over a slow fire for a day. Then boil it again for another day with ten to twenty *yu gan zi* (Phyllanthus emblica). Remove it, wrap small portions (three to five *fen* each) in boiled silk, and place each packet inside a large radish, hollowed out with its top cut open. Secure the top with a skewer, wrap it in cloth, and steam it over rice until the radish turns black. Grind the elixir finely, return it to a red-hot crucible once more, then form it into millet-sized pills with white congee. Taken thus, it will cause no vomiting or diarrhea.

**Method for Roasting Gold**
Take one *liang* each of male and female [gold], one *liang* of sulfur, and one *liang* of *pao sha* (calcined borax). Use a large crucible, coat its interior with egg white, then sprinkle powdered *ma huang* (ephedra) nodes inside. Add the four ingredients, surround the crucible with charcoal fire, and gradually sprinkle four *liang* of powdered *chan du yu jin* (toad-belly turmeric) over it. When exhausted, remove and grind the mixture into a fine powder. Return it to the crucible, cover with another four *liang* of *chan du yu jin* powder, and refine it over a strong fire. Once done, grind it into an extremely fine powder for use.

To apply: Hammer fine silver into thin sheets, coat them with saliva, then sprinkle the powdered medicine onto the surface. Roast the reverse side over an intense fire, and the color will penetrate in a single heating.

**Method for Refining Metal (Guan Geng)**
Take two *liang* each of Jiangxi green alum, alum, and green salt; one *liang* of *bo ke* (potassium nitrate); and two *liang* of mercury, suspended and boiled. Use a new, unused iron pot with two to three bowls of river water, and boil the mercury with the above ingredients until dry. Strain out the oil, wrap the mercury in paper, and bury it underground for a *fu* period (twelve days). Upon retrieval, it will be hard.

Another refining method: Take one *liang* of *bei lu gan shi* (a type of calamine, known in the West as *tutiya*). Use an unmeasured amount of jujube pulp, wheat, and cypress leaves. Pound them with strong vinegar into a paste, coat the dried mercury, and refine it in a *shao* furnace for two hours. Pour the contents into a vat of water to produce high-quality refined metal. If the *dao lu gan shi* is purple, the result will be purple.

For use as a body adhesive, mix with a small amount of arsenic yellow—highly effective.

**Method for Polishing Copper to Resemble Silver**
Boil objects in a solution of *po xiao* (sodium sulfate), then refine with salt and gypsum. Use *xiang si zi* (Abrus precatorius) and *ma ya xiao* (sodium nitrate). Grind finely and polish—this yields a silver-like finish with half a year’s effort.

**Deadening Borax (Si Peng Liu)**
Boil *peng tie jiao* (borax iron residue) in the natural juice of *feng wei cao* (Pteris multifida) for half an hour. For *liu* (sulfur), boil it in the juice of *shui tian cao* (water-field grass) for half an hour—both will be deadened.

**Liu Langxian’s Qi-Infused Great Elixir**
For every *liang* of mother [mercury], infuse five *qian* of cinnabar. The more mother used, the better.

Fashion a three-legged stand from thick iron wire and place a bowl securely atop charcoal, heating it from above and below. The bowl should be an iron or *jian* bowl. Add seven parts sesame oil, thirty castor beans, and a handful of Sichuan peppercorns, along with the mother and cinnabar, into the oil. Heat until the castor beans turn brown. Remove, wrap the mixture in silk, and squeeze out the oil and medicine along with the mother, leaving only the cinnabar to be formed into pills.

Next, use *dong qing* (wintergreen) leaves as a lining for the pills. Remove the veins from the leaves and wrap the cinnabar completely, calling these "Lao Jun balls." Mix rice vinegar with flour to make a paste, then coat the balls with a layer of clay. Further wrap them with *xin lian* (arsenic) mixed with water, applying two to three layers to ensure no gaps. Clean any cracks thoroughly, then place the balls in a charcoal furnace and heat with a bellows until red-hot. Once the fire subsides, remove the cinnabar—it will now resist the teeth.

Finally, melt five *liang* of salt in a crucible to form a liquid, then pass the cinnabar through this "gate."

First, dig an earthen pit matching the size of the crucible. Once the salt has melted to a third of its volume, pour it into the pit, then swiftly add the cinnabar and immediately seal it with a brick, pressing down firmly with the foot to let it settle. Retrieve the cinnabar and place it back into the crucible for another firing.

Next, prepare half a bowl of water with a paper trough inside. Pour the cinnabar into the trough, and it will become treasure. Skim off a small amount of *pengsha* (borax) to clarify it, then pour it out.

Before adding the cinnabar to the salt, ensure the pit is dug to match the crucible’s size, perfectly level, and without gaps. Use a brick to cover the cinnabar immediately after placing it inside. This is the swiftest method, though it differs slightly from the *Gan Geng* method.

The *Gan Geng* method, as before, involves adding the mother to the cinnabar, placing it in a fine *Jian* bowl, and mixing it with castor and peppercorns, along with a few slices of *qiannianren* (asparagus root), all steeped in oil. Instead of *Lao Jun balls*, use saliva to mix *lu ganshi* (calamine) powder and *qianbaishuang* (lead frost) as a coating, then fire it to form treasure.

Use high-quality alum, *wufangcao* (purslane), and *jincheng daocao* (golden city rice straw), burn them to ash, and leach the liquid. Boil it in a sugar jar over a husk fire until dry to make a *kui* (nourishing vessel). Fifty *liang* can nourish one *liang*.

From the *Tai Shang Zi Sheng Xuan Jing*, the *Four Spirit Kui* bestowed by Lord Wang Jun:
- Cinnabar
- Sulfur
- Realgar
- Orpiment

Weigh each equally. Crush them to the size of coarse rice grains, wrap tightly in multiple layers of white silk, and boil with *huanghua* (yellow flower) and *jichangcao* (chickweed) juice in a double boiler over a slow fire for seven *fu* (seven-day periods). Dry in the sun and reuse.

- *Pengsha* (borax): 5 *qian*
- *Danfan* (chalcanthite): 5 *qian*
- *Naosha* (sal ammoniac): 1 *liang*

Use warm water in a double boiler over a slow fire for fourteen days, then remove and dry in the sun.

Use five *liang* of red gold, hammered into a box. Place the *Four Spirit* medicine inside and seal it tightly. Use eight *liang* of silver, beaten into beads. First, place half the silver in a clay box, then set the gold box on top, covering it with the remaining silver beads. Seal the clay box tightly, bind the gold box inside and the silver box outside with iron wire, then coat with salt clay. Once dry, place it in an ash jar and nourish with fire.

Fire regimen: forty-nine days.
- Days 1–7: Use mature fire. 1.5 *liang* in two daily sessions—morning and evening—without fail, or the result will be poor. If the fire weakens, add half a *liang* of mature fire.
- Days 8–14: Use mature fire. 2 *liang* in two daily sessions. If the fire weakens, add half a *liang* of mature fire.
- Days 15–21: Use mature fire. 2.5 *liang* in two daily sessions. If the fire weakens, add half a *liang* of mature fire.
- Days 22–28: Use mature fire. 2.75 *liang* in two daily sessions. If the fire weakens, add half a *liang* of mature fire.
- Days 29–49: Use mature fire. 3 *liang* in two daily sessions without fail. If the fire weakens, add 1 *liang* of mature fire.

Once the fire regimen is complete, examine the medicine. If it is black, heat it further. If it turns yellow, stop. If not, continue nourishing for another fourteen days, and it will be complete. Divide each *liang* into ten packets.

**Refining Method:**
Use one *liang* of the finest silver. Melt it, then add 3 *qian* of medicine in three batches. Once the silver’s surface is clear and free of impurities, pour it out—it will become treasure.

Guard this secret, guard it well. Do not transmit it recklessly. Only those who aid the poor and accumulate merit may receive it.

**The Great Immortal Medicine: Four Spirit Kui Formula**
Use one *jin* of raw sulfur from overseas, transparent like cinnabar stone. Chip it into lychee pit-sized pieces. Use two *dou* each of *yimu* (motherwort) and *yashecao* (duck-tongue grass) juice. Place the sulfur in a kudzu cloth bag and suspend it in the juice to boil for one *fu*, maintaining the fire day and night for seven full days. Remove and test a small amount over fire. If not yet subdued, boil again until it is.

Divide into two portions and place in a large crucible. Use thirty *jin* of hard charcoal to fire it, with two people fanning vigorously until it melts into liquid. Pour into two *Jian* bowls. If the sulfur retains its original color, it has become the supreme medicine. Grind it into an extremely fine powder. Separately, use four *liang* of raw sulfur, chipped into small pieces as before, and boil in the two-herb juice for one *fu*. Remove it.

Use the previous one *jin* of sulfur to make a *kui*. Then take the later four *liang* and, following the *lotus* method, place it in a cinnabar box. Line with two or three layers of *Kunlun* paper, grind the sulfur into a fine powder, and spread a layer on the paper. Add a layer of fixed medicine, then fill the box with *baihu* (white tiger) powder. Seal tightly, place in an ash pool, and nourish with four *liang* of fire for seven days. Remove it—the sulfur will be properly subdued.

Next, use four *liang* of leaf orpiment, chipped to the same size as before. Boil it in *yangtigen* (sheep’s hoof root) juice for one *fu*, then remove and grind finely. Mix it with the second batch of four *liang* of sulfur, grind both into an extremely fine powder, and form into longan-sized honey pills. Place them in the sulfur *kui* and nourish for seven days with four *liang* of fire. By this point, no pressing is needed—the orpiment will be subdued.

Then use four *liang* of *jiguanxiong* (cock’s comb realgar). Boil it in *shanwoju* (mountain lettuce) juice for one *fu*, remove, and grind finely with the previous orpiment and sulfur. Form into longan-sized honey pills, place in the *kui* as before, and nourish for seven days—it too will be subdued.

The *Dan Jing* states: "If one yellow dies, all yellows grieve. If one yellow does not die, all yellows fly."

First refine the sulfur to render it inert, then subdue the *cinnabar* (female) and *realgar* (male). Once the Three Yellows are dead, further subdue *cinnabar* (vermilion), thereby completing the great elixir’s transformations.

Select four *liang* of *cinnabar* with mirror-like grains. Boil it in *diding* (Chinese violet) and *jichangcao* (chicken-gut grass) juice for one *fu*, then remove. Mix with *baifuzi* (giant typhonium) and *pengsha* (borax) powder, knead with refined honey into adherent pastilles. Place in the *kui* as before and nourish for seven days—upon retrieval, the cinnabar will have become a treasure.

Set aside the initial sulfur *kui* (weighing one *jin*) for other uses. Take the four previously nourished agents, combine them to make one *jin*, grind into fine powder, and prepare a *Four Spirits Kui*. First, use three parts of pure *geng* (lead) and seven parts of mercury to form cinnabar grains. Boil them in *ziheche* (purple river vehicle) and millet-water decoction (three *sheng*) for one day. Wrap the cinnabar grains in boiled silk, shaping them into small longan-sized pellets. First dry-roast them in lime until hard, then boil as in the *lotus method*. Arrange them in the *Four Spirits Kui*, cover, and nourish with four *liang* of fire for seven days. Upon retrieval, test over fire—if not yet subdued, nourish for two more days. Repeat this process three to five times until the *kui*’s power gradually awakens, yielding *erba gengsha* (two-eight lead-cinnabar). Continue nourishing three to five more times; if the substance becomes firm, heavy, and deep in color, resistant to melting or breaking, it forms *jiuyi qingsha* (nine-one light cinnabar). When the light cinnabar, through further nourishment, develops a deep, fine hue indistinguishable from true gold, the *kui* becomes fully efficacious and may be used to nourish *chensha* (cinnabar).

For *hantai geng* (mercury-containing lead), wrap each *liang* of large-grained cinnabar in gold leaf, press firmly, and arrange as before, covering and nourishing for a full seven days. Upon retrieval, the cinnabar retains its embryonic color, its radiance dazzling the eye, now infused with purple gold. If intending to pour mercury, divide the *Four Spirits Kui* powder into three portions. Place two portions in the vessel, tamp with a chopstick to form a cavity, line it with a layer of gold leaf, then pour mercury from a small kettle into the leaf. Cover with the remaining portion of *kui* powder and nourish for seven days as before. Each *jin* of the *kui* can, by the original method, nourish four *liang*, but prolonged use may deplete its power. If only three *liang* are nourished, the *kui*’s strength remains robust indefinitely.

During the first year, the *kui* requires a seven-day firing cycle. After one year, this may be reduced to five or three days. By the third year, the transformations reach the mysterious realm, and the elixir may be completed in a single night. Within three years, the *kui* accumulates abundant *qi* of gold and treasure, producing *zimo zhenjin* (purple-polished true gold), which may then be used for tempering and refining.

For this method, prepare *liusha* (sal ammoniac) and *pengsha* separately, grind them together, and nourish for seven days before retrieval. For each *liang* of mercury, place it in a water-grinding vessel, sprinkle a pinch of the *kui* powder on top, cover with a small dish, and seal the edges tightly with vinegar-soaked paper. Heat over a three-*jin* fire, and in an instant, it transforms into top-grade true gold.

This method has been transmitted orally from ancient times, never recorded in writing. I now compile and preserve it for posterity.

Within seven hundred years, this method may be transmitted to only three persons. One who obtains it may become the teacher of a nation. Observing this wondrous formula and its procedures—most simple, most easy—one seizes the creative power of Heaven and Earth. Having obtained it, one must widely aid others and benefit all things; guard against reckless use or careless disclosure. Keep it secret, keep it secret.

**Supreme Great Medicine of Master Pu**
Transmitted by Ge Kejiu to Chen Shuzi, who received and passed it on.

First take one *jin* of sulfur from a foreign vessel, break it into pieces the size of soybeans, and take the bark of the *shuiyi* tree, scrape it into powder, and dry it in the sun. Steep it to make five *dou* of thick decoction, clarify it, and pour it into a large jar. Suspend the sulfur in a cloth pouch within the jar. Also use a fine-mesh basket, suspend it as a support inside the jar, add the decoction, and simmer over a slow fire for three *fu* periods, ensuring the fire is neither too strong nor allowed to fail. When done, remove the sulfur and dry it in the sun. Divide it into eight portions, and take one *jin* of the finest *geng* (refined metal), also divided into eight portions, to purge the mother *qi*.

First dry the *shuiyi* bark in the sun, then burn it to produce thick smoke, and fumigate fifty *liang* of it. Prepare eight crucibles, place them in a charcoal fire, and ensure they are stable. Then melt two *liang* of red *geng*, and when it becomes liquid in the smoke, quickly pour it into the fumigated crucibles. Also melt two *liang* of the processed sulfur and pour it onto the *geng* liquid. Immediately cover the crucible mouth with a tile, taking care not to delay, lest the *qi* escape. Thus, the *geng* is infused with sulfur *qi* eight times in eight crucibles. When cool, break the crucibles, remove the sulfur, and take one *jin* to serve as the *kui* for nourishing *geng*.

For the *shenshi* (spirit chamber) yin-yang furnace, the *geng* may only be used to forge the outer vessel; it cannot be used for the inner *shenshi*.

**Dead Yin-Yang Transformation Method**
Take one *liang* of yin yellow and four *liang* of yang yellow. Use *diyu* (sanguisorba), *xusuizi* (euphorbia), *lucao* (daylily), *bimazi* (castor bean), *shuiyangpi* (willow bark), and *yashecao* (duck-tongue grass), gathered from barren fields or shallow rivers where they grow like tongues beneath the water. Dry these six ingredients in the sun, grind them into powder, and simmer them to make four or five *dou* of thick decoction. Clarify it, pour it into a sand jar, and suspend the yin and yang yellow within. Add the herbal decoction and simmer over a slow fire for fifteen *fu* periods, ensuring the fire never ceases. As the liquid evaporates, replenish it until the allotted days are complete. Then take five *liang* of red *geng*, forge a *shenshi*, place the two yellows inside, and add five *qian* of dead *liu* (sal ammoniac) to mix with them. Forge another larger vessel, place the sulfur *kui* inside, and embed the *shenshi* at its center. Fill the space above and below with dead sulfur *kui* to ensure solidity. Seal the vessel’s mouth with red halloysite mixed with vinegar, then apply *liuyi* mud to seal it firmly, two fingers thick, and dry in the shade. Place it in an ash pit, apply fire at the *mao* and *you* positions, and nourish it for a full hundred days. When removed, grind the yin and yang yellows into powder. Use one *qian* to refine one *liang* of mercury, producing the supreme treasure of red *geng*.

**Dead *Liu* Method**
Take any amount of *liu* (sal ammoniac), and boil it with the natural juice of *cirujiao* (thorn apple) to render it dead. Alternatively, boil it with the natural juice of *tianzicao* (four-leaf clover) to also render it dead, which is even more effective.

**Refining Method**
Take one *liang* of mercury and place it in a crucible. Add one *qian* of the fully nourished two yellows powder, sprinkling it over the mercury. Then cover it with a small amount of transparent pine resin, and add three to five drops of fragrant oil. Cover the crucible mouth with a stable tile, ensuring no gaps, and surround the crucible with charcoal. Ignite the fire at the crucible’s mouth. When the sound within ceases and the crucible glows red, pour out the liquid—this is the supreme treasure. If it is extremely red, it may be added to silver to produce ordinary red *geng*. The refined product is *shenggeng* (sacred *geng*), with boundless transformations.

**Transformation Method**
Take six *liang* of refined *shengjin* (sacred gold) and cast it into a *shenshi*. Place two *liang* each of yin-yang and foreign vessel sulfur, ground into powder, inside. Also forge the *shengjin* into thin sheets, cut into checker pieces, and mix them with the three powders. Nourish with fire and seal for the required days, and the *geng* will be miraculously transformed.

**Another Method**
Take the two yellows, fully nourished with a hundred days of fire, and refine five *liang* into *shengjin*. As before, cast it into a *shenshi*, place the nourished two yellows inside, lining the bottom and covering the top. Nourish with yin fire for four *gang*, from one to five *liang*. Remove the previous yin-yang *kui*, and use one *qian* of nourished yin to refine one *liang* of mercury, producing supreme red *geng*. If not refined, take five *liang* of yin and place it in the sacred *shenshi*, lining and covering it to form a *kui*. Nourish the sulfur for four *gang*, from one to five *liang*. This nourished sulfur, one *qian*, refines one *liang* of mercury into supreme *geng*, with boundless transformations.

**Chen Shuzi’s Transmission of the Arsenic *Kui***
**Method for Nourishing *Fenshuang* (Calomel) and Refining Transformations**
Grind *ziheche* (purple river vehicle) into powder. For every one *liang* of arsenic powder, mix it with one and a half *liang* of *ziheche* powder. Place it in a crucible, heat it from gentle to intense fire, and render it dead to form a *kui*. This method for nourishing *fenshuang* is most effective, surpassing all others.

**Method for Ascending *Fenshuang***
For desiccated alum, use:
- One *liang* of mercury
- One *liang* of table salt
- Two *liang* of alum
- Six *qian* of saltpeter

Grind these into fine powder, add one *liang* of mercury, and grind together until no specks remain. Place it in a water-fire vessel, seal the seams with red halloysite, then further seal the mouth with *guan* mud. Scrape the seam with a bamboo strip, then remove the bamboo when dry, leaving a small hole called the "mysterious aperture." Heat the vessel to expel all moisture, then seal the aperture tightly with red halloysite. If this aperture is not left, the moisture inside will force its way out, cracking the sealed seams. Use one *qian* of the dead arsenic to nourish *fenshuang*, and refine one *liang* of bone—most wondrous.

**Method for Transmitting the Great Refining of *Fenshuang* and Transformation**
Take one *liang* of *fenshuang*, grind it, wrap it in double-layered silk, and place it in a bowl. Pour boiling water over it, rinse away the alum and medicinal residue, dry it in the sun, and wrap it tightly in *kunlun* paper.

Place a silver dish weighing one *qian* and press it tightly to ensure firmness. Take *chuanlangdu* (Euphorbia fischeriana), *zhuyazao* (Gleditsia sinensis thorns), *qumai* (Dianthus superbus), and *shiwei* (Pyrrosia lingua), each half a *liang*, grind them into powder, mix with refined honey, and form into a ball around the silver dish. Then take one *liang* of *zhangliu* root (Tamarix chinensis) and two heads of garlic, peel and grind them into a paste, and form another outer layer around the ball. Place it into a sealed container, set it upon half a *bo* (a vessel), surround it evenly with vinegar ash, and heat with five *jin* of charcoal from above. When the ash mound turns red, withdraw the fire. After the time it takes to eat a meal, reintroduce the fire, and once the fire has completely cooled, retrieve the powder to reveal the treasure.

For every eight *qian* of powder, refine five *liang* of red material—this is the *Danyang* Elixir of Bone-Transformation, a secret method.

**Urgent Refining of Arsenic Powder**
Take one *liang* each of arsenic and mercury, and one and a half *qian* of *pao* (processed arsenic). Grind them together until no specks remain. Place in an earthen pot, press salt on top, seal with a mud cake, and secure entirely with salt mud. Place in a black furnace. First, arrange two layers of hard charcoal at the furnace bottom, then set the earthen pot inside, pile charcoal around it, and ignite from above. When the pot glows red to the bottom, stir gently, and once the bottom turns fully red, remove it. Let it cool before opening. For every three *qian*, transmute one *liang*.

**Urgent Refining of Solitary Male for Transmutation**
Steep *yangtigen* (Rumex japonicus) for one *fushi* (a period of time), surround the crucible with slow fire, and add three *qian* of *gengmu* (lead mother) to form a liquid. Once cooled, use it to transmute materials.

**Method for Subduing Orpiment**
Steep *jichangcao* (Houttuynia cordata) juice for one *fushi*, then cover with dried herb powder and seal in a container. Heat with ten *jin* of fire, and once cooled, retrieve it. For every one *qian*, transmute cinnabar silver—this is the supreme treasure.

**Method for Preparing Yellow Sprouts**
Take five *liang* (or three *liang*) of lead essence, melt into cakes, or hammer into a *□* barrel. Add three *liang* of mercury, place the lead cake inside, leaving two *cun* of mercury above it, and seal tightly with *liuyi* mud. Cover the barrel’s opening with a water bottle beneath the shade. Nurture with three *liang* of gentle fire for seven full days. Upon opening, the mercury will ascend onto the lead cake, forming needle-like sprouts of fresh golden color—this is the first transformation. Add another three *liang* of mercury and nurture for another seven days; the medicine will turn golden. Do not remove it; add another three *liang* of mercury and nurture for seven more days. The sprouts will deepen in yellow hue, growing long and resembling wheat shoots. Repeat this process seven times, adding mercury seven times over forty-nine days, totaling twenty-one *liang*. This is called *Purple Yellow Sprouts*. As it transforms within the vessel, its forms and colors vary—it is the mother of *huandan* (returned cinnabar). From the lead mass, twelve *liang* can be obtained. Beneath the lead, there remains stubborn mercury of about three *liang*, while mercury that has sublimated onto the lid appears as red cinnabar, also about three *liang*, called *Solitary Cinnabar*. Collect this medicine, steam it with cow’s milk, and grind into powder. For every one *liang*, mix with jujube pulp to form a thousand pills, or one *qian* into a hundred pills. Take three pills on an empty stomach with wine daily. It greatly tonifies the lower *dantian*, stabilizes the heart and benefits the kidneys, calms the *hun* and settles the *po*, expels the Three Corpses and evil *qi*, cold diseases, wind afflictions, and chronic illnesses. Its myriad benefits cannot be fully enumerated.

*Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Two—End
*Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Three

**The Supreme Numinous Cinnabar Great Elixir**
*Preface by Yang Qin, Grand Master for Court Discussion and Military Commissioner of Nanjian Prefecture*

Gathering the essence of Heaven and Earth, the radiance of the sun and moon, one refines the Great Medicine. With fire, yin is burned to break through poison; when ingested, it strengthens sinews and bones, replenishes marrow and essence, slays the Nine Worms, severs the Three Corpses, sharpens hearing and vision, reverses aging to restore youth, revives the decayed and raises the dead, and extends years to prolong destiny—thus accomplishing the merit of the Nine Cycles.

Fearing that those who cultivate the elixir may waver in doubt and disbelief, I expound upon it in detail. Those who attain it must accumulate merit and virtuous deeds, benefiting beings and saving lives. The crucial point lies in meticulous preparation, unwavering from start to finish. It relies on the proper union of yin and yang, the mutual support of water and fire, the interplay of flying and latent child and mother, and the nurturing of metals and minerals to achieve transformation.

The interplay of flying and latent child and mother, the nurturing of metals and minerals, bring about transmutation. To shed the mortal frame and exchange the shell, to depart seated or standing—this is the *inner elixir*. The mutual support of water and fire, the supreme treasures of lead and mercury, refined without escape or sublimation—this is the *outer elixir*. Worldly people favor the outer but cannot perfect the inner; the enlightened cultivate the inner but refuse the outer. Only cinnabar unites both within and without.

When chickens consume it, they become phoenixes; when magpies eat it, they turn into simurghs; when dogs ingest it, they transform into dragons; when humans take it, they ascend as immortals. Its merit is profound, and only then is it transmitted. Its workings are unfathomable, its transformations immeasurable. The aged who consume it regain youth; the dead who receive it are reborn.

Once the Numinous Cinnabar is completed, white whiskers are pinched away, replaced by black. When the Numinous Cinnabar is refined with milk, the milk reverts to blood—this is the inner vision of the Numinous Cinnabar. It requires no obscure medicines, no rare herbs. Its use is economical, its merit simple yet unburdened. At the outset, lead’s color shifts; with the advance of fire, mercury’s body dries. Enhanced with mineral medicines, augmented with a close-fitting vessel, a thousand years’ qi is fulfilled in a single day. The treasures of mountains and marshes are completed in seven days.

Ten *liang* can transmute a hundred *liang* of lead; one *jin* can desiccate a hundred *jin* of mercury—this is the outer vision of the Numinous Cinnabar. Transmitted by former sages, expounded by later sages, inscribed on jade tablets, and concealed in divine repositories, it must be hidden in sacred mountains and passed only to the most worthy. It began with the Supreme Lord bestowing it upon Master Xu, who transmitted it to Immortal Ge, who passed it to the Master of Embracing Simplicity, who conveyed it to the Perfected One of Western Florescence, Master Lü, who entrusted it to Attendant Gentleman Zhang, who bequeathed it to Ren Baoqu. Baoqu refined its methods in the past, while Zhang Zhonghe expanded them in later times. Now, its origins and conclusions are complete, its beginning and end whole. Those who obtain it will elevate seven generations of ancestors; those who attain it will surely ascend the cloud paths.

The Way yields great utility in enriching the state and pacifying the people, while in lesser application it fattens households and adorns dwellings. Yet when beginners in cultivation or disciples of the furnace and fire first hear the wondrous formulas of Numinous Cinnabar, lingering doubts may arise, leading them into confusion and preventing awakening. Thus, I recount these matters again to clarify their origin, manifest the great Dao, and point directly to the mysterious mechanism, setting forth each step of the ninefold transmutation in full.

First, the medicine is boiled; next, the cinnabar is roasted. It is tempered in the Cauldron of Primordial Unity and nurtured in the Repository of Longevity. When the Forest of Jade arises, all superior adepts marvel; when the Tree of Jade blossoms, all celestial immortals rejoice. Therein mercury truly dies, and the treasure is revealed—transmuting the bones, encased in golden foil. What was once *geng* turns crimson; what was once *xin* turns white.

From this we observe: the method of Numinous Cinnabar, in its essential subtlety, harmonizes with the creative transformations of Heaven and Earth. In its achievements, it fulfills the cultivation of sages and worthies. Extending its meaning, it aligns with the eight trigrams of the *Zhouyi*. Tracing its principle, it accords with the ninefold cyclings of the Old Master. Thus, its transformations emerge and vanish without limit, its movements—vertical, horizontal, curved, or straight—conform to all patterns.

The *Daodejing* states: "That which cannot be seen is called *xi*; that which cannot be heard is called *yi*." Hence, it is named the Way of *Xiyi*. This divine elixir is called Numinous Cinnabar, yet its meaning is one. The Perfected One of True Yang said: "A single grain of golden elixir determines longevity." This is that elixir. Though its names differ, its reality is the same. Sages and worthies of all ages cultivated this; the ten thousand volumes of alchemical scriptures likewise refer to this. Numinous Cinnabar is the steward of furnace and fire, the leader of self-cultivation.

Some may ask: If Numinous Cinnabar is so wondrous, why must it rely on the "mother" to reveal the treasure? They do not realize that swallows do not hatch phoenixes, nor do foxes and hares nurse horses. Solitary yin does not produce; solitary yang does not complete. Mercury is pure yin; lead is perfect yang. The *Yijing* states: "The alternation of one yin and one yang is called the Dao." Thus, it relies on the mother to reveal the treasure.

Now, when people of this world obtain Numinous Cinnabar yet cannot ascend lightly upon consuming it, or encounter obstacles in refinement, why is this? It is because their practice is shallow. The scriptures say: "Whether the divine is made luminous depends on the person." If it is not the right person, the Dao does not operate in vain.

Thus, if even a single medicinal substance, when properly subdued, can enable ascension to immortality, how much more so with Numinous Cinnabar? Those who obtain its method must cultivate utmost sincerity—for sincerity is the completion of practice. The noble ones who engage with Numinous Cinnabar, refining body and conduct, need not fear failing to ascend as perfected beings.

The required ingredients and the methods of preparation are reverently set forth below.

For those who refine the elixir and cultivate the Dao, one must first purify body and mind, burn incense, make vows, and invoke Heaven and Earth. Proceed with the elixir refinement in strict observance, aiming to benefit all beings and aid in their liberation. Only when free from demonic obstacles may one begin the work.

If sincerity is lacking and thoughts are wanton and unrestrained, the spirits will not protect you.

Master Zhang Zhonghe said:
*"Those who refine the elixir must know this well—
Without cultivating conduct, do not attempt the work.
Only when merit is complete and the task fulfilled
Will you believe the wondrous marvel of the elixir born into the world."*

**Method for Refining Numinous Cinnabar Elixir**

*Verse:*
Two eights unite yin and yang,
Examine closely in the Li Palace’s hall.
Who knows the true transformation?
The Weaver Girl weds the Cowherd’s son.

**First: The Method for Stir-Frying Numinous Cinnabar**
Take four taels of sulfur—preferably the finest imported variety, transparent and free of impurities. Soak it in the juice of *shuitian gongzi* grass (also called *tianzi* grass) for one *fu* period. If unavailable, substitute with *qumai*. Grind it into a fine powder, then boil it in river water. For one jin of mercury, add one tael each of *guanzhong* and *wubeizi*, along with two and a half mace of transparent pine resin. Grind them together, then soak in good rice vinegar and boil for half a day until it reaches a thick, paste-like consistency.

Remove the mixture and place it in a new iron pan. First, boil it with ginger juice for half a day, then wipe dry. Set it over a slow fire, melt the sulfur into a liquid, and then add the mercury. Stir slowly over a low flame with an iron spoon. If it forms clumps, pound them finely with a willow-wood mallet, then return to the slow fire to stir-fry. Under no circumstances should smoke or flames arise. If yellow smoke appears, immediately remove it from the fire. Do not stop stirring, and avoid impatience or haste. Do not sprinkle vinegar at any point. Violating this prohibition will bring grave consequences for the Numinous Cinnabar.

Stir-fry for a full day until it resembles aged bronze. When the Numinous Cinnabar is firm and solid, it will be free of stray mercury.

**Second: The Method for Crafting the Crucible and Tripod (omitted)**

**Third: The Method for Sealing Numinous Cinnabar into the Tripod**
Take ten taels of bronze and one tael of cinnabar—preferably in granular form. Grind the cinnabar to an extremely fine powder.

First, thickly grind good ink with strong vinegar and apply it to the bottom of the water tripod three to five times to ensure the Numinous Cinnabar can be easily removed later. Externally, mix clam powder and red halloysite with a small amount of honey, seal tightly, and secure with iron wire. Then, evenly coat the entire vessel with *liuyi* clay mixed with lead oxide. Allow it to dry thoroughly for a day and night before placing it into the furnace’s water tripod. Fill the tripod with water, then place three jin of charcoal beneath it to heat the base. When the water reduces by one or two cups, add two or three more jin of charcoal. Continue until the water has evaporated from three tripods, constantly replenishing the water and charcoal. After five *shi* periods, add five or six jin of charcoal for one firing, then wait until fifteen jin of charcoal have been used—this completes the fire cycle.

Cool the furnace, remove the vessel, and inspect the cinnabar. It should be hard and resonant. If the cinnabar is not firm and still contains oily mercury, it will fail to form the elixir, and the embryo’s color will not stabilize. Other issues, such as excessive consumption of the "mother" or various ailments, arise from improper subduing of sulfur and mercury, insufficient stir-frying of bronze, failure to use rice vinegar, uneven fire cycles, or insufficient fire intensity.

For further refinement, the water tripod must be replenished with hot water—never cold water. The fire should not be too high, and flames must not reach the seams of the water tripod.

The Most High said: *"True jia-geng is called bronze. When placed in the tripod and fired with fifteen jin of charcoal, the union is achieved, and the cinnabar’s body becomes solid. The fifteen jin of fire correspond to nine hundred years, the fifteen cycles of the Great Yang, and the number of the jia-zi. Thus, one day and night encompasses nine hundred years of transformation."*

Hence it is said: *"Numinous Cinnabar conceals the white, belonging to Kan. Its original color is red, belonging to Li. This is the union of Kan and Li, the completion of the alchemical process. Water, fire, metal, wood, and earth merge into one transformation, congealing to form the Great Medicine."*

*Verse:*
Five metals achieve union in Kan and Li’s palace,
Merging into one form, its body fundamentally red.
Wondrously endowed with the power of yin-yang’s union,
In ninety days of jia-zi, the work is complete in a single morning.

**Fourth: The Method for Boiling and Refining Numinous Cinnabar**
Burn young mulberry branches to ash and leach the juice. Take two taels of alum, two mace of realgar, one tael of Sichuan pepper, one tael of green salt, and three mace of chalcanthite.

Combine these five ingredients with the ash juice and vinegar in a new iron pan or a stoneware vessel. Place the Numinous Cinnabar in a fine, dense bamboo basket and suspend it within the medicinal liquid to boil for three *fu* periods. Once dry, stir-fry it, then bathe it in Sichuan pepper decoction.

*Question:* Why boil it?
The Most High said: *"When sulfur and mercury take form, they must truly die. This requires boiling and inversion. The five medicinal ingredients correspond to the Five Phases.
