Thus, it is called the method of boiling sulfur with Five-Phase mulberry ash juice—for when sulfur is inverted, mercury dies."*

*Verse:*
Yin and yang restrain each other, yet the treasure is not yet complete;
Only with mulberry’s green essence can poverty be averted.

Refining through nine transformations can transmute stone,
All by the mother’s power are the immortals revealed.

**Fifth Method: Refining the Lead-Sulfur Repository in the Floral Pool**
Take one *jin* of black lead and two *liang* of sulfur—translucent, shipborne sulfur is best; avoid that which has been boiled in paddy fields.

Place a clean iron pan over the fire and melt the lead into a liquid. Then take the prepared sulfur, grind it finely, and gradually add it to the molten lead while stirring continuously with an iron spoon. Let the sulfur blaze like fireflies in flight, or like stars appearing, then remove the pan from the fire. Continue stirring without pause until the sparks gradually subside. Return the pan to the fire, slowly sprinkle in the sulfur powder, and stir ceaselessly until all is incorporated. Once cooled, grind it into a fine powder to form the Floral Pool.

This is called the union of lead and mercury, where the two *qi* support each other, yin and yang conjoin, and *ying* and *wei* harmonize—thus obtaining water within fire, and yin within yang. Therefore, the Dao of longevity operates in endless cycles, its nourishment inexhaustible, its principle now made clear.

The Floral Pool of the *Gen* Dao is thus established.
Its application has its secrets.

**Sixth Method: Establishing the *Gen* Sulfur Repository**
Take four *liang* of prepared sulfur and half a *jin* of mountain marsh ore. Hammer the ore into thin sheets, slightly thicker, without regard to the number of pieces. Heat each sheet over a fire until extremely hot, then sprinkle the prepared sulfur powder onto it. Reheat and resprinkle until the sulfur turns a dark greenish-black, peeling like scorched cauldron fragments. Continue heating and sprinkling until the sulfur is fully embedded in the mountain marsh sheets. Then grind it into a fine powder and mix it with other medicinal ingredients to form the repository.

Take:
- Hematite, calcined seven times and quenched in vinegar until friable, ground to powder
- Pyrolusite, ground to powder
- Red crow’s foot, three ingredients, each four *liang*
- *Gen* sulfur, four *liang*

Grind the first three ingredients into powder. For every *liang* of *Gen* sulfur, use three *liang* of this mixture, blending them evenly to form the repository.

Next, take the previously heated sulfur and pure mountain marsh ore, grind them into powder, and use them as a body-adhering layer. Moisten the numinous cinnabar with vinegar paste, then apply the mountain marsh powder to one side. Then use high-quality mountain marsh sheets to wrap each piece, securing them tightly with silk thread. Remove the silk and place the bundle into the *Gen* sulfur repository, arranging them in a lotus formation and covering them with a layer. Next, fashion a divine chamber from mountain marsh ore. If unavailable, hammer the ore into round sheets, place them atop the *Gen* sulfur repository, then position the body-adhering cinnabar-sulfur layer on top. Cover it with another mountain marsh sheet, seal the edges with the Floral Pool, and bind it tightly with iron wire. Apply an outer seal, then place it into an ash jar. Add two *liang* of fire and nurture for two days. Increase the fire to two and a half *liang* and nurture for another two days. Then add three *liang* of fire and nurture for two more days. On the seventh day, add five *liang* of fire, insert it into the four directions, and nurture for one *fu* period. Once the seven-day cycle is complete, remove the cinnabar and discard the body-adhering medicine. Reboil the two ingredients:

- Chalcanthite, four *qian*
- Shipborne sulfur, eight *qian*
- *Huangyaozi*
- *Baiyaozi*, all ground finely

Grind the chalcanthite and sulfur into powder, then apply it to the numinous cinnabar and let it dry. Next, take the *Huangyaozi* and *Baiyaozi*, stir-fry them together over a low flame until they turn a purplish-black. Grind them into a fine powder, mix with vinegar paste, and apply it to the numinous cinnabar to moisten it, ensuring the medicine does not penetrate through. Then wrap it in Kunlun paper, bind it with silk, and place it into the mother repository for nurturing.

*Question:* Why use this medicine for the body-adhering layer?
The Most High said: *"This medicine is the very root of dead mercury. Using it to deaden mercury ensures absolute success."*

**Seventh Method: Warm-Nurturing the Mother Repository**
*Verse:*

Mother rectifies, child numinous—through them the transformations of creation flow,
Yet the numinous child does not cleave to the mother.
Let Southern Star be aided by *sanleng*,
Or if Black Dragon is used, let it too become a star.

Take one *jin* of superior mountain marshland, refine it according to method—either into millet-like grains or fashioned into a repository—and still employ a divine chamber.

*Question:* Why use a divine chamber?
The Most High said: *"Lest the upper and lower coverings fail to reach every part, the divine chamber ensures full and even enclosure. Moreover, it allows the cinnabar to fully absorb the mother’s robust qi."*

**Eighth Method: Warm-Nurturing with Fire Regimen**
*Verse:*
Gold and wood intermingle, entering the *bing* palace,
Know that *mao* and *you* may be compared as one.
Seven inquiries of the *Wei* maiden form immortal substance,
And once more the Liu lad ascends into azure emptiness.

Once the previous cinnabar is applied to the body and placed into the mother repository, arrange the lotus base, seal it properly, and set it into the ash pit.

**First day’s fire:** *mao* and *you* periods, two *liang* each.
**Second day:** three *liang* each.
Each subsequent day, add one *liang* more.
By the seventh day, increase the fire by half a *jin*, then nurture for one day.
Remove from the cold furnace, take one piece, wrap it tightly in the flesh of two half white plums, and roast in fire for the duration of a meal.
Then immerse in vinegar and examine—if it appears snow-white,
And feels light, the sulfur has departed.
Only mercury remains, and the mother suffers no loss or diminution.
If the inversion is not yet complete, remove the body-adhering layer at once,
For the color of the embryo will appear—this indicates the fire was too high, and the power did not penetrate fully.

Next, use rice vinegar boiled with alum to cleanse the mother repository, scrubbing it vigorously in the palm until dry.
Place it back into the vessel and nurture for three more days, with *mao* and *you* fires of five *liang* each—success is assured.

*Question:* Why bathe the repository in vinegar?
The Most High said: *"Lest the mother’s power weaken, this is to strengthen it further."*

*Verse:*
Without essence and radiance, the child does not vanish;
If the mother’s body is frail, the child cannot be born.
Failing to grasp the three essentials of the mysterious mechanism,
How can one achieve the great elixir’s completion?

For those with resources, use another *jin* of mountain marshland to craft a repository as before, and nurture for seven more days.
The cinnabar will be firm beyond compare, and when used for further refinement, its power vast.
After bathing, one transcends the mundane and enters sagehood—this marks the first transformation, refining the precious into treasure.

**First Transformation: Refining the Precious into Treasure**
*Diding* flower is a single-stemmed yellow bloom.
If unavailable, *jindeng* root may substitute.
*Bajing* flesh
*Bimazi* flesh
The above in equal parts.

Take the previous numinous cinnabar, remove the body-adhering layer, and grind it into powder in an iron mortar.
Wrap it in Kunlun paper to form a ball.
Then take the three aforementioned ingredients, pound them into a paste, and encase the cinnabar within.
Place it into a large cinnabar vessel, layering it with salt flowers.
Puncture two or three thousand holes in the salt layer, place a lead cake atop, then fill the remainder with salt flowers.
Seal the mouth tightly, ensuring the entire vessel is secured, and let dry.
Set it into the ash pit, apply five *jin* of fire, and calcine for one night.
Cool the furnace, remove a piece—if it resembles silver frost—then fashion it into a repository.

*Verse:*
The numinous cinnabar, sevenfold returned, holds three vehicles,
The wondrous principle, transmitted by the master, must be clearly understood.
Black and white distinctly part, penetrating creation’s transformations,
Bathed in the flowery pond, one naturally ascends in flight.

Bathe the previous numinous cinnabar:
Use one *sheng* of rice vinegar, half a *liang* of green vitriol, and three *qian* of saltpeter.
Boil them together in a pan for one day until the transformation is firm—this completes the first transformation’s elixir head.

**Second Transformation: Shedding the Mundane to Enter Sagehood**
*Verse:*
No need for a mundane womb to nurture the sacred embryo,
Follow the prior method to carefully cultivate.
This time, shedding the body, one forms immortal bones,
And begins to sense depths unfathomable.

Take the previous cinnabar, craft another repository, and refine with one *jin* of raw cinnabar placed into the vessel for nurturing.
One *liang* of black pepper
One *liang* of *bibo*
Five *qian* each of *zhimu* and *beimu*

Use yellow vinegar to suspend the embryo and boil the pearl for one *fu* period.
Then bathe the pearl in pepper-infused water to cleanse it, and let dry before proceeding.

*Fen Shuang*
*Paosha*
*Eguanshi*
*Baijiaoxiang*
*Ku Mingfan*
Two *qian* each of the above five ingredients, ground into fine powder.
Mix with honey or vinegar paste, apply to the body-adhering layer, and place into the first transformation’s repository.
Arrange the lotus base as before, seal it properly, and set it into the furnace for warm nurturing.
The fire regimen follows the previous method.
When the fire is complete and the vessel opened, the elixir is formed—this is the sacred embryo,
For not a trace of mundane qi remains.
Nurtured thus to one *jin*, it must not be melted but only broken for nurturing the great medicine.
The repository method adheres to the four-one ratio.

*Verse:*
No need for mundane mediums—with a white body it forms,
Free from its womb’s qi, it awakens of itself.
All spiritual transformations arise from this,
In an instant, cinnabar yang transforms the bones, purifying them.

If one wishes to ingest it, bury it in earth for seven days to remove fire toxin, then form pills with wood honey.

**Fire Regimen, Subtle Method**
**First day:** one *liang*
**Second day:** one and a half *liang*
**Third day:** two *liang*
**Fourth day:** three *liang*
**Fifth day:** four *liang*
**Sixth day:** four and a half *liang*
**Seventh day:** six *liang*
On the seventh day, at the crown: three *liang*
East: three *liang*
Evening crown: three *liang*
West: three *liang*
**Eighth day** dawn crown: three *liang*
South: three *liang*
Evening crown: three *liang*
North: three *liang*

**Third Transformation: Nurturing True Yang**

**Verse:**
To lay the foundation of the great immortal elixir,
First capture and bind the Crimson Dragon’s child.
Refine it to a nine-by-nine pure yang body,
Then trust the marvelous transformations within the crucible.

Once mercury has become a treasure, it remains a solitary essence. Without true yang, it cannot undergo transformation. Use one *jin* of arrowhead cinnabar.

**Ingredients:**
- Sichuan pepper
- Wild aconite
- Arisaema
- Daphne flower
- Alum
- Halite
*(each one *liang*)*
- Chalcanthite
- Sal ammoniac
*(each five *qian*)*

Place in good rice vinegar and suspend in a womb-vessel to boil for three *fu* periods. Then boil in wild knotweed juice for half a day. Bathe in pepper decoction until dry. Grind thick, fine ink and pour into a tile dish. Wrap the cinnabar in layers, dry over a clean tile, then wrap again in ink and dry once more. Repeat this five to seven times, then apply *faxin* paste to the body, making it thick.

Take the second-transformation numinous cinnabar, melt it into powder, and place it in a sealed vessel. Seal the cinnabar with *lián* (lotus?) as prescribed. First, use three *qian*—or five *qian*—of numinous cinnabar, shape it into round discs, and place them atop the vessel’s contents. Then add *Huachi* powder, seal tightly, and place in an ash crucible. Nurture it with fire according to the previous method.

When the days are complete, remove and polish it. If it resembles the hues of mountains and marshes, it is done. If it still bears a reddish tint, apply fire for three more days—two *liang* each time—and it will surely be complete.

The vessel method follows the four-one ratio: nurture it four times, using one *jin* per vessel for washing and infusion. If not refining the ninefold orthodox elixir, one may instead nurture the second-transformation elixir head, creating a "Fountain of Longevity" vessel to nurture the mother cinnabar.

This is the Dao of "one gives birth to two, two gives birth to three, and three gives birth to the myriad things."

---

**Fourth Transformation: Infusing the Yellow Sprout**

**Verse:**
Wood-crystal gold-fluid meets cinnabar,
The numinous medicine’s cinnabar is truly praiseworthy.
Relying solely on its nurturing power,
It congeals into a crucible full of crystal sprouts.

Wood-crystal gold-fluid refers to the previous numinous cinnabar, while the cinnabar is the nurtured vermilion. As the *Cantong Qi* states: "Cinnabar is the essence of wood; when it meets metal, they merge."

Take this fire-tamed cinnabar, shape it into lumps, and place it in a sealed vessel to nurture for three days—three *liang* of fire each day. Open the vessel and infuse four *liang* of mercury, first filtered through three or four layers of tough paper. Pour it over the cinnabar, seal tightly, and place in an ash crucible to nurture. Follow the previous fire regimen.

After seven days, remove it from the cold furnace. The mercury will have dried, though sprouts may not yet have formed. If not refining the orthodox elixir, one may nurture numinous cinnabar in a vessel to cultivate mother cinnabar—this is called "morning planting, evening harvest."

**Verse:**

Once more infuse, once more nurture—mercury dries again and again,
The luminous Dao is clear, naturally unburdened.
Fire-tending gently, never in excess,
Open the furnace to gather radiant jade-like brilliance.

Once the mercury is nurtured, there is no need to pluck it. As before, infuse and nurture again. With twenty *liang* of the vessel’s contents, one may infuse five *liang* of mercury, following the previous fire regimen for seven days. Upon opening, the mercury will have awakened, surging forth jade sprouts like *langgan* jade.

**Verse:**
Jade groves and jasper trees rely on the third infusion,
Wondrous elixirs and rare blossoms grow ever more resplendent.
At this stage, preserve it wholly without slackening—
Firmly guard the resolve, steadfast in heart.

After nurturing mercury twice, the fire’s power must increase further.
Then infuse seven *liang* of raw mercury, seal tightly as before, and nurture with fire for seven days. Upon opening, it will gleam with radiant jade blossoms—a jade grove and jasper trees indeed. In total, one *jin* of mercury sprouts will have formed. Pluck them and name them "Divine Talisman White Snow," which may be used to nurture the Great Elixir.
If one merely plucks them, they may be enjoyed for boundless benefit.

**Verse:**
White Snow and Divine Talisman—how rare the encounter!
The Crimson Dragon revolves anew, guarding the Central Palace.
Clouds and thunder roar as the tripod boils for three days—
Then craft the supreme achievement of the immortals’ art.

**Method for Hardening the Sprouts**

Here the *jin* of mercury sprouts is finely filed and placed in a pan. Stir-fry with the lees of medicinal wine made from rice vinegar cakes for two *shi*-hours. Then sprinkle with medicinal water and stir-fry again. Afterward, place in a sealed vessel and nurture for twenty-one days until the sprouts become firm and potent, ready for fire-nurturing.

**Method for the Fifth Transformation: Granulating the Great Elixir**

**Verse:**
The Crimson Dragon subdues fire, called the Returned Elixir—
A secret held by immortals, rarely encountered.
Forty-nine days complete the work—
A single grain transforms mercury entirely.

Take the nurtured cinnabar sprouts, crush them, and place in a sealed vessel. Nurture in emptiness for fourteen days. Following the four-to-one method, infuse with mercury and two *liang* of fire, nurturing for forty-nine days. When the count is complete, open to reveal a jade grove and jasper trees. Remove the cinnabar as before, prepare a divine chamber, and take one *qian* of jade bamboo shoots to granulate one *liang* of mercury into the Elixir. Set up a bowl, place mercury inside, and sprinkle the granulated medicine on top. Seal tightly and place over fire—naturally, a cicada-like chirping will sound. When the sound ceases, it is dry.

**Sixth Transformation: Producing the Five Metals, Subduing the Three Yellows, and Refining into Treasures**

Take one *liang* each of the Three Yellows, grind together for one *fu*-hour, then add one *liang* of Jade Snow powder (the jade bamboo shoots). Grind evenly and place in a crucible, covering the top with half a *liang* of subdued fire sal ammoniac. Seal the mouth, apply nine *jin* of fire in three cycles, and refine. Remove from the cold furnace to obtain a single red Elixir. To test it, melt five *liang* of the Five Metals in a bright furnace and add one *qian* of the Three Yellows—all will transform into purple metal. At this stage, the work is complete, but one must proceed with careful measure. Only those of profound virtue and conduct may partake; one must also aid the poor and rescue the destitute. Cultivate the body and nurture life. If one relies on this for greed or excess, disaster will swiftly follow. Beware and take heed.

**Method for Subduing Sal Ammoniac**

Use half a *liang* of sal ammoniac and one *qian* of *tianqiezi* powder. Seal in a vessel and refine with one *jin* of fire. Remove from the cold furnace—it will be fully subdued. Grind finely and store in a sealed vessel.

**Verse:**
For the love of yellow blossoms gilding white frost,
What transformation is beyond comprehension?
The Three Primes receive the furnace’s snow—
Let not the foolish darkly speculate.

**Seventh Transformation: Sevenfold Returned Elixir**

Take eight *liang* of sulfur and two *liang* of mercury, grind until black. Then add one *liang* of the previously subdued Three Yellows and grind evenly. Place in a porcelain vessel, cover with three *liang* of the Three Yellows, seal the seams with red halloysite, and secure the entire vessel with salt clay. Once dry, place in an ash pit. Apply four *liang* of fire at the *mao* and *you* hours daily for seven days. Remove and grind into powder.

**Verse:**
The Twin-Braided Maiden naturally aids,
Reversing and returning in harmonious union.
When the medicine matures, transformation is complete—
Father and son unite without doubt.

**Eighth Transformation: Granulating Mercury into the Complete Eight Trigrams Metal**

Take five *liang* of the nurtured sulfur-mercury, add half a *liang* each of the finest raw Three Yellows and one *liang* of southern borax. Grind evenly, seal in a vessel, and place in an ash pit. Apply two *liang* of fire daily for twenty-one days and nights, totaling two *liang* of fire. When the count is complete, remove. Use one *zi* of this to granulate five *liang* of mercury into purple metal. If one dare not partake even at the sixth transformation, how much more should one fear the greater power of this stage? Only a man of destiny should proceed—how can one not be cautious?

**Verse:**
The Elixir completes eight transformations,
No further toil is needed.
A single grain of pure Yang medicine
Can refine the finest metal.
If one cultivates to this point,
Accumulate virtue and temper greed and wrath.
When merit and conduct fill three thousand,
One becomes a long-lived, ever-seeing person.

To ingest at each transformation, form pills with wood honey the size of *wutong* seeds. Take one pill on an empty stomach with flowing water. Upon completing the nine transformations, the methods are as previously listed. Since ancient times, cinnabar has originated from this.

**Ninth Transformation: Elixir for Reviving the Dead**

**Verse:**
Months deep in Elixir refinement,
Divine transformations are naturally entrusted.
What need for gold seals and purple sashes?
Bright moon and clear wind delight this life.

The Most High says: If one refines to this stage and ingests it, the mortal body becomes sacred, and old age returns to youth. One may build an altar on a blessed highland, use a jade-oil carriage to pay homage to the stars, and set up a tripod and furnace to refine the Great Medicine as prescribed. Mix paper mulberry juice with clay to coat the tripod, then add the Elixir. Place a water basin below, seal tightly, and place in the altar furnace. Apply five *liang* of fire daily for one hundred days. When complete, remove the Elixir and bury it three *chi* underground for one year. Someone may ask: Why bury it? The Most High says: To release the fire toxin. After one year, retrieve it and suspend it in a well for another year. Then soak it in flowing water for one year. After three full years, retrieve it, grind into fine powder, and form pills the size of chicken heads with licorice juice. Place in a furnace and nurture with fire for seven days. To test it, feed one pill to a chicken or dog—over time, they will transform into dragons or phoenixes. When humans ingest it, both form and spirit become wondrous, and one ascends in broad daylight. After forming the pills and completing the fire-nurturing, prepare several vats filled with freshly drawn water and place the Elixir inside. When the water warms, transfer it to another vat. Only then is the process complete.

**Method for the Nine Transformations of the Golden Sprout Tripod**

**Li Dongxuan’s Wondrous Elixir Secret Formula**
**First Transformation of the Golden Tripod**
Take ten taels of arsenic and divide into thirty packets. First melt two taels of black lead in a crucible until molten, then add the arsenic packet by packet, waiting each time until fully dissolved. After three or four packets, pour out the mixture, then add more arsenic as before until all is used. From ten taels of arsenic, only six taels will be refined. If a golden hue is desired, omit the lead.

The method states:
*To use lead or not—one must work within the lead.*
*Yet when lead is used, it remains an error.*

**Second Step: Calcining with Cinnabar**
Take five taels of cinnabar and mix with the five taels of refined arsenic, grinding finely. Place in a *jian* bowl, cover the surface with two or three *qian* of dead arsenic, and set in the furnace. When glowing red, use a bellows to melt into liquid. Sprinkle a small amount of raw arsenic to revive the dead arsenic, continuing to fan until the arsenic is exhausted and the liquid clears—this indicates the cinnabar is fully refined. Remove and cool, then break the bowl to retrieve the cinnabar. Re-smoke it to eliminate all arsenic, then pound into pieces the size of soapberries. Boil with the following medicines:

- Wheat bran salt
- Madder root
- Bitter bamboo
- Wolfsbane
- Pumice
- Magnetite
- Needle sand

Each one tael. Boil five taels of cinnabar in a sand pot for three *fu* periods until it turns black. Then rinse with boiling water sixty times—no less—soaking and grinding into powder to form a *kui*.

Next, take one tael of raw cinnabar in granular form, coat with gold leaf using vinegar, shaping like a lotus. Place in a porcelain box, seal the seams with red halloysite mixed with vinegar, bind crosswise with iron wire, and dry. Set in an ash pit with two taels of fire at the top, nurturing for seven days. Repeat the nurturing as before.

**Third Step: Transmuting Copper and Iron**
Take two taels of plowshare iron, heat and shatter. Place a crucible with one tael of cinnabar at the bottom and the iron on top. Apply intense fire until molten—the cinnabar will ascend while the iron sinks, producing a sound like a woodpecker’s pecking. Wait until the sound ceases and the elixir is complete; do not pour out. Pour cold water over the crucible’s surface, and the cinnabar will naturally congeal into flakes on top. Break the crucible to retrieve it, while the iron below will have transformed into fine silver. Reuse the cinnabar in a furnace for further transmutation. The second and third transmutations may yield a bluish hue and greater hardness. Combine the first batch of silver and smoke it to achieve uniform color, producing superior silver—unlike anything in the mortal world, known as *elixir silver*. This is the supreme treasure of immortals. The method for transmuting copper is the same.

If the cinnabar is exhausted after the third transmutation, prepare a new *kui* and nurture mother cinnabar with raw cinnabar to form a treasure. Similarly, lead may be refined into silver without loss.

**Fourth Step: Transcending the Mortal to Attain the Sacred**
For every four taels of nurtured cinnabar, gather eight taels (or four taels) into one *kui*. Take raw cinnabar as before, coat with gold leaf, and nurture with fire for seven days. Retrieve and combine with the mother cinnabar in equal parts—eight taels or one *jin*—grinding together. Add one tael each of realgar and orpiment, grinding all three ingredients into the *kui*. Nurture with two taels of fire for seven days, yielding a total of ten taels, which are then refined into superior metal.

**Fifth Step: Gathering the Hun and Po**
If the previous ten taels of elixir do not refine into metal, prepare another *kui*. Take three taels of raw cinnabar, one tael each of granular realgar and orpiment, combine into lumps, coat with gold leaf, and nurture with fire for seven days as before, yielding five taels. Grind one tael, mix with one *qian* of fire-subdued borax, form into ten pills with yellow wax, and transmute one tael of *shan gen* into metal.

**Sixth Step: The Method of Using the Hun to Restrain the Po**
If the above fifteen taels do not transmute into metal, grind and add five taels of raw cinnabar, two taels each of realgar and orpiment, coat with gold leaf, and nurture with three taels of fire for seven days, yielding twenty-four taels. Take one tael, add one *qian* each of fire-subdued saltpeter and borax, grind together, form into ten pills with yellow wax, and each pill will transmute one tael of dry mercury into metal.

**Seventh Step: Refining Yang to Dissolve Yin**
The above twenty-four taels serve as the *elixir head*. If transmutation is incomplete, construct an elixir chamber and select an auspicious mountain site to begin refining the *Lesser Return Elixir*. Take the twenty-four taels of elixir, grind into a *kui*, and pour mercury in three stages: first two taels, then three, then five, each time nurturing with three taels of fire for seven days, yielding thirty-four taels. The elixir will gleam with purple-gold radiance, filling the room with brilliant fragrance. Bathe it in fragrant water, then nurture for another seven days, repeating the bathing process. After a full *jiazi* cycle and one month, the *Lesser Elixir* is complete.

Grind finely, mix with human milk and honey to form a paste, and shape into pills the size of tung seeds. Take one pill on an empty stomach with well-flower water. After ten days, the Three Corpses will depart, and all parasites die; chronic ailments will be cured. After a hundred days, hunger and satiety become irrelevant, and one is immune to plagues, miasmas, evil spirits, tigers, rhinoceroses, blades, and weapons. The Dao of immortality is thus achieved—this is the first step for the lesser adept toward transcendence.

**Eighth Step: Refining Qi to Attain Spirit**
With three taels of fire, take the aforementioned *Lesser Return Elixir*, place in a *kui*, and nurture for seven days, bathing once. After one full celestial cycle (one year), the work is complete, and the elixir will turn white, radiating light like a Buddha’s hair curls.

When removed, it fills the chamber with radiant light, and divine beings will guard it—mountain spirits and demons dare not face it. One must fast, cultivate goodness, and perform myriad virtuous deeds to preserve the elixir. Even those who obtain it should first accumulate merit and conduct before ingesting it, whereupon they may soar through the void and become earthbound immortals.

**Ninth Step: Refining Spirit to Merge with the Dao**
Use four taels of fire. Follow the method of bathing once every seven days, and continue for three years (one thousand days). When the work is complete and the tally full, golden light will break forth—this is the sign of success. One must invite accomplished Daoists to jointly safeguard it, and further perform rituals to honor Heaven and Earth. Without this, great demons will arise to wreak havoc, ruining the elixir and wasting one’s efforts. When the elixir is perfected, its color returns to yellow—this is the Way of returning to the origin and restoring truth. It first arose from the Yellow Sprout, and now, having reached completion, reverts to yellow. When grinding it, avoid exposure to sunlight, lest it ascend with the sun and scatter. It must be bound into pills with wood honey. If a single grain is scattered in a region, a thousand *li* will be blessed—evil spirits, demons, insects, tigers, droughts, and floods will vanish. If a single grain enters the body, one may wander the Ten Continents and Three Isles, attaining the rank of immortal, with a lifespan equal to Heaven and Earth. One may deliver the living and the dead, and with a thought, all wishes are fulfilled. Chickens fed with it become phoenixes, dogs transform into dragons, and myriad wondrous changes occur—its efficacy defies full description.

Those who study the Dao and learn of this elixir are all destined by past good deeds, not mere mortals of this lifetime. Wherever this elixir scripture arrives, divine beings will protect it. Those who lightly slander these teachings are but newly born into humanity, their fates constrained by meager destinies. If there are seekers bound by karmic affinity, they should offer sincere gifts of gold and treasure to receive this text, but never show it to the unworthy. Guard these precepts with utmost care.

*Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Three—End
*Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Four

**The Eastern Slope’s Three-Yellow Crucible Method: A Potent and Proven Technique**

Take purple-flowered motherwort, pound it thoroughly to extract its natural juice, and boil half a *jin* or one *jin* of sulfur in it without regard to duration. Cease only when testing reveals no ghostly flames or smoke. Place it in a sweet-pot crucible to melt and refine into an ingot, ensuring purity. If storing in a sealed box within an ash pit, use four *liang*. Nurture one *liang* of *yin* (female) for seven full days, then nurture one *liang* of *yang* (male). For larger quantities, nurture one *jin* or half a *jin* of *yin* and *yang*, maintaining a ratio of four to one. Replenish the yellow *yin* and *yang* seven times daily, each piece the size of a dice block, and nurture in a lotus-shaped arrangement.

To prepare the crucible, ensure the three yellows are evenly proportioned, reserving the sulfur. Take the nurtured *yin* and *yang*, and boil them again in mallow juice for three *fu* periods. Then, combine them with the three yellows, grind finely, and form into a crucible to drench with mercury. Use fine bamboo to create dozens of holes in the crucible, pour mercury inside, and nurture with fire for seven days. Upon opening the box, the mercury will have transformed into high-grade gold. The ratio is four pours of mercury to one. A wondrous secret—guard it well.

**Cinnabar Drenching Method**
Take half a *jin* of cinnabar and wrap it loosely in silk, securing it tightly. Place it in a sand pot with rice vinegar, suspending it above the liquid, and simmer over low heat for one *fu* period. Add four *liang* of finely ground Sichuan aconite, wild aconite, Sichuan pepper, black pepper, paulownia bark, coptis, dog spine, *dijin tian*, and eggplant herb to the vinegar, then boil for another three *fu* periods. Remove, wipe clean, and while still hot, swiftly wrap each piece in mercury sand, ensuring meticulous and tight wrapping. If any part is left uncovered, replace it with a new piece of cinnabar. Coat with honey, roll in paulownia bark powder, then in the herbal powder, and place in a box. Line the bottom with herbs, evenly spread the cinnabar, layering two or three times, and cover with more herbs. Mix red halloysite, dipsacus, and gypsum with vinegar, add *liu yi* mud, and seal with Kunlun paper, applying a two-finger-thick layer. Repair any cracks, then dry in the shade.

Bury a jar in clean ground, filling it nine-tenths with water, level with the surface. Place the box on top, sealing the seams with salt mud. Mix fine charcoal ash with vinegar and mound it around the box. Pile five *jin* of live charcoal on top, ignite naturally, and let the fire burn for two-sixths or seven-sixths of the time before covering with yellow earth. The next day, remove the box, clear away the herbal ash, and the cinnabar will have transformed into silver-like pellets.

**Mercury Sand Binding Method**
Take ten *liang* of fine silver and chisel it into five to seven pieces. Heat half a *jin* of sesame oil in a Jian ware bowl over low fire, add mercury and the silver, and cook until the mixture breaks into a hundred strands. Slowly add the fragments one by one into the oil, continuing for two *fu* periods until hard sand-like granules form.

**Drenching and Fire Secrets**
Take the calcined cinnabar and line the bottom of a porcelain box with the aforementioned herbs. Add a layer of paulownia bark, then arrange the cinnabar silver pellets (quantity unrestricted) on the herbal powder in a lotus-like pattern, layering two or three times. Pour two *liang* of mercury on top, add another layer of paulownia bark, cover with herbs, and nurture over low fire for three full days. Upon opening the box, all will have transformed into *hanlin yushu* (frosted silver trees)—harvest and store them. Repeat the drenching and nurturing process five times, after which the cinnabar’s golden essence will no longer require herbs for drenching. Add four *liang* of nurtured mercury to collect sprouts. For larger quantities, use mountain silver to form beads. If using herbs to cover, nurture the sprouts for seven days. For every *liang* of sprouts, nurture two *liang* of fine silver beads. First melt the silver beads, then add the nurtured sprouts to refine them into an extraordinary silver, suitable for crafting crucibles and universally applicable.

When the sprouts fail to transform into silver, return them to the cinnabar crucible and nurture through nine cycles to produce the Great Elixir. It can transmute alum into gold, and when calcined into a *dao gui* (knife-point measure), it becomes flying sand.

**Dragon-Tiger Crucible Method**
Take three *liang* of fine, luminous cinnabar and half a *liang* of sulfur, grind them together finely, and wrap in boiled silk, binding it tightly. Then take one *jin* of needle sand, wash it thoroughly, and dry it. Place a large sweet-pot crucible in a furnace, first adding the needle sand, then the wrapped medicine, and cover with the remaining needle sand, sealing the mouth. Fire it once until the contents turn to ash. Upon removal, the medicine will appear green—this is the Dragon-Tiger Crucible.

Grind two *liang* of this fire-tamed sand, add half a *liang* of raw cinnabar, and grind evenly with the tamed sand. Place in a thick porcelain box, seal it, and nurture in an ash pit for seven days. Open, then add another half *liang* of raw cinnabar, grind with the tamed sand, and nurture for another seven days. Repeat the process, adding raw cinnabar until three *liang* of tamed sand are nurtured in the box, following the same method. For every *liang* of tamed sand, one *fen* of raw sand is managed. When nurtured to five *liang* or half a *jin*, pour three to five *liang* of mercury into the tamed sand, seal, and nurture for seven days. The three *liang* of mercury will merge into the sand, forming granules. Add another two *liang* of mercury and nurture for seven more days, whereupon a white frost will cover the sand. This frost, when ingested, grants immortality and can transmute mercury into treasure. Continue adding mercury to nurture it, and the elixir’s wonders will be boundless. If raw sand and mercury are repeatedly added to the tamed sand, its marvels defy description.

The fire must not exceed four *liang*; this must not be rashly transmitted.

**Secret Formula of the Golden Elixir**
The art of the Great Elixir does not extend beyond lead and mercury. The medicines of lead and mercury form the foundation of the Great Elixir. Lead and mercury mutually stimulate and restrain one another, yet neither departs from the principle of Heaven and Earth, the female and the male.

Now, lead pertains to *yin*, its color black, and it is the Dark Warrior. In terms of trigrams, it occupies the *Kan* position, receiving the *ren* and *gui* waters of the north. Water generates metal, whose color is white, and it is the White Tiger. Its trigram is *Dui*, belonging to the *geng* and *xin* metals of the west.

Mercury pertains to *yang*, its color blue-green, and it is the Azure Dragon. In terms of trigrams, it occupies the *Zhen* position, receiving the *jia* and *yi* woods of the east. Wood produces cinnabar, whose color is red, and it is the Vermilion Bird. Its trigram is *Li*, belonging to the *bing* and *ding* fires of the south.

Thus, *Kan* is lead, water, and the moon; *Li* is mercury, fire, and the sun. When *Kan* and *Li* are conjoined, the sun and moon unite, lead and mercury contend, the dragon and tiger couple. Neither dominates in function, for they mutually restrain one another. Only when the Yellow Dame facilitates their meeting does one attain the realm of perfection, and the Way of the Golden Elixir is effortlessly achieved.

1. First, take four *liang* of pure lead from superior mountain marshes, melt it, and fan to collect four *liang* of lead flowers for the crucible—this is the foundation of the elixir.

2. Take one *liang* of cinnabar as the standard, add four *fen* of raw sulfur, grind finely, and place in the water-and-fire crucible. Following the usual method, refine the mercury seven or eight times. Remove from the cold furnace, grind finely, then add half a *qian* of raw sulfur, three *fen* of raw male [ingredient], and two *qian* of mother powder boiled with lead. Grind these together, place in a small pot, and press firmly. Use equal parts of soft gypsum and talc powder to seal the top, ensuring it is tightly packed. Cover the pot’s mouth with a tile, bind with iron wire, seal, and place in the *weiji* furnace. Apply fire for half a *fu* period. When cool, remove the dice-shaped pieces, wrap them in silk, place inside, and suspend in a clay jar. Simmer with gentle fire for three *fu* periods.

3. For boiling the medicine, use *shibi* lychee and *yangjiao* vine. Chop finely, boil, add one cup of fresh ginger juice, and mix evenly. Place the juice inside and boil the cinnabar for three *fu* periods. After boiling, take the two aforementioned herbs in their dried, raw state, stir-fry with the cinnabar pieces until the herbs turn black and charred, then blow them away. Add fresh herbs and stir-fry for a full day, then place in the herb crucible.

4. **Herb Crucible Medicines**
   - One *liang* of *cewu* leaves.
   - One *liang* of *tiejiao* *poluomen*, finely divided.
   - One *liang* of gallnut powder.
   - One *liang* of cardamom powder.

Mix the above ingredients evenly, then place them in a box, lining the top and bottom. Seal tightly and bury in an ash jar for three *yang* cycles. For the first day, apply three *liang* of fire in the morning and two *liang* three *qian* in the evening. The next morning, apply one *liang* seven *qian*. All should be top-fire. After three cycles, remove the cinnabar pieces, roll them in refined honey, then coat with lead frost and mother powder, pressing closely. Return them to the mother crucible. For every *liang* of cinnabar, use three *liang* of mother powder refined with lead, layering and covering the cinnabar in a small box. Seal tightly to form the inner box, then place it within a larger box. For each *liang* of lead flowers, mix in three *qian* of yellow lead and blend evenly. Grind finely with milk, then fill the inner box completely, pressing firmly to form the outer crucible. Seal tightly, bind, and place in an ash jar. Nurture with gentle fire for twenty-one days. When the time is complete, open and inspect—if not yet "dead," nurture for another seven days, and it will be truly dead. Apply two and a half *liang* of top-fire for three days; three *liang* of top-fire for three days; three and a half *liang* of top-fire for five days; four *liang* of top-fire for five days. From the sixteenth to the twentieth day, apply four *liang* of top-fire, with three *liang* inserted in three directions. When the days are complete, remove the cinnabar—it will be truly dead. The mother must be saved each time before making another crucible. For each *liang* of mother, add three *qian* of mercury in a small box, seal tightly, and nurture with one and a half *liang* of fire for four or five days in an empty cycle. Then add the mother to the cinnabar and nurture again as before until the days are complete. The mother is then reused as before to nurture the cinnabar once more until the days are complete. The mother is again mixed with mercury and nurtured empty for three to five days. Then, as before, nurture the cinnabar once more until the days are complete. For three *liang* of mother, nurture one *liang* of cinnabar in the first cycle, another *liang* in the second, and another *liang* in the third, totaling three *liang* of cinnabar. Combine all, pound to break, then grind six *liang* of cinnabar finely with six *qian* of raw sulfur. Place together in a water-and-fire cauldron, seal tightly, and apply great fire for one *yang* cycle to form a molten mass. If any stray mercury remains on the water cauldron, scrape it off, then break the cauldron to retrieve the cinnabar. Pound it finely, then place in a clay vessel to stir-fry the cinnabar until red, removing the sulfur fumes. As the *Dan Jing* states: "Stir-frying with sulfur to harden"—this is it. Then return it to the original nurturing mother, using six mothers to make a crucible. The *Dan Jing* says: "Seek the living mother again to nurture together"—this is the harmony of the Four Symbols. Then nurture the bare cinnabar, which is the Way of the Infant and Elder Brother. For cinnabar that is lustrous and crystalline like a wall, use the previous method with herbal medicines for boiling and refining, then place in the herb crucible and nurture for seven cycles. The methods, fire phases, and durations remain the same as before, with no additions. When complete, remove the cinnabar, wash with water until clean, then roll in refined honey and coat with lead frost, pressing closely. Place in the mother cinnabar crucible, layering with lotus petals. For example, if using half a *jin* of dead cinnabar, use half a *jin* of the original nurturing mother to make the crucible, nurturing the bare infant—cinnabar—with up to four *liang* of cinnabar. Thereafter, make the Longevity Crucible. Apply one and a half *liang* of top-fire for fifteen days, increasing to three *liang*, with only top-fire for a total of twenty-one days. Open to inspect if it is truly dead. If there is a slight smoke, remix evenly, then layer with lotus petals as before, seal tightly, and nurture with three *liang* of fire for five to seven days—then it will be truly dead. When nurturing the Elder Girl, though the Infant and Elder Girl share the same origin, their forms differ. The Elder Girl has not yet given birth, while the Infant has already formed essence. Once the Infant is born, it is divine, numinous, communicative, and transformative, with boundless applications. When the husband and wife—Infant and Elder Girl—cohabit: two *liang* of cinnabar is the Infant, four *liang* of powder frost is the Elder Girl. For the powder alone, wrap in paper, then in silk, and suspend in a clay jar. Use *diding* herb, or purple river vehicle, or lotus leaf ash, and juice in a clay bottle. Simmer with gentle fire for two or three *fu* periods to remove the salt and alum fumes. Then grind finely with dead cinnabar, mix with paper mulberry juice to form a paste, and shape into cakes, each weighing about one *qian*, pressing tightly. Wrap each cake in two layers of black crucible paper, place in a small box, pressing firmly layer by layer. Cover the top with mother-made rhombus pieces to prevent any leakage. Then place another layer of black crucible paper on top, press the head with good dead arsenic, bind with iron wire, seal tightly as before, and place in the Uncompleted Cauldron to nurture with fire. The Elder Girl, in heaven, is white snow; on earth, the dark gourd; in humans, powder frost. Immortals compare her to the Elder Girl—nothing more than mercury. Born from the womb of living cinnabar, she is the essence of mercury and the blackness of cinnabar. Stirred, she does not cloud; settled, she does not clear. Born in the crevices of high mountains, nothing can obstruct her form. Gentle, bright, and pure, chaff cannot sully her substance. This is the medicine of longevity, the treasure of transmutation, the world’s most precious thing—nothing compares. In the Uncompleted Cauldron, fire above and water below, all with top-fire. From the first to the fifth day, one *liang*; from the sixth to the tenth day, one and a half *liang*; from the eleventh to the fifteenth day, two *liang*. When the days are complete, transfer to the Bright Departure Cauldron to nurture. Remove the cinnabar powder, and for each *liang* of cinnabar powder, use two *liang* of bare cinnabar to make the crucible. Place the cinnabar powder cakes in a small box, layering with lotus petals, then cover with gold crucible paper. As before, cover the surface with sacred silver pieces, press the head with honey-dead arsenic, seal tightly, and place in a large crucible box. Fill the exterior with arsenic and sulfur, seal tightly, and place in the Bright Departure Cauldron. On the box, make an iron wire cover, about half an inch high above the box, to serve as a standard. Place in an ash jar to nurture with fire. When changing the fire, apply it only to the cover, so the fire’s height will naturally be regulated.

The Bright Departure Cauldron and its top fire. Nurture for one seven-day period with three *liang* of fire. For the next seven days, three and a half *liang* of fire. For the following seven days, four *liang* of fire. For the next seven days, five *liang* of fire. Within the first seven days, maintain three *liang* of top fire, inserting eleven *liang* in three directions. When the days are complete, open and inspect—true death of the powder is the standard. If smoke or flame appears, nurture with fire for another seven days, and it will truly die.

For example, if the nurtured cinnabar powder frost amounts to six *liang*, adjust the size of the crucible accordingly. If there are six *liang*, extract four *liang* of cinnabar powder and store separately. For the remaining two *liang* of cinnabar powder, mix with two *liang* of raw powder, also forming cakes, and place in the previous cinnabar crucible. Nurture with fire as before until the days are complete. Then remove this cinnabar powder and combine with the previously stored four *liang*, totaling half a *jin*, to serve as the Jade Field Crucible for nurturing White Snow.

**Jade Field Crucible Standard: Half a *jin***
Take four *liang* of raw powder, break into pieces the size of soybeans, and boil with lotus leaf ash or soap bean ash infusion for one to two *fu* periods using slow fire. Coat with raw *cizhong* powder and lead white frost mixed with vinegar, applying it to the dead powder. Then place in the Jade Field Crucible, layer with lotus, seal tightly, and nurture with slow fire for fifteen days—it will truly die. If not, nurture for another two or three days, and it will truly die.

At this stage, use two *qian* to transmute one *liang*, forming treasure. When the days are complete, remove it. Fire regimen and top fire:
- One *liang* of fire for five days.
- One *liang* and two *qian* of fire for five days.
- One *liang* and five *qian* of fire for five days.

When the days are complete, remove and obtain four *liang* of White Snow for storage. Add another four *liang* of raw powder, also boiled with lotus leaf ash infusion for two *fu* periods. Coat with raw *cizhong* and lead white frost as before, then place in the Jade Field Crucible and nurture for thirty-five days. At this point, obtain half a *jin* of White Snow, named the White Snow Crucible, for nurturing the Divine Talisman Great Elixir.

**White Snow Crucible Standard: Half a *jin***
Take four *liang* of raw powder pieces, break into small soybean-sized chunks, and boil with ginger juice, lotus root juice, and half a *qian* each of raw *cizhong* for one *fu* period. Remove, wash clean, coat with White Snow, place in the White Snow Crucible, seal tightly as before, and nurture with fire in the Bright Departure Cauldron. Fire regimen and top fire:
- One *liang* of fire for five days.
- One *liang* and two *qian* of fire for five days.
- One and a half *liang* of fire for five days.

When the days are complete, remove and obtain four *liang* of Divine Talisman for storage. Add another four *liang* of raw powder, boil with lotus root and ginger juice for one *fu* period, then boil with raw *cizhong* as before. Coat with White Snow, place in the White Snow Crucible, and nurture with fire for fifteen days until it truly dies. Obtain another four *liang* of Divine Talisman, totaling half a *jin* for the crucible.

**Divine Talisman Great Elixir Longevity Crucible**
For half a *jin* of Divine Talisman, take four *liang* of cinnabar mercury, shred with paper, and use a goose feather tube to pour the seed into the Divine Talisman Crucible. Nurture with one *liang* of fire for three days to form Jade Sprouts. Extract these sprouts without boiling or washing, shape into dice-sized pieces, and place back into the crucible. Nurture with fire as before for fifteen days to form the Supreme Treasure. One *qian* transmutes one *liang* of base metal into Supreme Treasure, and one *qian* can dry one *liang* of mercury into Supreme Treasure. Proceed thus in stages without end—this is the Longevity Great Medicine, perpetually unbroken across generations.

**Danyang Bone-Transmuting Method**
For dead arsenic, grind purple river vehicle into powder. For each *liang* of arsenic powder, mix with one and a half *liang* of river vehicle powder, blend evenly, and place in a sweet pot. Heat from mild to intense fire to instantly kill, then form a crucible. This method is most efficacious for nurturing powder frost, surpassing all others.

For refined powder frost, boil and coat with raw male essence, then place in the crucible to nurture. Ingredients:
- One *liang* of mercury.
- One *liang* of salt.
- Two *liang* of alum.
- Six *qian* of nitre.

First grind the three ingredients into fine powder, add one *liang* of mercury, and grind until no stars remain. Place in a water-and-fire vessel, heat slowly from mild to intense, until four cups of water have evaporated. When cool, remove the next day—all will have ascended to the bottom of the cup. Remove, boil with lotus leaf ash infusion for one *fu* period, and wash with boiling water several times. Then remove the alum flavor, place in the arsenic crucible, layer with lotus, and nurture for two seven-day periods. Fire regimen:
- First day: two *liang* of fire, top fire in the ash pool.
- Second day: two and a half *liang*.
- Third day: two and a half *liang*.
- Fourth to sixth day: three *liang*.
- Seventh to tenth day: three and a half *liang*.
- Tenth to fourteenth day: four *liang*.

Remove and test over fire. If not subdued, nurture for another seven days.

**Alternative Method**
For dead arsenic, boil with natural spinach leaf juice for one *fu* period to instantly kill. Use *tuoti* teeth (i.e., northern *huihui* calamine) ground into powder, mixed with northern date pulp, and pounded into a paste. Coat the bottom of a sweet pot, shape like a pot, and dry in the sun. Then place one *liang* of bone and one *qian* of dead arsenic on top, cover with *tuoti* date paste, fill the pot with salt, and heat from mild to intense until the pot glows red. Remove to obtain top-grade silver.

**Cinnabar Crucible Pouring and Drenching Method**
Fire regimen: civil and martial fire from top to bottom. Fire control is crucial for the sealing method—this is the first and foremost divine verification of the elixir path. Guard it well; intense fire will cause primordial leakage.

Grind one *jin* of *shan* (realgar), half a *jin* of *hu* (tiger bone?), and half a *jin* of mixed powder evenly, sift finely, add well-flower water, and pound with a stone pestle a thousand times until it becomes a glue-like paste for sealing.

**Oil Method**
Select fine, blue-white porcelain shards, grind them to powder, place in an iron pan, and stir-fry over intense fire. Add equal parts bamboo leaves and rush pith, continuing to stir-fry until the porcelain turns to ash. Sift through fine silk, then mix with well-flower water to create an oil-water sealant. Apply this oil to the surface of the accumulated medicine—aged oil is best. For sealing the mouth of a crucible: first twist *tangxin* (arsenic trioxide) into paper strips with tapered ends, insert tightly into the seam, then apply the aforementioned paste to level it. Brush the surface with oil-water, wait a day for it to dry, add another layer of paste, and finally seal with salt-clay. For sealing the bottom of a crucible or any sand holes or small pores that may leak medicine: first apply a thin, water-diluted layer of paste, then line with two or three layers of *tangxin* paper. Apply the paste to a thickness of two or three *fen*, brush with oil, and finally seal with salt-clay. All superior sealing methods derive from this—top-grade, top-grade.

**Elixir Method**
Take half a *jin* of cinnabar and suspend it in good rice vinegar, gently simmering for three *fu* (forty-day periods). Then add four *liang* of powdered herbal medicine and continue simmering until dry. Remove, wipe clean, and while still hot, quickly wrap each piece of cinnabar with mercury sand as prescribed. Any piece left unwrapped will be ruined. Once wrapped, coat with honey, sprinkle with *wutonglü* (paulownia twig powder), apply another layer of honey, then dust with herbal powder. When dry, line the bottom of a box with herbal medicine, arrange the cinnabar pieces evenly, cover with another layer of herbs, then another layer of cinnabar, repeating three to five times until full. Seal the box’s seams with red halloysite clay, patching any damaged areas, and let dry in the shade. Then reinforce externally with salt-clay and dry again in the shade. Bury a jar in a clean place, filling it with water to nine-tenths capacity, its mouth level with the ground. Place the sealed box atop the jar, seal the junction between box and jar with clay, and mound vinegar-mixed ash around the box. Pile five *jin* of charcoal around it, ignite naturally, and when the fire reaches six or seven-tenths intensity, cover with yellow earth. The next day, remove the herbal ash to find the half-*jin* of cinnabar transformed entirely into silver-like pellets.

**Herbal Ingredients for Cinnabar (Half-*Jin* Cinnabar Requires Half-*Jin* Each of the Following):**
Aconite (*chuanwu*), wild aconite (*caowu*), black pepper, Sichuan pepper, coptis, *gouji* (cibotium), *nanxing* (arisaema), pinellia, *wutonglü* (paulownia twig powder).

**Method for Wrapping Cinnabar with Mercury Sand**
Take five *liang* of mercury and five *liang* of silver foil, divide into three to five pieces, and place in sesame oil. Gradually transfer to a crucible and heat until amalgamated. Remove the mercury-silver sand, repeat the process until all mercury is exhausted.

**Verse on Pouring and Nurturing Fire After Cinnabar Transformation**
Lead sand resists fire, no smoke remains,
A swift path to the Elixir’s alchemical gains.
Nine herbs within the crucible confined,
A single lead without—its power enshrined.
Lead leaves its mother, child follows wife,
Transcending the mundane, the Dao’s subtle life.
Once cinnabar submits to fire’s embrace,
Behold: mercury dries without a trace.

**Method for Completing the Great Elixir Through Pouring**
Take the transformed cinnabar, line the bottom of a vessel with the aforementioned herbs, then add a layer of *wutonglü* powder (quantity as desired). Arrange the cinnabar evenly in two or three layers, then pour mercury over it. Begin with two *liang* for the initial nurturing, sufficient for three days. Upon opening, the contents will resemble a forest of jade trees in winter—gather and grind them to an extremely fine powder. Repeat the process: line with herbs, arrange cinnabar, sprinkle the gathered "winter forest" powder evenly over the cinnabar, then pour another two *liang* of mercury. Repeat the gathering, grinding, and layering, ensuring the mercury is absorbed into the "winter forest" powder rather than the cinnabar. After five iterations, the cinnabar will grow increasingly potent, eliminating the need for herbal lining—thus forming an immortal crucible. For pouring, add four *liang* of mercury to cultivate "sprouts." To produce more "mountain silver smoke" as beads, or if using pre-subdued white灵砂 (mercury sulfide) resembling lotus seeds, nurture one *liang* of sprouts with two *liang* of it for seven days to yield top-grade immortal silver, a metal beyond the ordinary. It can be used to refine *geng* (lead) into a crucible, nurture the Three Yellows, or produce yellow sprouts for transmuting *geng*. With prolonged mercury application, it becomes high-grade purple gold. If not used for a crucible, place it in a cinnabar vessel and nurture it nine times to become the supreme Elixir. It can transmute base metals, copper, iron, and the Eight Stones into gold; ingesting a *daogui* (knife-tip measure) will make one immortal.

**Method for True Dead Cinnabar Juice Crucible and Pouring to Form the Great Elixir**
Found abundantly in the western mountains, also called "golden lotus herb." Take any amount of cinnabar and *huanghua jichangcao* (yellow-flowered chicken-intestine herb, also called "step-by-step lotus" or "immortals sitting face-to-face grass"). Pound to extract juice, simmer the cinnabar for three *fu*, then dry it. Wrap the cinnabar in the herbal residue, encase in *kunlun* paper, and seal externally with salt-clay. Dry, then heat from mild to intense until the vessel glows red. After prolonged cooling, open to find the cinnabar truly dead—unaltered by fire. Alternatively, wrap the cinnabar in herbal residue, place in a vessel, pack tightly with yellow clay, seal the seams with oyster shell powder, and nurture with two *liang* of fire for seven days to achieve true death. Then mix with realgar, orpiment, and lead yellow flower (one part to ten parts cinnabar), add three parts juice, grind uniformly with the cinnabar, heat a crucible until red-hot, add the medicine, and fan with intense fire until it melts into liquid. Once cooled, it becomes a treasure.

To refine mercury, use four parts to one. Add it to the previous elixir, nurture with two *liang* of fire for three days, and the mercury will die and sprout buds. When pouring to stack and nurture the buds, take as much as desired—all will become supreme treasures, entering the *geng* Dao.

**Method for Obtaining Lead Yellow Flower**
Alternatively, knead the stems and leaves of *linglingxiang* into small balls and place them in the juice. If the juice does not form, add one *liang* of yellow lead, pack tightly into a crucible, and heat until red-hot. Pierce a hole in the center with an iron rod, insert a white aconite, and fan with intense fire until the elixir melts into liquid. After prolonged cooling, open the crucible to retrieve the lead yellow flower, its color fine, equal to two parts orpiment. The lead residue at the bottom of the crucible may weigh two or three *qian*, resembling silver. Then place the previously dead cinnabar into the crucible, melt the settled lead into liquid, pour it over the cinnabar, and heat—all will become a supreme treasure. Wondrous, this is the art of immortals.

**True Dead Cinnabar to Transmute Lead into Silver and the Pouring Method for Vault Heads**
Take one *liang* of cinnabar. Boil it in a small bowl of natural juice from pounded *yege* until dry. Then wrap the cinnabar in the herbal residue, place it in a jar, pack tightly with the residue, seal externally with spirit clay, and dry. Heat with three *jin* of charcoal fire. After cooling in the furnace, the cinnabar will be truly dead, not diminished by a single fraction. For every *qian*, transmute one *liang* of pure lead into red-colored silver, resisting fire to become a true treasure. It may also transmute base metals. Alternatively, pour mercury into a vault to nurture it, and the "Laughing Jade of the Cold Forest" will form into the Great Elixir.

**Another Method**
Grind *guibeijianghuang* and *tiannanxing* into powder. Boil cinnabar with them for three *fu*. Then mix the fine powder with honey, wrap the cinnabar, place it in a crucible, and heat—the cinnabar will be truly dead. Next, combine with *jindingpi* and melt into liquid, or use dead *pengsha* alone to achieve the same. Alternatively:

**Method for Dead *Pengsha***
Spread powdered *zhimu* on the bottom, place *pengsha* in the center, and cover with more *zhimu*. Heat until it melts into liquid for use.

**Another Method**
Wrap three to five layers of cinnabar in *xiazhucao*, bind with iron wire, and place in a vessel. Use *baizhi* and *caowu* as auxiliary powder, stir-fry the wrapped cinnabar until ready, then grind into fine powder. Mix with rice vinegar into a paste, line the bottom and top of a crucible, seal the mouth with a clay lid, bind with iron wire, and seal tightly. Heat with three *jin* of fire. After a long while, remove and cool—the cinnabar will be truly dead, its original color unchanged. Most wondrous, it transmutes substances, nurtures cinnabar in a vault, or pours mercury. Secretly transmitted by the "Undying Yang Lord," after nurturing the "Sun and Moon Elixir" in a vault, pouring mercury yields the Great Elixir.

**Refining Sulfur**
Take one *liang* of good sulfur, pound into powder. First boil with *wubeizi* for a day, discard the residue. Then replace with *huangqin*, *huanglian*, and *dahuang*, decoct into a thick juice, and boil for two more days until fully subdued. Next, use *wubeizi* to blacken it. Mix with egg white, first coat the inside of a box once. Then blacken again and coat two or three more times. Place the sulfur inside and nurture for seven days—its color will resemble yellow gold. Use this to further nurture *song* into a "Spiritual Sage Vault," and nurture the "Two Yellow Elixir Heads" for fourteen days to succeed. Nurturing cinnabar thus yields endless transformations.

**Nurturing Cinnabar Spirit**
Take ten *liang* of subdued cinnabar as the base. Retrieve the treasure, grind into powder, and first form a treasure vault. Then gather five parts of "Mother Sand" and process each according to the method. For every *liang*, divide this sand into four or five rounds, arrange them like lotus petals in the treasure vault, nurture for seven days, then open to retrieve the mercury sand. Extract the "Old Man’s Beard," sift the dry mercury—white as willow catkins, forming strands—this is the true dead dry mercury, the treasure of elixirs and the essence of supreme medicine. Heaven and earth gain brilliance from it, all things gain spirit from it. This is the boundless transformation of creation, the eternal cycle of life, an everlasting plan. Though there are thousands of classics and ten thousand scrolls, none surpass this principle. Those who seek recklessly will find it difficult to align with the Dao.

**Mercury Pouring Formula**
First take the previously nurtured, visible treasure cinnabar as the elixir base, grind into mung bean-sized pieces—ten *liang* for example. First pour five *liang*, open once every seven days, reseal, and nurture for five more days. Retrieve the mercury, now firm and dry. Then take the remaining five *liang* of subdued mercury, refine for seven days, open, and nurture for another seven days. Retrieve this true treasure, the transformed dry mercury, named "White Snow Divine Elixir." With ten *liang* of secret transmission, pour mercury to transform into treasure.

**Dry Formula**
Use ten *liang* of the previously nurtured cinnabar spirit as the base, lightly crush, and collect with subdued mercury. Use *yangtigen*, *longdancao*, and *duniuxi*. Boil the mercury with the spiritual herbs, pour the subdued mercury onto the base, and pour four *liang* of this subdued mercury from heaven, opening after seven days. Then pour three *liang* of subdued mercury from earth, nurture for seven days, and open—do not pour this mercury at this time, but nurture for five days before removing. Add another three *liang* of poured subdued mercury, nurture for seven days, and open. Altogether, the original ten *liang* of subdued mercury and the elixir base total twenty *liang* of treasure. First use the original ten *liang* of subdued mercury elixir base for the furnace process, leaving this as the "seated womb mother." Then set aside the ten *liang* of poured mercury treasure, boundless in transformation, the great champion of the world.

**Subduing and Pouring Dry Treasure *Kun* Mercury**
Use a twelve-*liang* crucible, place two *liang* of the previously poured treasure mercury inside, with ten *liang* of raw mercury on top. Sprinkle two *qian* of true dead cinnabar to cover, secure externally with silk paper, and brush gently with *yangtigen* juice. Heat in the crucible, gradually subduing until soft and pliable. Then remove and place on the ground, cool, open, and retrieve the treasure—twelve *liang* in total.

Use a single clay tile to cover securely, binding and sealing it tightly within. Then take the dregs of *yangtigen*, pound them into a paste, and smear them thoroughly over the seal. Bury in a pit in a shady spot, pile charcoal around it, and ignite a top fire. After one night with the lower crucible in place, remove and pass through the barrier—thus the treasure is formed.

The classic states:
When mercury dies, then mercury dies again,
Dead mercury, ah, dead mercury.
Living mercury transforms into true guest mercury,
As you command, its wondrous transformations reach the divine.

**First Transformation**
This wondrous method begins by uniting two substances of cinnabar spirit, placing them in an alum matrix as the chamber, and nurturing them until the treasure appears for use.

**Second Transformation**
Within the cinnabar spirit chamber, nurture the mother cinnabar until the child is born. When the aged *xi* must emerge, it gathers the qi of heaven and earth, forming cinnabar and dry mercury.

**Third Transformation**
Take the aged *xi* whiskers obtained, accumulate them as the chamber, and pour subdued mercury to grow jade shoots and jasper branches.

**Fourth Transformation**
Combine the previous jade shoots and jasper branches with the aged *xi* whiskers in equal parts to form the sacred chamber, then refine them into cinnabar divine elixir.

**Fifth Transformation**
Use this cinnabar and blend it into the sacred treasure chamber.
Then nurture the yin and yang to create the great medicinal divine elixir.
These two transformations, when added to golden elixir immortal medicine, still fall short—only the latter two suffice.

A poem says:
Seven transformations of cinnabar, the work of creation,
The mortal womb now becomes a great immortal elder.
Clad in white, leaping beyond the Dragon Gate,
A great minister’s body commands all phenomena.
Sun and moon, heaven and earth lie in your palm,
Transforming into red, soaring as crane’s tracks.
The great medicine refined, gold within mercury,
As you command, its divine transformations abound.

**Elbow-Pouch Wondrous Medicine**
Use the previous sacred treasure chamber to first nurture four *liang* of powdery frost into pills. Divide each *liang* into five pills, then place them in the chamber for nurturing. Open once every seven days, and outside the chamber, condense three *qian* of mother cinnabar into one *liang*. Knead into cakes or balls, bind securely, and nurture for another seven days, opening twice. Then return them to the treasure chamber for a full seven days, and upon removal, they become white snow divine elixir—three *qian* subdues one *liang* of red silver.

**Smelting Cinnabar into Liquid for the Chamber**
Take one *liang* of *geng*-path cinnabar and half a *liang* of realgar, grind them together. Boil yellow flower and chicken-intestine grass for three *fu* periods, extract the juice, and mix with the cinnabar and realgar to form balls. Then wrap the balls with the boiled grass, coat externally with plaster made from gypsum powder and honey, and seal with refined clay. Once dry, gradually increase the fire from gentle to fierce until thoroughly red. After cooling, retrieve it—the cinnabar has truly melted into liquid. For use in the *geng*-path, apply gold leaf as adhesive medicine to each piece, then use lead white frost and realgar powder to stir-fry with the cinnabar. When the gold leaf merges with the cinnabar, place the medicine in the crucible, and with one firing, it becomes golden cinnabar, suitable for transmutation or as a chamber.

**Method for Dead Cinnabar**
Take one *liang* of cinnabar and *wanzhou* yellow medicine the size of a chicken egg (all others are not genuine), along with half a *liang* each of *qumai*. Grind them into fine powder. Then take fresh *yi*, pound it to extract the juice, and mix it with the two medicines to the proper consistency. Place half of this mixture at the bottom of the tripod, set the cinnabar in the center, and cover the top with the remaining medicinal paste. Gently press to level and compact it. Cover with two layers of damp paper, then seal with a water-filled dish, ensuring it is airtight and dry. Gradually increase the fire from gentle to intense, adding water as the charcoal fire burns. After the fire has thoroughly reddened the vessel, allow it to cool, then open—thus the cinnabar is truly dead.

**Another Method**
Take any amount of cinnabar, and use mulberry root bark, *gouqi* berries, *nanxing*, and *wutou* ground into a fine powder. Boil them to extract the juice, suspend the cinnabar in the liquid, and boil for three *fu* periods before removing. Grind *xipeng*, *daqing*, alum, *que*, and powdery frost into powder, then mix with vinegar to form a paste. Coat the cinnabar thoroughly, then place *peng* sand and table salt in the bottom of a sweet crucible. Set the cinnabar ball in the center, cover the top with *peng* salt to fill completely, seal with a clay tile, and ensure it is airtight and dry. With one firing, the treasure is formed, suitable for nurturing mother cinnabar in the chamber. After seven days, the chamber yields the treasure.

For the first and second days, use one and a half *liang* of fire.
For the third day, use two *liang*.

For the third, fourth, and fifth days, use two and a half *liang* of fire.
For the sixth and seventh days, use three *liang*.

**Another Method**
Take one *liang* of cinnabar and one and a half *liang* of *yimu* herb, along with sheep’s-hoof leaves. Grind these two into powder, spread them to line the bottom and cover the top, ensuring it is tightly packed, then seal and dry. Fire with five *jin* of flame for one firing. The sulfur is subdued into liquid.

Boil in rehmannia juice for seven *fu* periods, then cease the fire. If the cinnabar’s color remains unchanged and it liquefies upon heating, the rehmannia water will separate: that which floats is "heavenly yellow," that which is half-submerged is "human yellow," and that which sinks is "earthly yellow," indicating the loss of *qi*.

**Subduing Sulfur**
Use the natural juice of *daqing*, boil for twenty-eight days, and "nurture the pine to true death" three times before adding one *jin* of mercury. For each instance, add two *liang* of mercury to the sulfur, then replenish with fresh mercury for restoration. Do not allow contact with iron vessels.

**Another Method**
Use the natural juice of chive blossoms, boil in a ceramic vessel for seven *fu* periods, and it will immediately die. "Nurture the pine to true death" as before, then coat with mercury. This is also suitable for restoration.

**Another Method**
Use the natural juice of white-flowered *yimu* herb, boil for seven *fu* periods, then test over fire. If not subdued, boil for another two or three days. Spread the dregs of *yimu* herb to line the bottom and cover the top, then fire gradually from slow to intense. Add three to five days of firing, and it will die. Prepare a chamber for the great elixir to nurture the Three Yellows.

**Another Method**
Pound *shuijiaojiao* to extract its juice, boil sulfur for one or two days until subdued and dead, then fire.

**The Supreme Cavern-Mystery Great Elixir Formula**
This formula was eternally concealed by the Supreme Emperor within the Jade Casket. When it appears in the world, it is because the primordial will has destined it for those of true Daoist intent. When the Emperor manifests in the mortal realm, divine beings transmit it. One must fast, bathe, purify the heart, and face the Three Palaces of the Jade Emperor to solemnly swear an oath, vowing never to recklessly divulge it. Thereafter, burn incense, focus the mind, and contemplate it.

The Four Yellows must be supported by the Four Sands.
**Explanation:** The Four Yellows are: water-cave realgar, imported sulfur, leaf orpiment, and arsenic yellow. The Four Sands are: Chenxi cinnabar, radiant sleeve cinnabar, lustrous *xipeng* sand, and needle sand.

These eight ingredients—first take needle sand, place it in a mortar, and grind finely with good rice vinegar. Then transfer to an iron pan and stir-fry until red. Next, add the remaining ingredients.

"Present them toward the frost base to unite at the corner."
**Explanation:** The "frost base" refers to *fen shuang* (powdery frost). Among the nine ingredients above, *fen shuang* is the essence of yin. The other eight are all yang. Using this one yin is called "the old yang seizing the young yin."

"Grind them three thousand times, yielding one *jin* and two *liang*."
**Explanation:** Grind three thousand times, and the two nines make eighteen, which is one *jin* and two *liang* of the medicine. Grind them together in one place.

"Master Ge’s harmonization requires skillful effort."
**Explanation:** "Master Ge" refers to purple *ge* vine. Take about five *jin*, remove the rough skin, and pound to extract the natural juice. Mix the nine ingredients above into a paste, adjusting its softness and hardness appropriately.

Sun Simiao said: "Purple *ge* vine is the essence of earth and can capture the Four Yellows and Four Sands to form the treasure."

"Within the golden hall, it is fitting to refine thrice."
**Explanation:** Coat the previous medicinal paste with gold foil, layering it threefold.

"In the Azure Water Palace, fire one furnace."
**Explanation:** "Azure Water" refers to green salt, which is the essence of water. Use a sand box—an iron box is even better. Fill the box with green salt to cover the top completely. Bind the seams with iron wire, then seal with red halloysite, white kaolin, salt flowers, and oyster shell. Choose an auspicious day to place it in the furnace.

The furnace should be three *chi* and two *cun* high and one *chi* and eight *cun* wide. Beneath it, bury a water vat, also one *chi* and eight *cun* deep, called "yearning for yin." Construct the furnace above with new bricks and clay. Inside, create a measuring seat to hold the medicinal ball, covering it with fine ash. The fire should be eight *cun* and four *fen* away from the medicine—just as the human heart is eight *cun* and four *fen* from the kidneys.

One must fast, bathe, and enter a purified chamber, contemplating the Dao and meditating on the true. Nurture the fire for three days, ensuring the fire-timing method is precise. Add charcoal four times daily, aligning with the *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* hours. Once the fire-timing is complete, add mercury as follows.

"When the old woman’s daughter marries, she must be a match."
**Explanation:** After nurturing the fire, grind the previous medicine finely in a mortar, then add two *liang* of mercury. Grind until no specks remain. Mix again with purple *ge* vine juice and seal as before.

"Civil ends, martial concludes, and the world responds to the primordial."
**Explanation:** The sage observes the fire, making the heart’s fire like the external fire. Heaven has form: the sun, moon, and stars. Earth has form: metal, water, and fire. Refine them with civil and martial fire.

When using it, form purple *ge* vine into pea-sized pills.
**Explanation:** Open the ball to retrieve the medicine, grind it finely, and mix with purple *ge* vine juice to form pea-sized pills. Store them in a clean box, and they will emit radiance.

"One pill can transmute five *liang* of the withered."
**Explanation:** Place five *liang* of mercury in a Jian ware bowl, set it over a boiling water steamer, and add one pill of the medicine, grinding it finely and sprinkling it in. Cover the bowl and seams with damp paper, then heat the steamer with intense fire. After a moment, a sound like fine rain will be heard, followed by a long silence, then a single sound like tearing silk—the mercury will be dry. Pour it into a mold, and upon exposure to wind, it will harden into the finest soft, malleable silver.

**True Silver**
Melt five *liang* of silver into liquid, then add three pills of the medicine in three separate applications. When poured out, it will be one hundred percent pure.

For five *liang* of *shanxue* red gold or copper, remove all lead *qi*, then add two pills in two applications. When refined, it becomes *danyang* "bone-changing" pure white silver.

"If people in the world can ingest it,"
**Explanation:** For any severe illness, regardless of age, take one pill, grind it again into powder, and form it with jujube pulp into mung-bean-sized pills. Take one pill on an empty stomach with well-drawn morning water. This will prolong life, prevent aging, and ward off all diseases.

Only to transform the earth into a realm of immortals.
**Explanation:** This elixir is most secret—if lightly disclosed, it will bring calamity upon nine generations.

*Yudao Ji*, Scroll Four concludes.
