*(Note: Before the phrase "these two transformations," it is suspected that the sections on the Sixth and Seventh Transformations are missing.)*

*Yudao Ji*, Scroll Five

**Method for Destroying Cinnabar**
Hundred-flower serves as the base—this is honey.
Red seal makes the lid—this is Sichuan pepper.
Morning glory acts as the companion—white morning glory.
Wolfberry serves as the worthy companion.
Charcoal fire, by the *jin* measure, until the cinnabar dies—then cease.

*For ten years I studied the elixir’s tortoise,*
*What more could I seek after this?*

Use a porcelain box, coat the inside with honey, then sprinkle morning glory and wolfberry powder atop. Next, place the prepared cinnabar inside, cover it with Sichuan pepper, bind it tightly with iron wire, seal the seams with salt-clay, and subject it to fire for destruction.

**Method for Sprinkling and Steeping**
Take cinnabar, regardless of quantity, and use mallow (red mallow is also suitable). Grind it into a paste. First, spread a layer inside the box, then grind the cinnabar to remove its sharp edges. Use willow-leaf gold-star herb powder, mixed with honey to form a close-fitting wrap, and place it over the mallow paste. Cover it again with mallow paste. Seal the opening with red halloysite, then reinforce the exterior with salt-clay. Wait until dry, then apply an eight-*jin* fire for steeping. Once cooled, remove it, replace the inner lining, and seal as before. Apply another eight-*jin* fire for destruction. Repeat this process three times, and the cinnabar will be "dead."

Use three *liang* of this dead cinnabar to nurture one *liang* of raw cinnabar. Gradually increase the quantity, and with each transformation, it will grow more potent, capable of steeping mercury. For every three *liang* of the vessel’s contents, one *liang* of mercury can be steeped, with two *liang* of top-fire applied for seven days to complete the process.

**Method for Further Nurturing Raw Cinnabar**
Take one *liang* of dead cinnabar powder and mix it with one *liang* of raw cinnabar, grinding them finely together. First, spread one *liang* of dead cinnabar at the bottom of the box, then place the mixture inside, and cover it with another *liang* of dead cinnabar. Seal the seams with red halloysite, reinforce the exterior with salt-clay, and wait until dry. Apply two *liang* of top-fire and nurture for seven days. Then, subject it to a three-*jin* fire for one firing, and the raw cinnabar will also be "dead."

For steeping on the powder, first press the cinnabar to make it level and firm, then create a small depression in the center. Pour mercury into it. Seal the seams with red halloysite, reinforce with salt-clay, apply two *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for seven days. It will form a single mass within the depression—most wondrous.

**Method for Subduing Cinnabar**
For each *liang*, pack the cavity tightly with five-phase herb powder, then apply a one-*jin* fire until exhausted. Repeat this process once more, after which it can be subjected to white destruction.

**Cinnabar Subdued by Fire Reveals Treasure**
Also called *Nine Transformations Increasing the Gushing Spring Vessel*, or *Buddha Nods Approval*.

Two *liang* of silver powder
Four *liang* of mercury

Place the above ingredients together into a crucible, add half a spoonful of *Stellera chamaejasme* powder on top.

Again take two layers of round paper, moisten them with saliva, and seal the crucible’s mouth. Apply two *jin* of charcoal fire to press it until the paper slightly scorches and the fragrance of *Stellera chamaejasme* is detected. Then lift it onto cold ashes, and when it cools enough to handle, remove the paper. Pour the contents into a ceramic vessel, blow away the *Stellera chamaejasme*, and grind the cinnabar lumps thoroughly in an iron mortar. Sift through two layers of boiled silk, and weigh it—if less than six *liang*, refine it again. Even if it falls below six *liang*, it may still be paired with the mother-mercury, which is even more wondrous. Wash it three times with water, then sift again, and it will become cinnabar powder.

Next, take five *liang* or ten *liang* of granular cinnabar from Chenzhou, place it in a one-*liang*-weight raw silk pouch, and suspend it in a jar. Use fermented water or mild vinegar, along with one *liang* each of *Stellera chamaejasme* powder, *Sanguisorba officinalis* powder, and *Clematis chinensis* powder in the jar. First add three spoonfuls and boil, then replenish gradually over the next day until the medicine is exhausted, steeping it in a double boiler for three days. Remove the pouch, rinse with warm water, and dry it in a wok. For each piece of cinnabar, wrap it tightly with the previously refined cinnabar powder, adjusting the amount according to size—six *liang* of powder for two *liang* of cinnabar.

Then take five *liang* or ten *liang* of asbestos (quantity flexible), grind it to a fine powder, and prepare a clean ceramic box. First spread a layer of asbestos powder at the bottom, then arrange the cinnabar pieces like lotus seeds, cover with another layer of asbestos, add more cinnabar, and top with asbestos, pressing firmly. Seal the box’s seams with clam powder mixed with vinegar, then reinforce with paper-fiber and salt-clay. Without waiting for it to dry, place it in an ash pit and nurture it with three or four *liang* of charcoal fire for five to seven days. Remove the box and apply five to six *jin* of fire until it glows red—no harm in excess. When two-thirds of the fire’s intensity has passed, withdraw the heat, open the box when cool, and the cinnabar will have transformed into silver ingots, now weighing no more than four *liang*. The mercury has departed, leaving only the cinnabar-silver matrix, which is the elixir head.

Grind this cinnabar and refine it again into powder as before, wrapping it around cinnabar pieces, placing them in the box, and layering with asbestos. Subject it to full refinement, then remove the cinnabar—this is the first transformation. Weigh it and divide into two portions. Refine one half again into powder, wrap it around cinnabar, nurture and refine it, then weigh and divide—this is the second transformation. Repeat this process for a total of nine transformations, at which point it becomes void, ascending from the mundane to the sacred. The alum-silver is entirely exhausted, leaving only mercury.

Grind this medicine finely, mix half a *liang* with mercury, and place it in the box. Alternatively, mix one *liang* with four *liang* of mercury, omitting the asbestos. Seal it tightly and nurture for seven days, then pour more mercury. If the box becomes half-full, add more. When one or two *jin* of "dead" mercury is obtained, crush it to make an outer vessel. Place a smaller box inside this vessel, as when nurturing sulfur, and nurture for seven days to "kill" it. This method also applies to realgar, orpiment, cinnabar, arsenolite, powdered cinnabar, and mercury.

To refine mother-cinnabar powder and "kill" one *liang* of sulfur: first moisten the cinnabar powder with saliva, wrap it around the sulfur, then take equal parts of black pepper, Sichuan pepper, and *Asarum* ground into powder. Scoop two or three *qian*, mix with vinegar to form cakes, layer them with clay, and apply five *jin* of charcoal fire to refine it. Alternatively, "kill" sulfur by stir-frying ten *liang* to form blue-gold, place it in a box, and calcine. When cool, grind it to powder to make an "immortality vessel" for nurturing all substances and golden cinnabar. This medicine is highly potent, with endless transformations.

For mercury extracted through nurturing: boil *Pinellia ternata* in wine to form a paste, shape into pills the size of mung beans, and take one pill on an empty stomach while facing east, swallowing it with cold water—this is called the *Lesser Return Elixir*. It cures all illnesses. Take one pill every three to five days, up to three or five pills, and one will remain free of disease for life.

**Method for Preparing the Great Elixir**
- Alum: four *liang*
- White alum: four *liang*
- Saltpeter: four *liang*

Add a small amount of binding medicine and boil until dry. Place in a large *Jian* bowl, set on an iron stand, add the three ingredients, and cover with another *Jian* bowl. Apply five *jin* of charcoal fire to refine it. When the medicine boils and settles, do not disturb the fire. Gradually reduce the heat, and when the bowl cools, remove the medicine—it will resemble rock crystal. Weigh it without loss, grind to a fine powder, and place in a cinnabar box. Then prepare the following:

- Realgar: two *liang*
- Orpiment: two *liang*
- Arsenic: two *liang*

Grind finely, mix with *Tetrastigma* root juice to form cakes, and place them around the cinnabar box. Seal with iron wire, then coat with a mixture of four *liang* of clay and six *liang* of salt. Dry in the sun, bury in ash, and apply one *liang* of charcoal fire on top, covering with ash. Replace the fire daily and nurture for forty-nine days. Remove the medicine cakes, add two *liang* of mercury, and grind finely. Mix again with *Tetrastigma* juice to form cakes, place in the cinnabar box, seal as before, and nurture with gentle fire for another forty-nine days. Repeat the process, adding two *liang* of mercury, grinding, mixing with *Tetrastigma* juice, forming cakes, sealing in the box, and nurturing for forty-nine days.

Grind the extracted substance finely into pills. For each use, take one *zi* of the powder to transmute five *liang* of mercury into treasure.

**Refining Cinnabar (White Cinnabar)**
Take cinnabar in any quantity, place it within lotus rhizome nodes, then seal externally with clay. Refine until red and remove.

**Washing Cinnabar in the Cinnabar Vessel**
Take four *liang* of fine cinnabar, one *liang* of *Euphorbia pekinensis*, two *qian* of lead frost, one *liang* of *Iris domestica*, and one *liang* of *Aconitum carmichaelii*. Grind these into powder, then boil with three *sheng* of mild vinegar in a suspended vessel for one full day and night. Remove and apply the following body-adhering medicine.

**Body-Adhering Medicine**
Grind three *qian* each of *pengxin* and alum into powder, then mix with refined honey to form the body-adhering medicine as follows.

For each grain of cinnabar, wrap it tightly in a silver sheet. Then take eight *liang* of silver mother, hammer it into fragmented cinnabar, and place it together with the cinnabar in a vessel, layering them repeatedly. Seal the top and bottom with *shengwuzhi*, then use water-mixed red halloysite to secure the seams. Nurture with fire for three days, then remove and subject it to the *tiandi* process.

Mix *xin*, alum, saltpeter, and clamshell powder evenly, then lightly refine. Next, take ten *baimei* fruits, grind them into a paste, and wrap the cinnabar grains. Place them in a crucible and refine until reduced to ash.

Then transfer to the *tianchi* vessel, adding five *wen* of alum, a small amount of *xin*, five *baimei* fruits, and five *wen* of white kaolin. Grind these finely, then wrap the cinnabar and lightly refine until cool. Remove, wash clean with hot water, and prepare the vessel. Pour one *liang* of mercury, nurture for three days, then collect half a *liang* of sprouts, which will transmute into white furnace treasure.

**Dead Body-Adhering Medicine**
Five *wen* of *Anemarrhena asphodeloides* and five *wen* of *Fritillaria cirrhosa*. Grind these finely, first fumigate the crucible until black, then heat the crucible until red-hot. Quickly add *shengwuzhi*, saltpeter, and alum into the pot to form a molten liquid. Fan rapidly, pour out, and grind into powder to make the body-adhering medicine. Nurture with fire for seven days, then subject to the *tianchi* process before proceeding to nurture mercury, wash, and extract treasure.

**Gradual Fire Nurturing**
First day: half a *liang*.
Second day: eight *qian*.
Third day: one *liang*.

**Gradual Fire Nurturing (continued)**
Fourth day: one *liang*.
Fifth and sixth days: one and a half *liang*.
Seventh day: two *liang*. Cease.
Thereafter, pour mercury and nurture with fire.
First day: in the morning, apply one *qian* of fire; in the evening, half a *qian*.
Second day: in the morning, apply seven *qian* of fire; in the evening, half a *qian*.
Third day: in the morning, apply one *liang* of fire; in the evening, half a *qian*.
On the fourth day, when fully matured, collect half a *liang* of white sprouts. The furnace yields treasure.

**Longevity Fire-Nurturing Mercury-Washing Cinnabar Vessel**
Refine eight *liang* of cinnabar into solid lumps. Wrap the cinnabar in raw silk and secure it tightly. Suspend it in rice vinegar and boil for one *fu* period. Add *shizhu* powder (i.e., *Alpinia officinarum*) to the vinegar and boil together. Remove the cinnabar and discard the silk.

**Dead Body-Adhering Medicine**
*Stellera chamaejasme* (Sichuan) and *Asarum sieboldii* (Taiwan), in equal parts. Grind into fine powder, mix with honey to form a paste, then coat each piece of boiled cinnabar. Allow to dry slightly.

**Vessel-Entry Method**
Use a sand box. Place *shizhu* powder inside, firmly tamp half full, then arrange the cinnabar pieces (coated as above) like lotus seeds within the powder. Cover with the remaining powder, tamp firmly, seal the lid, and secure the seams with red halloysite mixed with vinegar. Proceed to nurture with fire.

**Fire-Nurturing Method**
Place the box in an ash jar, covering it with two fingers’ thickness of paper ash.
First day: morning and evening, four *liang* of fire.
Second and third days: same.
Fourth day: morning and evening, six *liang* of fire.
Fifth day: same.
Sixth day: at dawn and dusk, seven *liang* of fire.
Seventh day: at dawn, four *liang* of fire.
By evening, lift the box and heat it with three *jin* of fire until red-hot. Allow to cool, then remove the cinnabar.

**Further Fire-Nurturing Method**
Eight *qian* of silver and eight *qian* of mercury. Combine the two to form cinnabar, wash clean, then grind finely with the cinnabar from earlier. Place in a box, seal the seams with red halloysite, and set in a paper ash jar. Nurture with fire as before until complete. Apply two *liang* of fire morning and evening, avoiding excessive heat. The next day, allow to cool and remove.

**Nurturing Mother Cinnabar Method**
Wash and refine *sanqi* mother cinnabar. Divide each *liang* into three cakes, secure with raw silk, then use *Akebia quinata* and *Anemarrhena asphodeloides* in equal parts, ground to powder. Add one cup of water, suspend the cakes, and boil with gentle and strong fire until dry. Remove, then wrap with *Lilium brownii* (sifted into balls). Seal entirely with salt clay, heat with intense fire until red-hot, then quench in water. Remove the cinnabar, place in a cinnabar vessel like lotus seeds, and nurture with fire as before for seven days. Remove and refine in the furnace to yield treasure.

**Immortal’s Repeated Refinement of Metal (Geng) Method**
One *qian* of *geng* and one *liang* of mercury. Place in half a cup of true sesame oil and boil over fire. Add one *Trichosanthes kirilowii* seed and simmer until the mixture turns yellow. Add another seed, repeating until seven seeds are used. Then gradually add six to seven *qian* of *Pistacia lentiscus* resin and simmer briefly. Remove and cool, then pour the mixture onto four or five layers of paper mulberry paper. Extract the *geng*, squeezing out the oil; the refined mercury will remain within. Repeat the process until all *geng* is exhausted. Wash the cinnabar in hot water until clean and lustrous.

**Vessel-Nurturing Method**
Split a black plum pit into two halves. Fill each half with *geng* cinnabar to resemble plum kernels, then remove the cinnabar. Moisten the pit halves with honey, then dust thoroughly inside and out with refined fire-nurtured cinnabar (ground extremely fine). Place the *geng* cinnabar inside, seal the pit halves, and bind with thread. Moisten the exterior with paper mulberry juice, then coat the seams with honey. Dust the edges with *Aconitum kusnezoffii* powder, then wrap the pit with four or five mashed black plum kernels. Coat the exterior with *Aconitum carmichaelii* powder mixed with vinegar, then seal with salt clay to a thickness of one finger. Allow to dry.

**Ash Jar Method**
Fill a jar with paper ash, place the medicine ball at the center, and cover with ash. Surround with embers and nurture overnight. The next day, remove the *geng* pit; the remaining medicine will have turned to ash.

**Further Sealing Method**
Mix *Placenta hominis* root powder with honey to form a paste, shaping it into balls the size of marbles. Place the *geng* pit inside, then wrap securely with silk. Coat the exterior with a mixture of *Asarum sieboldii*, *Aconitum carmichaelii*, *Lilium brownii*, and *Croton tiglium* (in equal parts, ground to powder and mixed with honey). Seal with salt clay to a thickness of one finger, allow to dry, then place in an ash jar. Surround with fire and nurture overnight before removing.

**Furnace-Refinement Method**
Three *qian* of halite, and half a *qian* each of *chalcanthite*, *yellow alum*, *gold-wrapped earth*, *alum red* (as substitute for cinnabar), *dead cinnabar*, *Gardenia jasminoides*, and *Trichosanthes kirilowii* seeds. Grind into powder, mix with vinegar to form a paste, and encase the *geng* within. Coat the exterior with *limonite* and *hematite* powder, then place in a crucible. Fan until smoke appears to yield treasure.

**Cinnabar Body-Adhering Method**
Place one *liang* of cinnabar in a *Jian* bowl, then cover with a thick layer (one finger’s depth) of *Zanthoxylum bungeanum* powder mixed with honey. Seal with another bowl. Secure the seams with red halloysite mixed with vinegar, then bind with iron wire. Coat the exterior of the bowl with a mixture of *Aconitum carmichaelii*, *Phellodendron amurense* bark, *Dioscorea bulbifera*, and *Dianthus superbus* spikes (in equal parts, ground to powder and mixed with vinegar) to a thickness of one finger. Use *qinglong* vessel (vinegar ash) to seal the top and bottom, leaving only the bowl’s base exposed. Place on the ground and heat with eight *jin* of fire until fully red-hot. Gradually reduce the fire, allow to cool, then remove for use.

**Cinnabar Refinement Method**
Take one *liang* of cinnabar, boil with *jichang* grass for one day and one night, retaining the grass residue, then dry by fanning. Use the following ingredients, each one and a half *liang*: *Arisaema erubescens*, *Scutellaria baicalensis*, *Angelica dahurica*, *Ampelopsis japonica*, *Dioscorea bulbifera*, *Polytrichum commune*, and *Pyrosia lingua*. Additionally, use one *liang* each of *Epimedium brevicornum* bark, *Dendrobium nobile*, and *Glycyrrhiza uralensis*. Take three *liang* of the pre-boiled grass residue, place together with the cinnabar in a sand box, seal the seams with honey-mixed red halloysite, then coat the exterior with salt clay to a thickness of one finger. Dry in the shade, then heat with five *jin* of fire until the charcoal is spent and the furnace cools.

**Cinnabar Leaching Method**
Take one *liang* of cinnabar and one *liang* of *sanqi* mother cinnabar. Wrap half in *nang* cinnabar, place in a *shizhonghuang* vessel, and nurture with three *jin* of fire for one *zha*. Remove the cinnabar, discard the adhering medicine, place in a crucible with one *liang* of mercury and one *qian* of cinnabar, cover with *Asarum sieboldii* powder, then heat to extract half a *liang* of cinnabar grains. Drive off the mercury oil, yielding one and a half *qian* of silver. Boil the cinnabar again with vinegar and alum, then refine and coagulate as before.

**Leaching Method (Alternative)**
Use one and a half *liang* of *sanqi* cinnabar to wrap one *liang* of cinnabar, place in a *shizhonghuang* vessel, and nurture with four *liang* of *maoyou* fire for seven days. Remove the mother cinnabar, then leach four *liang* of cinnabar with two *liang* of mercury, alternating between water and fire with four *liang* of *maoyou* fire for three to five days. Leach five times, then cease the fire without further leaching. Grind the leached cinnabar into a fine powder, place in a box, and use finely ground aged tea leaves as a vessel lining. Nurture for seven days with four *liang* of fire. When the time is complete, remove, wash with water, and dry by baking. For every four *liang* of powder, nurture one *liang* of cinnabar for seven days. Remove the powder, adhere *qiuyuan* mother cinnabar to the cinnabar, place in a vessel to nurture, then extract silver. Take the nurtured cinnabar and leach five times as before. Repeat this process, alternating up to seven times, and the efficacy will grow ever stronger.

**Medicinal Calcination Method**
Use *huangdan* calcined to a molten state, place in a pot, and collect the finest powder from the furnace front.

**Cinnabar Leaching Method (Variant)**
Take four *liang* of cinnabar and five *liang* of silver, cut into dice-like blocks, and mix evenly. Boil together with *duanchang* grass juice and *diwugong* juice for three days. Remove the cinnabar and silver, place in a box, and nurture for seven days with four *liang* of *maoyou* fire. Then leach with two *liang* of mercury, following the previous fire regimen. Leach again with two *liang*, and by the third leaching, remove the silver. Cease after five leachings, then boil and leach to achieve the "Longevity" transformation.

**Monolithic Cinnabar**
Take one *jin* of sulfur, cut into dice-like blocks. Place in a silk pouch and suspend in a vessel. Add half a *jin* each of *tianzi* grass and *chuanyin yasheshe* grass (found by the water’s edge). Boil the two ingredients in eight *sheng* of river water, reducing to five *sheng*, then add the sulfur and boil for one day and one night. Remove, dry, and grind into powder. For each *liang* of cinnabar, cover with half a *liang* of the powder, place in a bowl, and seal with another bowl. Place three large charcoal pieces beneath the bowl and nurture for seven days. If the sulfur rises to the upper bowl, scrape it down and cover again. After seven days, remove the cinnabar from the bowl and leach with two *liang* of mercury. Cover again with sulfur, nurture for seven days, then leach with two *liang* of mercury once more, sealing the upper and lower bowls as before. After seven days, remove the cinnabar, wash clean with *Gleditsia sinensis* water, place in a box, seal the seams, and nurture with four *liang* of *maoyou* fire for seven days per leaching. When the powder matures, gradually collect the fumes.

**Monolithic Cinnabar (Verified Family Transmission by Xue Zili)**
Take ten *liang* of *shanze* mother, shape into beads. Use four *liang* of large-grained cinnabar, boil with the natural juice of chopped *Phytolacca acinosa* root for three days and nights. Remove, bathe in jujube decoction. Then boil *pengsha* with *Arisaema erubescens* and *Aconitum carmichaelii* for one day, remove, dry, and grind into a fine powder for adhesion. Drain the boiled cinnabar, dry with *peng* powder, and apply as an adherent layer. Once dry, line the bottom of the vessel with a layer of mother beads, then place the cinnabar in lotus-like arrangement within the beads. Add another layer of mother beads, then more cinnabar, and cover with mother beads. Seal, place in an ash jar, and nurture with two *liang* of *maoyou* fire for fourteen days. The extracted cinnabar will appear bluish-white; when blown in the fire, it forms beads, and the cinnabar is thus inverted. To strengthen the vessel’s potency, use more mother beads. Generally, nurture one *liang* of cinnabar with two and a half *liang* of beads—this is the first transformation. Take the inverted cinnabar from the previous nurturing, grind it, and place in a box. For every four *liang*, nurture one *liang* of pre-boiled cinnabar, adhering the medicine as before. It can be inverted in nine days. Remove and test by blowing into beads as before. Eight *liang* of beads make the best vessel—this is the second transformation. Take four or eight *liang* of second-transformation inverted cinnabar as the vessel head. Boil fresh cinnabar with *Phytolacca acinosa* for three or five days. Encase the cinnabar tightly within the grass residue, then coat the exterior with paper-fiber salt clay. Dry in the shade, surround with warm ash on the ground, and calcine with two *jin* of charcoal. When six-tenths of the charcoal is spent, cover with paper ash to retain the red fire, allowing it to cool naturally. Remove when the furnace is cold; the cinnabar will appear bluish, no longer red. Then coat with honey-mixed *peng* powder as an adherent layer, place in the second-transformation vessel, arrange in lotus formation, seal as before, and nurture for seven days with fire.

On the first, second, and third days, apply one and a half *liang* of fire. From the fourth day to the seventh, use two *liang* of fire. Once the furnace has fully cooled, remove and test the beads by blowing as before. With this most potent third-transformation cinnabar, every two and a half *qian* can transmute one *liang* of base metals into supreme treasure.

**Secret Transmission: Non-Detaching Yang-Hour Vessel for Nurturing the Sun-Moon Elixir Head**
This method employs one *jin* of aged sulfur, ground to powder. First, boil *Galla chinensis* for one *fu*-period, then strain off the residue. Next, replace with a concentrated decoction of *Scutellaria baicalensis*, *Coptis chinensis*, and *Rheum palmatum*, boiling for a full two days. Then, fumigate a box with *Galla chinensis*, first coating the interior with egg-white solution once, then fumigating thickly, and applying two more coats. Use this sulfur to nurture in vacuity for seven days; it will emerge resembling yellow gold in hue. Employing this method to further nurture yields the numinous sacred vessel. When nurturing the Two-Yellow Elixir Head, success is achieved in two seven-day cycles with wondrous efficacy.

**Subduing the Azure Dragon Treasure Vessel**
This is the method for subduing sulfur. The sagely Azure Gold Mother Cinnabar transforms through the *geng*-pathway, its marvels boundless. To nurture *fen shuang* and obtain the Azure Dragon: pound the true juice, boil sulfur for three *fu*-periods, place in a box with black paper as a divider, and seal the top with a paste cake of *chi shi zhi* and bittern. Add a layer of White Tiger, seal tightly, and bind. First nurture for seven days, then bury in an earthen pit and steam with *nie*. Upon removal, it becomes truly dead.

This *geng*-vessel transmutes cinnabar within, yielding elixir heads for medicinal use. When refined alone, it produces solitary yang; when combined with beads, it forms elixir heads. Its transformations are manifold. This vessel nurtures elixir heads without altering their innate hue. For instance, when nurturing Azure Gold, take ten *liang* of the medicine as the base. First extract two *liang* of green vitriol and two *liang* of Two-Eight Mother Cinnabar, kill them together, and consolidate into one body. Pack this firmly at the bottom of the box, then add the remaining eight *liang* of Azure Gold to cover. Seal and refine for seven days, then remove. Repeat the process: combine two *liang* of Two-Eight Mother Cinnabar with the previous eight *liang*, add two *liang* of Azure Gold, grind together, pack at the box’s base, and cover with six *liang* of Azure Gold. Nurture for another seven days, then remove, reserving six *liang* of Azure Gold treasure. At this stage, the original four *liang* of treasure are ground to powder and mixed with the six *liang* of Azure Gold to form a vessel, totaling fourteen *liang*. Transformations proceed at will; follow the method and accumulate through repeated cycles, for abundance ensures superiority. Proceed according to capacity—none shall fail to attain numinosity.

If one seeks to kill mercury, mercury must first be killed. The vessel’s uses are sixfold:
1. Nurturing cinnabar,
2. Stir-frying *jin gong* into a body,
3. Transmuting substances,
4. Separating treasures for manifestation,
5. Applying cinnabar mother as an adherent layer,
6. Sprinkling to cover the cinnabar’s surface.

This method pertains to subduing and refining Azure Gold Elixir Heads, with wondrous transformations in its latter stages.

**Another Method for Killing Sulfur**
Take ten *liang* of sulfur, boil with the natural juice of lotus root and radish for one *fu*-period. Then wrap the boiled sulfur in the residue of lotus root and radish, place in a cinnabar box, seal tightly, and secure with salt-clay pellets. Set upon the ground and steam with thirty *jin* of fire. Once the furnace cools, use it as a vessel to nurture Mother Cinnabar and the Two Yellows.

**Refining Sulfur**
Grind sulfur of any quantity finely, then pound with *Houttuynia cordata* and spinach to extract two large bowls of juice. Boil the sulfur in an iron pan for a day and night until the juice evaporates and the sulfur is subdued.

**Killing Sulfur**
Grind four *liang* of sulfur to powder. In an iron pan, boil with the decoction of *Dioscorea bulbifera* for about one day. Transfer to an amber jar: first coat the interior and lid with honey, then add *Ephedra* nodes and roots, place over fire, and burn until the smoke subsides and turns to ash; blow the ash away. Repeat with fresh roots and nodes two or three more times until the smoke ceases. Place the sulfur in the jar, seal the seams, bury in an ash pit, and nurture for three days. The sulfur will invert, becoming suitable as a vessel to nurture *geng*-cinnabar, numinous cinnabar, mother cinnabar, and the Three Yellows for transmutative medicine.

To nurture the Three Yellows, first employ the latter method: gather ample *Euphorbia lunulata* and *Marsilea quadrifolia*, pound to extract juice, and boil the Three Yellows. When the juice turns black, discard it and replace with fresh juice, repeating until the juice remains clear. Then place in a sulfur vessel to nurture; later transmutations will not darken.

**Steaming Method to Kill Sulfur for Vessels**
Pound *Cayratia japonica* and *Pteris multifida* together to extract juice, then boil sulfur. Later, wrap the sulfur in *Broussonetia* fiber, coat externally with salt-paper-fiber clay, dry, place on the ground, and steam with intense fire to kill instantly.

**Method for Boiling Sulfur to Invert Azure Gold**
Take sulfur of any quantity, decoct *Dioscorea bulbifera* in water, and drizzle the juice into a pan to stir-fry the sulfur. When the sulfur is half-dead, add mercury and stir-fry together for one *shi*-period; the Azure Gold will invert immediately. Alternatively, grind realgar, green vitriol, saltpeter, and lead frost together, invert the Azure Gold, heat a crucible until red, and collect the resulting liquid as treasure. Another method: use only raw saltpeter and Azure Gold, pack tightly into a crucible, pierce a small hole in the center, insert a *Polyporus umbellatus* stalk, steam, and collect *shao fen* and lead from the crucible’s bottom, using borax powder for the furnace—this yields great efficacy.

**Method for Killing Sulfur to Make Vessels**
Take sulfur of any quantity, pound *Rumex japonicus* root to extract juice, and boil the sulfur for one *fu*-period. Wrap the sulfur in the *Rumex* residue, seal externally with salt-clay, dry, and steam with fire to achieve true death.

**Another Method for Killing Sulfur**
Boil sulfur with winter melon juice and a small amount of glutinous rice for three days, then nurture for one seven-day cycle. Upon removal, it will resemble purple gold in color.

**Further Refinement of Sulfur**
Steam again, then nurture for two seven-day cycles until the original color is restored, and test by ceasing the fire.

**Secret Transmission: Methods for Subduing, Nurturing, and Refining Solitary Powder for Wondrous Alchemical Use**
Place within the former Azure Dragon sulfur vessel for nurturing.

Shape *fen shuang* (calomel) into small dice-like blocks weighing five *liang*. Boil with *Rheum palmatum* (rhubarb), *Galla chinensis* (Chinese gall), *Gardenia jasminoides* (cape jasmine), *Zanthoxylum bungeanum* (Sichuan pepper), *Asarum* branches, ginger juice, honey, and thick rice vinegar in river water for one *fu*-period until blackened—this is the standard. Once dry, place into a Yao vessel, then sprinkle five *qian* of raw sulfur powder and stir-fry gently until properly aged and dried as before. The original weight of five *liang* and one *qian* or more confirms success. This powder may then be applied to the essence of cinnabar ore. For every *liang* of stir-fried powder, add one *qian* of mother flakes, layer upon layer, binding them into a ball. Externally, apply two *qian* of white lime powder and one *fen* of *Alpinia oxyphylla* (black cardamom) powder as a protective coating. Then introduce to cinnabar sulfur within the former Azure Dragon vessel, nurture for two seven-day cycles, and retrieve as an alchemical treasure. If smoke appears during firing, nurture for an additional seven days—this yields wondrous transmutation.

**Secret Transmission: Mother Vessel for Nurturing Cinnabar Without Absorption**
This method is wondrous in application. For instance, take ten *liang* of true mother essence as the base and first melt it into a liquid. Then add five *liang* of pure lead to the mother solution, stirring left and right to blend evenly. Sweep into small pearl-like granules, then nurture and boil five *liang* of *ling sha* (spirit cinnabar) within this mother vessel. Arrange in a lotus pattern, and success will be achieved in seven days. Upon retrieval, each granule will be truly dead, assuming a crow-black hue. When burned over fire, they should form silver pearls as the standard. After destruction and nurturing, the alchemical treasure emerges, and the sacred embryo is separated.

A poem reads:
*On a fine night, three lone stars revolve,*
*Shattering the sweet crucible to reveal jade skin.*

This method divides the medicine to stand as the foremost under heaven—guard it closely and never reveal it to others.

First, use true iron slurry to refine saltpeter, stir-frying until dry, and set aside. For each *liang* of *ling sha*, first grind the cinnabar into powder, then add two *qian* of subdued saltpeter. Pack tightly at the crucible’s bottom, then place two *liang* of silver toad (silver) as a pressing weight on top. Expose to an open-air furnace, applying intense fire until thoroughly red-hot for a full period. Only then gently fan with a bellows. If the contents melt completely into a clear, limpid liquid, remove the crucible. The surface should be free of cicada-like pores or cavities, its color a scorched yellow—this confirms extraordinary efficacy. Among ten thousand methods, none surpass this. Guard it well.

**Subduing and Refining: First Extract Blood Paste, Then Purify to Form the Body’s Essence**
By this method, place the red dragon (mercury) into a crucible and add one *fen* of aged earth medicine, three *fen* each of edible salt, *lu gan shi* (calamine), and northern saltpeter. Combine thoroughly, seal the top tightly, and fire once in a vigorous furnace. After firing, break the crucible to retrieve the red blood. Place it into a new crucible, layering with borax powder and equal parts raw saltpeter and raw salt, filling to the brim. Once melted into a liquid, remove and gently tap to separate the embryo below, which will appear as a tender, delicate hue.

For the next step, melt pure material and add two *qian* of small elixir seeds, nurturing to produce tile sprouts. Secretly add half a *qian* of raw arsenic powder, then pour over the cinnabar. Press into the liquid, and apply coatings of black soybean decoction, fermented grain wash, and *Asparagus cochinchinensis* (heavenly winter) decoction—each in equal measure. After two applications and transformations, add a small amount of saltpeter, sweeping into powdered pearls for later use.

This method first nurtures and refines the elixir seed through prolonged firing, accumulating sufficient yang-blackness. Only then does the elixir’s transmutation succeed, termed *dan yang* (cinnabar yang), the pure yang. Later, this pure yang medicine is used to transmute pure yin—namely, the red dragon. Nowadays, those who pursue the Dao lack enlightened masters and clumsy disciples, content with fleeting, easily obtained medicines. How can such treasures possess a thousand years of qi? This follows the darkness of heaven and earth’s four seasons, employing herbs, woods, metals, and minerals to achieve success.

The seven stages are:
1. Vastness
2. Great Elder
3. Crimson Flesh
4. Staff
5. Bone
6. Transmuting Thatch
7. Cinnabar Yang Bone Replacement

**Method for Refining Arsenic Powder and Calomel for Transmutation**
Take equal parts arsenic powder, calomel, *Ricinus communis* (castor bean), and *Croton tiglium* (croton), pound into a paste, and adjust the quantity as needed. Place into a water-and-fire vessel and strike—it will instantly die for any use.

**Refining Arsenic to Transmute Staffs**
Grind one *liang* each of arsenic and *Melia toosendan* (Sichuan chinaberry) powder evenly, place into a crucible, and cover with a water bowl. Boil until the water evaporates completely. Upon cooling, retrieve the arsenic, which will have sublimated onto the bowl’s bottom like a snow mountain. Use one to two *qian* of this arsenic to transmute staffs into snow-white mother essence, combining to form treasure.

**Arsenic Vessel for Transmuting Cinnabar Yang**
Take two *liang* of calomel and eight *liang* of bright arsenic. Shape each into small blocks, place into silk bags, and boil with *Rumex japonicus* root and leaves, along with fresh ginger, extracting their natural juices. If the juice is insufficient, add several bowls of water. Boil for three *fu*-periods, then sun-dry the residue. First retrieve the boiled calomel, then wrap it in a silk cotton ball. Next, grind the eight *liang* of arsenic into powder and layer it on top, also wrapping in a silk cloth ball. Protect externally with the former residue, place into a sealed vessel, and steam with three *jin* of fire until thoroughly heated. Upon cooling, grind the arsenic milk into a vessel. Then divide the calomel into four blocks, wrap tightly in silver foil, seal with lotus petals, and place into an ash pool. Fire with two *liang* of heat morning and evening, nurturing for fourteen days. Retrieve, and for every two *qian* of powder, transmute one *liang* of cinnabar yang using arsenic as the vessel.

**Steaming Calomel to Transmute Cinnabar Yang**
Grind one *liang* of calomel finely, wrap in two layers of silk cloth, and place with one hundred shelled *Croton tiglium* and *Ricinus communis* seeds each.

**Further Processing with Fresh Ginger**
Take one *jin* of fresh ginger, pound to extract the juice, and let settle. Reserve the ginger residue for separate use. Combine with the two previous medicines, suspend in a "womb" vessel, and boil the calomel until the liquid fully evaporates. Retrieve the calomel and grind finely again. Then mix the ginger residue with the calomel to form pills, wrap in *Kunlun* paper, and pound the previously boiled *Croton tiglium* and *Ricinus communis* into a paste. Apply a layer of this paste, then coat externally with an equal-part mixture of saltpeter, salt, alum, and oyster shell powder, ground into a paste. If the paste does not hold, add a small amount of sour rice vinegar and pound again into a paste. Apply another layer, briefly pass over ash fire, and dry in the sun. When shaken, the pills should rattle loosely. Place on the ground with bricks arranged beneath, and calcine with five *jin* of fire. Retrieve after the furnace cools, yielding only six *qian* of true "dead" powder. For each *qian* used, melt seven *qian* of base metal, and transmute it into pure white silver. Adding three *qian* of silver and refining together yields *hua* silver.

**Jade-Ring Arsenic Method**
Grind four *liang* of arsenic into powder, place in a crucible, and cover the mouth with two layers of hemp cloth, securing tightly with thread. Set the crucible over fire and calcine. Frequently sprinkle fresh ginger juice onto the cloth to keep it moist. Over time, the arsenic will form jade-ring-like crystals at the crucible’s mouth. Retrieve and use to transmute *he* into treasure. First, burn silkworm-eaten mulberry leaves, twigs, and stems into ash, then stir-fry the *he* until clean. Transmute with arsenic, then alloy with base metal to form treasure, suitable only for crafting vessels.

**Arsenic-Nurtured Calomel to Transmute Cinnabar Yang as a Vessel**
Grind one *jin* of arsenic finely and place in a large jar. Take *Ricinus communis* stems and leaves (excluding seeds), pound to extract two large bowls of juice, and boil the arsenic until the liquid fully evaporates. Then calcine with three *jin* of intense fire, rendering the arsenic truly "dead." Retrieve only twelve *liang* to serve as a vessel for nurturing calomel. Take four *liang* of calomel, selecting uniformly sized granules. Soak sliced turmeric in wine lees until soft, wrap each piece of calomel, then secure with fine iron wire. Place into the former arsenic vessel and nurture day and night with one *jin* of fire for three days. Upon cooling and opening, the calomel will be "dead," its color like dark indigo. For every two *qian* used, transmute one *liang* of base metal into supreme treasure.

**Dead Calomel Method**
Grind any amount of calomel finely. Mix with wood honey to form pills, place into a *kuzhang* tube, and seal the mouth with *kuzhang*. Grind *kuzhang* leaves into powder, mix with wood honey to form a paste, and coat the tube. If the leaves dry, use wood honey to adjust the paste; if fresh, simply pound into a paste and apply. Place into a "dead" saltpeter vessel and nurture until "dead." Suitable for transmuting base metal or *shimengsha*, yielding a soft, pure white, and exquisite product. When alloyed with silver in a 3:7 ratio, it becomes perfect treasure. Nurture "dead" saltpeter as follows: Place two *liang* of saltpeter into a crucible and heat until molten. Add a one-*cun* piece of *duya* soapberry and a small lump of tallow soap into the molten saltpeter, allowing the mixture to boil over them. Repeat this process five times. Once the saltpeter stabilizes, apply intense fire for one calcination, yielding truly "dead" saltpeter powder in the crucible. If the fire is insufficient, the saltpeter will solidify like a jar of jade; place in a box and nurture with fire for two days to loosen it into a vessel. Use to nurture the aforementioned calomel to immediate "death" for transmutation. When nurturing *sanshi* mother cinnabar, ensure proper alignment, though it is inferior to nurturing calomel for transmuting cinnabar yang.

**Dead Arsenic Method**
Extract juice from *mao’er yanjing* grass and *tie jiao poluomen* grass, boil arsenic with it, then wrap the arsenic in a grass residue ball. Seal externally with *guan* mud and dry. Dig a pit, place the ball inside, burying half with ash, and calcine with five *jin* of charcoal. Once the charcoal slightly diminishes, add three *jin*, then later two *jin*, for a total calcination. Retrieve after the furnace cools, yielding truly "dead" arsenic.

**Cinnabar Yang Arsenic Formula**
Grind four *liang* of arsenic and four *qian* of frankincense together evenly. Pound scallions to extract juice, mix to a suitable consistency, and place in a *jian* bowl. Burn *lamu* vine into ash, spread thickly over the arsenic, and set over fire to calcine. When white smoke rises, add more *lamu* vine ash to the smoking area until the bowl turns red. After cooling, remove the ash and retrieve the arsenic. For each *qian* of silver foil, use one *qian* of arsenic, melt in a base metal crucible, and add red charcoal fire to the molten mixture. The result will be soft and pure white, highly desirable.

**Dead Calomel**
Grind one *liang* of calomel finely, mix with fresh ginger juice to form a paste, wrap in new silk cloth into a ball, and secure tightly with thread, removing the stem. Melt four *liang* of raw honey and two *liang* of white rosin together, add the calomel ball, and stir-fry over fire until the honey and rosin dry. Place in a box, seal the seams, and nurture with slow fire overnight. If the calomel has not yet inverted, nurture for three more days. Once the calomel melts into liquid or fully inverts, burn over fire until no smoke remains—it is then "dead" and ready for transmutation.

**Dead Arsenic Method**
Burn dried *kuzhang* into ash, use any amount, and boil arsenic in the ash-infused water for a day to invert it—this is the most excellent method.

**Golden Crucible Arsenic-Nurtured Divine Elixir True Death Method**
Afterward, add alum and calcine again for best results. Grind four *liang* of arsenic and four *liang* of alum into powder. Melt four *liang* of lead into liquid, stir-fry with paper ash to form granules, wash clean with water, and dry. Mix evenly with the arsenic and alum. First, heat a crucible until red-hot, then add the mixture. Once the arsenic melts, apply intense fire for a long duration. The arsenic will be truly "dead," resembling orpiment in color.

The lead will naturally settle beneath the arsenic. Remove the arsenic, grind it finely, and use one *liang* of mercury, three *qian* of cinnabar mother, and two *qian* of raw sulfur. First, congeal the mercury mother into cinnabar sand, then add the sulfur, and stir-fry with one *qian* of dead arsenic. Add another two *qian* of arsenic, cover the crucible, and apply fire. The divine cinnabar will melt below and invert, though it will be black in color. Reheat it in a lead pool, and it will instantly become a pure white treasure. Alternatively, use the dead arsenic to form a chamber and nurture it with cinnabar mother or two *liang* of cinnabar mother foil. Fire-nurture it for seven days, then remove and refine it to instantly form a treasure.

**End of *Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Five**
**Beginning of *Gengdao Ji*, Scroll Six**

**Dan Yang Techniques**
*Transmission of Master Shen of Guangde, from Daoist Zhang of Huating*

**First: Method for Refining Copper Strips**
Prepare fifty *wen* of copper coins—select the finest—and place them in a crucible to melt into liquid. Next, add refined alum, using a tile to stir with a fingertip until the liquid becomes clear and lustrous. First, boil two bowls of sour *dong* juice with one cup of persimmon lacquer until scalding hot, then pour into a flat tub. Place a brick at the center, ensuring the liquid does not overflow its surface. Gradually pour the copper liquid onto the brick, allowing it to flow naturally into the water—it will then be pure, soft, and refined.

**Second: Method for Refining Alum**
Grind two *liang* of fine, bright alum into powder, mix with two *qian* of sour grass powder, and blend evenly. Once the copper strips are melted into liquid, gradually add the alum mixture, stirring with a tile fingertip until the liquid becomes clear and lustrous. Pour it into the aforementioned tub onto the brick.

**Third: Method for Refining Arsenic Powder**
Grind two *liang* of arsenic with one *liang* of powdery frost, then mix with one *liang* of *zhimu* powder and grind evenly. Place in a water-and-fire vessel and process with three *jin* of water, measured precisely, until the water is exhausted. If powdery frost is unavailable, use one *liang* of mercury instead, grinding it with the arsenic medicine until no specks remain. Process with water, using four *jin* precisely, until exhausted. Each *qian* of this powder can refine one *liang* of the aforementioned copper strips, rendering them soft, white, and free of black haze. Then, add one *liang* of silver, melt together in a bright trough, and pour to cast ingots.

**Fourth: Method for Making Powdery Frost**
For every one *liang* of mercury, use approximately three *qian* each of alum and table salt, with a small amount of red *jiaojiao*. Grind together, place in a crucible, and fill it halfway. Seal the mouth with a tile cover, securing it properly. Dig a pit in the ground, tamp it firmly, and fill with water. Place the crucible upside-down in the pit, ensuring the water level is about one *cun* below the crucible. Pack soil tightly around the crucible’s exterior, then apply a cluster of fire until the ground becomes scorching hot. Once cooled, the frost will have formed and is ready for use.

**Method for Congealing and Calcining Powdery Frost: Dan Yang Bone-Transforming Technique**
- Five *liang* of mercury
- Two *liang* of arsenic
- Five *liang* of salt
- Three *liang* of calcined alum
- Three *liang* of sal nitre

First, heat and grind the calcined alum until hot, then gradually add the arsenic, grinding finely. Incorporate the mercury, salt, and sal nitre, grinding until no specks remain. While still hot, scoop the mixture into a crucible, spreading it evenly and loosely. Cover the mouth with a tile lid, then brush the lid’s underside three to five times with a thick mixture of ginger and ink, allowing it to dry. Seal the crucible’s mouth with finely ground red halloysite and nameless powder, mixed with brine and kneaded into a paste, applying a ten-finger-thick layer to the crucible’s exterior. Construct a celestial plate as in the method for ascending divine cinnabar. Begin with gentle fire, gradually increasing intensity. When the lid’s interior bubbles and boils, the medicine has ascended. Apply stronger fire for a long duration, then cease. Once cooled, collect the medicine from the lid’s underside, forming it into lumps. Wrap in silk, then boil with a mixture of sheep’s hoof root and its sprouts, extracting the pure juice. Bring to a boil once, then cool and clarify. Pour the clear liquid into a vat, suspend the wrapped medicine within, and boil for three full days. Remove, then grind the previously used alum, sal nitre, and salt on an iron grinding wheel until fine. Recalcine for two days, then cool and collect the medicine from the lid. Crush it as before, then boil again in the pure single-medicine juice for three full days. Remove, and for every one *liang* of pure bone, use two *qian* of this medicine to refine it—it will become snow-white.

**Method for Extracting Bone**
Once the copper strips are melted into liquid, add dead arsenic, white alum, calamine, and dead sal nitre, all ground evenly, and stir into the copper liquid until it boils like a mirror. Ensure no cloudiness remains; if it reappears, add more and stir again. Use a new tile to draw out the red "blood," and continue until the mirror-like surface is clear and cloud-free. For every one *liang* of red-hot copper, refine five to six *qian* for best results.

**Method for Dead Arsenic**
Take bright arsenic, first split into lumps, wrap in a silk bag, and suspend in a sand pot. Boil with a thick decoction of *jiegeng* for three full days to render it dead.

**Method for Dead Sal Nitre**
Use any amount of sal nitre. Fumigate a pot with five *liang* each of *fangfeng* and *fangji*, then add the sal nitre and melt into liquid. Toss in *duya* soapberry seeds—if the sal nitre ceases to swirl, it is dead. If it still swirls, continue heating with the medicine until the copper strips become soft as cotton.

**Method for Bone-Dissolving Paste**
Use one *liang* each of *duzhi*, dog fat, and sesame flowers. Place in a sand pot and gently heat until it forms a paste. This paste can dissolve bone into liquid to extract blood. Once thoroughly cleaned, scoop this oily medicine into an iron trough, pour the copper liquid into it, and soak two to three times—it will become soft as cotton, then ready for transmutation with the elixir head.

**Four Whites Head: Dan Yang Method**
- One part *peng*
- Two parts *liu*
- Three parts arsenic
- Four parts powdery frost

Grind into fine powder. First, place a stalk of purple grass in a bottle, then add the medicine powder to fill the bottle. Seal the mouth with a tile lid, bind with iron wire, and seal the seams with red halloysite. Dry with a mixture of sheep’s hoof root and mud. Apply three rounds of fire, allowing it to cool in the shade. Increase the fire to three *jin* for calcination. One *qian* of this medicine can refine one *liang*, turning it snow-white. First extract the blood, remove the black haze, then proceed with transmutation.

**Blood-Extracting Medicine Stick**
Take ten *liang* of the stick. First, mix with one *jin* of raw water chestnuts and pound together a thousand times, then remove and place in a crucible. Melt into liquid, then stir to form beads. Next, add a small amount of raw salt and a pinch of white kaolin powder, blending evenly with brine until moist. Place in the crucible and melt freely until reddened by the fire. Remove, wash clean, then return to the crucible to boil into liquid. A red oil will form on the surface, with clear water beneath. Skim off the oil scum, pour into a brush-water solution to form beads, then use the black-removing medicine to stir and eliminate the black residue.

**Eastern Mountain Mugwort, Dao-Subduing Mugwort, Goldthread Vine Juice.**

**Four Whites Head for Nurturing White Sand**
Arsenic, powdery frost, *peng*, *liu*, and cinnabar. To nurture one *liang* of powdered silver, use this to transmute twenty-four *liang* as the treasure.

**Cinnabar Method**
Equal parts of *daji*, *langhua*, and *yuanzhi*. Take one *liang* of cinnabar—select solid pieces with well-formed walls. Grind the herbs into coarse powder and stir-fry with the cinnabar. First, boil three *liang* of the herbs and cook for one full day and night. Then, stir-fry the cinnabar with the same herbs until scorched, blow off the ash, and stir-fry again. Repeat three times, then remove. Grind the cinnabar finely, mix with honey into a single mass, wrap in silk, press flat, and place in a box. Line the bottom with the Four Whites Head nurturing medicine, place the cinnabar in the center, and cover with more nurturing medicine. Seal the box tightly, place in an ash jar, and nurture with two *liang* of fire at the top, keeping the sides slightly distant. Nurture for one full day and night, then remove and grind finely. Add five *qian* of silver mother, and nurture again for one full day and night following the previous method. Remove and grind finely. Next, melt fine flower silver in a crucible, pour into a mold to form a solid block, then roll in honey and place in the box atop the silver. Sprinkle the previously nurtured cinnabar over it, seal tightly, and return to the ash jar. Nurture with three *liang* of fire at the top, keeping the sides slightly kindled, for one full day and night. Remove, peel off the treasure, mix with one *liang* of powdery frost, and place in an arsenic nurturing jar within the ash jar. Nurture with fire for five to seven days, using one day as the standard. Remove and proceed with transmutation.

**Boiling Medicine for Nurturing the Elixir Head**
*Heche*, Sichuan pepper, ginger juice, *diding*, lotus root juice.

**Method for Refining Arsenic Powder into Cinnabar-Yang**

Combine equal parts of arsenic powder and frost powder, place in a water-fire crucible, and refine by sublimation. Then add to the boiled medicine.

Take seven *jin* of undamaged soap beans, burn to ash—avoid over-burning, retain their nature. Steep in five *sheng* of fine vinegar, boil and strain five times. Then crush the soap beans, soak in five *sheng* of fine vinegar for two hours, knead and filter the dregs, and combine with the previous ash liquid. Suspend and boil for three days. Return to the crucible for sublimation, gradually increasing the heat until midnight. Remove the crucible when cool. Suspend again using *wutong* wood ash as the womb, and refine once more. After sublimation, grind finely and refine again. The residue at the bottom or the ring formation serves as verification. Take one *qian* to transmute one *liang* of snow-white silver.

**Method for Stir-Frying Frost Powder**

Use equal parts of *fozuo* grass, poppy grass, *gujing*, *shangu*, *diyu*, *husuntou* grass, and *guiyu*. Grind into powder, mix evenly with mulberry ash liquid and lotus root juice, set aside half, and boil the remaining small portion for one full day and night. Remove and wrap in silver foil.

Then combine the remaining medicine with lotus root juice and mulberry ash liquid, wrap the silver foil-covered frost powder within, and bind tightly with silk cloth. For external sealing medicine: grind *daji*, *shanglu*, *weilingxian*, rhubarb, and *huanglian* into powder, mix with lotus root and mulberry ash liquid to form cakes, and wrap around the bundle. Fry until charred, replace several times, then place in a crucible. Layer with boiled herbal medicine, cover with *huangdan*, litharge powder, and refined saltpeter, ground finely. Mix with lotus root juice, mulberry ash liquid, and rhubarb to form cakes, seal tightly, and calcine into a solid mass. Crush for use.

**Method for Subliming Arsenic, Cinnabar, Frost Powder, and Sal Ammoniac for Transmutation**

Wrap one *liang* of frost powder, half a *qian* of arsenic, half a *liang* of cinnabar, and two *qian* of sal ammoniac tightly in silk cloth. Boil in scallion and ginger juice diluted with water for one night. Remove, dry, and place in the crucible.

Crucible medicine: *difuzi*, pinellia, fritillaria, scutellaria, *caowu*, *juanwu*, and *huixian*. Grind into powder, mix with the previous medicine, place in the crucible, and cover with additional medicine. Seal the seams and dry. Refine in the water-fire crucible for transmutation into snow-white silver.

**Master Ge’s Method for Seeing the Treasure Arsenic**

Use Sichuan pepper, *cangmu*, *chuanlang*, *duchuan*, *lianzi*, *shiwei*, and purple-backed *huer*. Grind ten *liang* of arsenic into powder, mix evenly, and place in a clay pot. Refine in a water crucible with one cup of water until boiling vigorously. When the fire subsides, remove the next day—it will resemble silver, suitable for making crucibles and ready for transmutation.

Grind the previous ten *liang* of arsenic into fine powder, wrap with four *liang* of frost powder in silver foil, place in a sealed container, and nurture with fire for three days. Apply three *liang* of fire at dawn and dusk each day. After the full period, remove—it is now ready for transmutation.

Melt one *liang* of *rongzhangzi*. First use high-quality arsenic the size of a soybean to open the surface, then apply one *qian* of dead powder for wondrous effect. If not using dead powder for transmutation, nurture cinnabar in a dead powder crucible, with cinnabar placed in a western-facing container against the body. Nurture for seven days—it will be ready for transmutation. If not using a dead arsenic crucible for transmutation, nurture realgar in a dead arsenic crucible, also with a western-facing container against the body. Nurture for seven days—it will transmute metal. Alternatively, nurture mother cinnabar with dead powder for fourteen days to form treasure. If nurturing mother cinnabar with dead arsenic, seven days suffice to form treasure.

**Method for Refining Arsenic Powder to Transmute Bone into Bone-Head Crucible for Nurturing Divine Cinnabar**

Use six *liang* of frost powder and four *liang* of arsenic. Grind equal parts of *difuzi*, *cheqianzi*, Chinese gall, *baifuzi*, leek seeds, Sichuan *lianzi*, pine nuts, *hezi*, and *chushizi* into coarse powder. Place the arsenic powder in an iron pan, boil in flowing water for one day, then stir-fry until dry. Refine in a water crucible with fifteen *jin* of charcoal for one day. Remove when the furnace cools, repeat the process the next day, and refine again for one day. Use one *qian* to transmute one *liang* of bone.

Crush the bone to make a mother crucible. For each *jin* of bone, nurture four *liang* of divine cinnabar. Apply two *liang* of fire at the top, nurture for three days, then increase to four *liang* of fire for another four days. Remove when the furnace cools, discard the mother, and place the divine cinnabar in a crucible. Refine with saltpeter and other medicines. Combine the divine cinnabar with the mother in a four-six or three-seven ratio for optimal effect.

**Arsenic Crucible for Nurturing Calcined Frost Powder and White Divine Cinnabar (Dogwood Head)**

**Making the Crucible**

Grind one *jin* of arsenic finely, mix with finely pounded *xuancao*, and boil in water for three days. Remove, dry, and refine in a water-fire crucible for one day. Nurture with two *liang* of fire at dawn and dusk for seven days. Increase the fire and nurture for another seven days until no smoke remains. Then add two *liang* of raw arsenic, wait seven days, add another two *liang*, and repeat until four *liang* of raw arsenic are added—the crucible is now potent and can nurture white divine cinnabar. When first adding arsenic, place mercury and *he* in the center for potency, enabling the nurturing of frost powder.

**Method for Adding Mercury and *He* to the Arsenic Crucible**

Melt *he* into liquid, add a small amount of white rosin, stir until clear, then add mercury. For every five *liang* of arsenic, use three *liang* of *he* and nine *qian* of mercury—this ratio is standard. Distribute evenly into the arsenic crucible.

**Method for White Divine Cinnabar (Dogwood Head)**

Grind twenty *liang* each of mercury and arsenic into powder until no mercury stars remain. Gradually add five *liang* of western-facing container and five *liang* of alum, grind finely with the previous medicine, and refine in a water-fire crucible to form dogwood heads. Remove after one day, shape into chess-piece blocks, then boil with *mubie*, *duanchangju*, *matixiang*, and Sichuan pepper in three large bowls of water. Suspend the dogwood heads and boil for one day, then place in the arsenic crucible. Nurture with fire for fourteen days, then invert and remove for crucible use.

**Method for Calcining Lead Frost and Nurturing in the Arsenic Crucible**

Boil lead frost with fish-pond-grass juice until refined, then decoct with licorice nodes. Mix *sanleng*, *shihu*, *diyu*, and *wujia pi* into a powder to form a body-wrap, and nurture within the arsenic crucible before placing the dogwood-head crucible.

Once the dogwood heads are refined and boiled, use two *liang* of the previous arsenic crucible powder to cover both top and bottom. Then, soak the powder with natural juices of iron-pagoda grass and fresh ginger until moist, and nurture with water for seven days, applying two *liang* of fire at *mao* and *you* hours.

Remove, grind finely, and return to the crucible. Soak again with true juices of fragrant celery and fresh ginger, then nurture for another seven days with half the fire. Grind finely to form a crucible, then proceed to nurture the lead frost.

**Fire Regimen for Nurturing Lead Frost**
- Day 1–4: one *liang* each
- Day 5–6: one and a half *liang* each
- Day 7: two *liang*

**Method for Subduing Fire in Sulfur and Realgar**
Grind one *liang* each of sulfur and realgar with one *fen* of crane-crown frost, place in a box, and cover with another *fen* of frost. Seal tightly, then bury in an earthen cauldron. Apply five *jin* of external fire, then increase by half a *cheng* to subdue the fire. This is the Elixir of Pure Yang and Two Qi.

**Method for Refining Sulfur**
Take one *liang* of sulfur, one *liang* of ephedra, and two *liang* of *daji*. Burn to ash, layering top and bottom, seal tightly, and calcine in a well-mouth furnace until red. Pour into water, collect the floating sulfur, remelt, and refine as before for use.

**Method for Refining the Three-Yellow Crucible**
Grind one *liang* each of female sulfur into fine powder. Use a small oil-stained *meng* box, fill halfway with female sulfur, then sprinkle summer-withered grass powder lightly over the medicine. Mix another half *liang* of summer-withered grass with water to form a mud-like seal for the box’s mouth. Further seal with four *liang* of thoroughly mashed field-cross grass. Then, coat with salt-clay to a thickness of one *cun*, dry in the sun, and ensure no cracks form.

Place in a clean room on the ground, surround the box with one bowl of mulberry-wood ash sprayed with vinegar to moisten, then tightly pack the box with vinegar-soaked ash to conceal it. Arrange half a *cheng* of charcoal evenly, ignite from the top, and calcine. Once the fire has fully cooled, break the box, collect the medicine, and grind finely. Add another *liang* of male sulfur, grind finely, place in the box, seal as before, dry, and calcine. Wait for the fire to cool, then grind again.

Add one *liang* each of raw three yellows, grind together, and refine with fire as before. Then, add three *liang* of three yellows, grind, place in a large box, seal with grass powder, and calcine until cool. Add three *liang* of mercury and one portion of "yellow essence," grind until no mercury stars remain, then place in the box, seal with salt-clay, and bury in an ash pit (the nurturing fire ash pit).

Apply four *liang* of mature fire top and bottom, nurture for seven days, replenishing morning and evening with a constant four *liang* of fire. After seven days, if the yellow has formed into powder, shape into a golden-mother crucible.

Then, take one *liang* of refined gold, hammer into foil, and place with five *liang* of mercury in a jar. Add five *qian* of Sichuan pepper powder, seal the mouth with fresh ginger, and warm with ash fire, shaking frequently. Continuously add Sichuan pepper powder until it forms sand-like granules. Remove when tightly clustered like lotus seeds, and combine with true gold.

Use another sand box: first layer four *liang* of golden-crucible powder, then place a layer of sand granules, followed by another four *liang* of powder. Cover with the remaining powder, seal with salt-clay, dry, and place in the ash pit. Initially apply two *liang* of mature fire for one *fu* period, then increase to three *liang* for another *fu* period. Apply four *liang* of fire, then nurture for five more days. Finally, use three *jin* of mature fire to calcine until fully red, then remove for crucible use.

**Method for Calcining Sulfur**
Place any quantity of sulfur in a crucible and calcine with gentle fire. When ghostly flames arise, drip birch-leaf juice until the flames subside. Then, plug the crucible mouth with birch-leaf residue, calcine until red, and remove for crucible use. Nurture cinnabar, male and female sulfur, and mother sand in the crucible.

**Method for Calcining Realgar**
Take one *liang* of realgar, shape into blocks, and boil in wintergreen juice for one *fu* period. Then, use a fumigation crucible. Prepare equal parts of grass, mugwort, *juanwu*, and *diyu* into powder, fumigate the crucible until thick smoke fills it, then place the realgar inside. Cover with the powder, and calcine with slow fire until the crucible turns red. Remove when cool, break the crucible to retrieve the realgar, and simmer in goose fat for two hours. For every *liang* of silver, use one *qian* of yellow, applied in three doses to form red *geng*.

**Method for Subduing Sulfur**
Grind one *liang* of sulfur with two *liang* of mugwort ash, place in a crucible, and tightly cover with cold-water stone powder. Apply three *jin* of fire. When cool, place on paper, rinse with a bowl of water, and filter the clear liquid. Repeat with two *liang* of mugwort ash, rinse again, dry, and grind for transmutation use.

**Method for Subduing Realgar**
Take any quantity of realgar, grind with *wasong* and oyster shell into a thick paste, and coat the exterior of a crucible. Seal the mouth tightly, leaving three finger-widths of height and one finger-width of thickness. Place the realgar powder inside, then apply five *jin* of fire to the opening and calcine, monitoring closely. When the smoke dissipates and the substance shines like a mirror, remove and refine.

**Method for Subduing Sulfur**
For each *liang* of sulfur, wrap it in ink-dipped vinegar paper, cover the top with *wufang* grass, and seal the seams with saltpeter and clam powder. Then, mix bamboo-leaf ash with salt clay to reinforce the exterior. Apply half a *jin* of fire twice for tempering, then increase to five *jin* of fire and calcine until fully transformed.

**Four Spirit Receptacle**
Take one *jin* of sulfur in large chunks, each the size of a fist. Use three *jin* of fresh rehmannia root, extracting its natural juice. Place the sulfur chunks in an iron pot, cover them with the rehmannia residue, and press firmly into the pot’s base. Then, mix three *sheng* of true mulberry wood ash with the rehmannia juice and spread it over the residue. If ghostly flames appear around the edges, sprinkle dry mulberry wood ash on top to prevent ignition.

Heat the pot’s base with wood fire until the sulfur glows red. Remove the residue and ash from the sulfur’s surface, grind them together finely, and set aside. Take the sulfur from the pot’s base, combine the two ash mixtures, and rinse with boiling water until the liquid runs clear. If the rinsing liquid remains turbid, add more hot water and repeat until it clarifies.

Place the sulfur back into the pot with the clarified rinsing liquid and boil until dry. Transfer the sulfur into a copper-melting crucible, applying intense fire as in silver-smelting. When the sulfur turns to golden liquid, pour it into a mold to form "golden larvae," retaining its innate color and density.

After smelting, take one *liang* of this sulfur and combine it with one *liang* each of orpiment and realgar. Place the orpiment and realgar at the bottom of a sand crucible, cover with the smelted sulfur, and apply a cluster of fire until the crucible glows red. Grind the orpiment and realgar together finely, add one *liang* of dead sal ammoniac, and grind again into powder. Place the mixture into a copper-melting crucible, cover with a lid, and heat in a water-fire vessel until five cups of water evaporate. Separate the layers: sal ammoniac on top, sulfur in the middle, and orpiment-realgar at the bottom.

Take the three substances—sulfur, orpiment, and realgar—and refine one *liang* of cinnabar. Layer the cinnabar at the bottom and top, then apply fire morning and evening for seven days. Repeat with four *liang* of fire for another seven days. The resulting product forms the *Four Spirit Receptacle*, used to nurture *geng* silver mother-sand or for cyclic transformation methods. For sand, avoid forming pellets; instead, use long strips inserted into the receptacle for calcination. If the sal ammoniac turns uniformly white and separates on the surface, it may be removed. Do not grind sal ammoniac with the three yellows.

If ash frost appears on the receptacle’s surface, it must be removed by separating the layers until the frost is fully cleared.

**Dead Sal Ammoniac**
Take any quantity of sal ammoniac, boil it with two bowls of natural juice from *ruolian* (also called *mucai*), wrap it in silk, and suspend it to boil until the juice evaporates. Remove the silk, place the sal ammoniac in a *jian* bowl, and calcine it with the vegetable residue covering both top and bottom until the residue turns charred black. The sal ammoniac, now separated from its fumes, is ready for use in the three-yellows receptacle.

**Method for Calcinating Sulfur**
Take four *liang* of sulfur, grind it into fine grains, and boil it for one *fu* period with five or six bowls of juice from *tianzi* grass and spinach in equal parts, suspended in a silk pouch. Remove the sulfur, place it in a crucible, and cover the top and bottom with the vegetable residue. Temper with fire for three days until the residue dries inside. Then, apply three *jin* of fire for calcination. Remove the sulfur, sprinkle plum-kernel sand moistened with vinegar, and grind it into powder. Place the sulfur back into the crucible, secure it with thread, and coat the exterior with a honey-mixed paste of fivefold powder and *tiannanxing* in equal parts. Seal with *liuyi* clay, let dry, and heat in gentle and strong fire for one to two hours. Remove and proceed as follows:

First, heat a pot in the furnace until half-red. Add the sand, then sprinkle one *qian* of sulfur powder over it. When the substance transforms, add another *qian*, and repeat until all is added. Vigorously fan the fire, then add a small amount of borax. When the substance appears lustrous and pure, pour it out as treasure.

**Method for Boiling Dead Sulfur**
Boil sulfur for one day in equal parts of *cheqian* grass juice, mugwort juice, and banana oil. If it boils over, add paper-ash juice dropwise. One *qian* of this sulfur can transmute silver into *geng*.

**Method for Subduing the Three Yellows**
Grind leaf orpiment, water-ground realgar, and imported sulfur into an extremely fine powder. Mix with bitter wine to form a paste, wrap in *Kunlun* paper, and bind with a paste made from one and a half *liang* each of *fangfeng* and *huangqin*, along with *yangti* (not sheep’s hoof but *luti* vegetable). Next, extract juice from *qianzhen* grass, mix with *quezi* root and salt, and use yellow clay to seal the mixture. If unavailable, use leek juice or earthworm castings instead. Seal with a half-inch-thick layer of clay and let dry. Place the receptacle in a shallow pit, surround it with ash, and apply three *jin* of fire to calcine two-thirds. Then, apply fire again to complete the transformation. Cover with cold ash until cool, and it is ready for use.

*Poem:*
The grasses subdue the three yellows’ might,
Revealing the Dao’s profound alchemy.
The immortals’ secret arts take flight,
Uniting the heart with the Way’s decree.

**Method for Calcinating Sulfur**
Grind one *liang* of arsenic into powder, place it in a pot, and press it down with castor beans. Cover the pot’s mouth with silk, brush ginger juice onto the silk until it is fully absorbed, then invert the pot into cold ash and seal. Remove the arsenic, and use one *qian* per *liang* of substance for transmutation.

**Five Metals Powder Method**
Take one part each of arsenic, fivefold borax powder, and mercury, along with half a *liang* of refined cinnabar. Grind each ingredient in a mortar until no specks remain, then spread the mixture thickly between two layers of paper.

**Honey-Pepper and Poria with Five-Ingredient Resin Method**
Take honey-pepper, poria, and five-ingredient resin, along with grass-decision (cassia tora). Use one or two of these ingredients, wrap them in a cloth pouch, then tightly bind with hemp thread. Coat the exterior with fine ash mixed with vinegar, shaping it delicately. Use eight *jin* of hard charcoal, applying intense top-fire to calcine thoroughly.

*Secret Formula:*
Divide the medicine into seven parts, half-cooked, then separate. Use an iron shovel to cluster the fire, turning it repeatedly. Burn red-hot fire beneath until reduced to ash. Cover with a tile basin, encircle with clay strips, and leave overnight. Seal the base’s seams with clay strips for another night.

For three *liang* of bone and one *liang* of flesh: first boil the bones into broth, add half a *qian* of medicinal powder, stir rapidly, then pour out. Re-calcine, adding another half *qian* of powder, repeating four times. Ensure the base fire is well-arranged, with two *qian* of powder added continuously.

When using the trough: after firing, drip water—if it beads without scattering, pour into the trough to form a honeycomb texture. Mix two *qian* of nitre with one *qian* of arsenic; once complete, remove the greenish residue. For half a *qian* of calcined cinnabar and one *qian* of nitre, add one *fen* of fragrant scales, grind into powder, and coat evenly. Fire until no trace remains.

Grind the three ingredients into powder, mix with milk to form a thin paste, and apply with a goose feather. Then use fire to press it in.

**Powder Refinement Method**
Grind one *liang* of powder with two *qian* of silver filings, mixing evenly, then wrap in silk. Next, take one *liang* each of arisaema, black sesame, sanguisorba, pig-tooth soapnut, *qiannianrun* (evergreen vine), and aconite, grinding them into fine powder and dividing into two portions. Mix one half with honey for wrapping, and the other with camphor willow root and garlic juice, pounding evenly and wrapping in a layer to compact. Seal with salt-clay, calcine with three *jin* of top-fire until red-hot, then cool and remove.

For another *liang* of powder, divide into ten pieces, wrap in silk, discarding excess. Suspend in a crucible, boil in ginger juice, honey, and rice vinegar overnight. Then place in a kiln, stir-frying with *madouling* (birthwort fruit) nine times.

**Three-Preservation Method**
Mix one part arsenic, half a part powder, and one *liang* of three-seven cinnabar, grinding evenly. Wrap in boiled silk, suspend in a crucible, and boil in one bowl each of camphor willow and onion juice with four *liang* of honey until dry. Then take one *liang* each of eucommia bark and tangerine peel, grind into powder, and pack tightly in a crucible, sealing top and bottom. Cover with one *liang* of raw alum powder, sprinkle with water, then fill with lime. Seal the mouth with a tile, bind with iron wire in a cross, and reinforce with salt-clay. Once dry, calcine with three *jin* of top-fire until red-hot. Remove, cut into chunks, using one *qian* per *liang* of substance.

**Calcinated Lead Frost Method**
Grind one *liang* of powder (basin-mouth grade) into fine powder. Mix with paper mulberry juice to form a lump, wrap tightly in two layers of coarse silk, binding with thread and trimming the ends. Prepare the following medicine:

- Gardenia
- Chinese gall
- Sliced turmeric

Take equal parts of these three ingredients, half a *liang* each, grinding into fine powder. Mix with half a cup of rice vinegar, half a cup of ginger juice, and honey. Place in a *jian* bowl, set over two *jin* of mature fire. When the medicinal liquid boils, add the three ingredients, stirring into a thick paste. Place the powder ball in the center of the medicinal liquid, using a well-fire method. Once the medicine ignites, remove the well-fire and apply intense fire until the smoke dissipates. The center of the bowl should form a pellet the size of a bullet. Remove the bowl, cover with half-dry, half-wet ash. Once cooled, remove, using one *qian* per *liang* of substance, divided into three applications.

**Calcinated Arsenic Method**
Grind one *liang* of arsenic finely in a basin. Take equal parts of sophora root, arisaema, and acanthopanax bark, grinding into coarse powder. Use a six-*liang* crucible, place the medicine inside to fumigate the crucible, then cover with damp paper. When the crucible turns black, remove the medicinal ash and add the arsenic, covering it with the previous medicinal powder. If arsenic fumes appear, add more powder, and remove after half a day. Once cooled, break the crucible, taking out the arsenic. Use one *qian* per *liang* of substance, divided into three applications, adding arsenic first, then powder.

**Calcinated Arsenic Powder Method**
Grind together one *liang* of arsenic, half a *liang* of powder, two *qian* of calcined substance, half a *liang* of *xipeng* (borax), two *qian* of cinnabar, and two *qian* of mercury. Wrap in silk to form a ball, place in a jar, and fill with banana ash juice. Bury the medicine in the center, nurturing with fire for fourteen days. Seal externally with *didancao* (blister beetle), then reinforce entirely with spirit-clay.
