Place in a furnace, nurturing with fire: first seven days, use four *liang* of *mao-you* fire; second seven days, use five *liang* of *mao-you* fire; fifth and sixth days, six *liang*; seventh day, half a *jin*. Once complete, remove and place on the ground for seven days before opening the jar to retrieve the medicine. Use one *qian* per *liang* for transmutation.

**Calcinated Arsenic Powder Method (Alternative)**
Grind two *liang* of arsenic and one *liang* of powder into fine powder, then add three *qian* of psoralea powder, mixing evenly. Wrap in silk to form a ball, boil in natural spinach juice until thoroughly permeated. Then pack the vegetable residue and ball tightly into a bottle, firing until the residue chars. Remove. Use one and a half *qian* per *liang* of substance, divided into three applications.

**Another Method**
Grind four *liang* of arsenic into powder. Divide three *liang* of lead frost into three packets. Take an unspecified quantity of *wufangcao* (five-direction herb), pound thoroughly, and extract the natural juice to mix with the arsenic into balls. Then use the *wufangcao* residue to form cakes, layering the arsenic in a sand jar. Fill the jar’s top with finely pounded fresh ginger.

Seal the mouth and seams with red halloysite clay, then coat the entire vessel externally with salt-clay to a thickness of approximately half an inch. Once dry, place it in an ash pit, apply four *liang* of fire, and nurture for one full day and night. The following day, add four *jin* of fire, calcining until the fuel is fully consumed. After a day, open and inspect—the arsenic will have been rendered inert, forming a single mass. Grind to a fine powder, add one *liang* of lead frost, and grind evenly. Also use *wufangcao* (five-direction herb), following the previous method to mix, seal, and dry. Then apply three *jin* of fire to calcine until red. After a day, open and inspect, then add another *liang* of lead frost, repeating the method as before. After three such cycles—along with the single calcination of arsenic—four firings in total are recorded. The medicine will resemble amber in color. Grind finely into powder; for each *liang* of substance, use one *qian* of amber arsenic, melt together, and pour out. Once it achieves the superior hue, it may be fashioned into vessels. Boil in plum juice, and it will never develop a cloudy tint nor exhibit harshness or volatility.

**Another Method**
One *liang* of arsenic yellow, one *liang* of subdued-fire *pao*, half a *liang* of lead frost, and half a *liang* of arsenic.
Grind the above ingredients together, place in a sand jar, seal as before, and apply gentle and strong fire, nurturing for seven days. Conclude with a strong fire of one *chi* in height. Cool and grind; divide each *liang* into two portions, each portion sufficient to refine one *jin* of high-quality material.

**Subduing Fire for *Pao* Sand**
For each *liang* of *pao*, use one *liang* of cuttlefish bone.
Grind the two ingredients together, first heat a pot until red-hot, then immediately add the medicine and pour out once melted.

**Method for Subduing Lead Frost**
One *liang* of lead powder.
Mix with *jindeng* flower juice to form balls, wrap in ink-dyed paper, place in a jar, and cover with one *liang* of *tiannanxing* (arisaema). Further cover with five layers of lotus leaves, seal as before, apply three *jin* of fire, and calcine to completion.

**Calcining Arsenic**
Use an unspecified quantity of arsenic.
Cover with gypsum powder, place in a crucible, and seal the top with a bowl. The arsenic will sublimate onto the bowl; collect it. Then take the arsenic, pound *bima* (castor bean) meat into a paste, wrap the arsenic inside, further wrap in *kunlun* paper, and seal externally with mud. Apply three *jin* of fire to calcine until cool.

**Five Spirits Seizing the Seven Po**
Grind one *liang* of lead powder finely, place in a *jian* bowl, and steep repeatedly in boiling water to remove alum taste, five or six times, until tasteless. Divide into two balls using white silk, tying tightly. Extract juice from fresh ginger and radish to make one cup, add one *liang* of honey, place the lead powder balls inside, and suspend to boil until dry. Stir-fry in an iron pan until the silk turns charred black. Do not remove the silk fragments. Grind *langdu* (wolfsbane) and *kushen* (flavescent sophora) in equal parts into powder, mix with four walnut meats, grind finely, add a small amount of honey, and form into cakes to encase the lead powder balls. Further wrap with pounded *didancao* (blister beetle herb), place in a jar, and cover the top and bottom with fine powder of mulberry leaves and eggplant leaves. Seal the seams, apply two *liang* of fire morning and evening, and nurture for three days. Then place in a furnace, apply three *jin* of fire to calcine until red-hot, cool, and remove. Crush into powder, add two and a half *liang* of mercury, seal as before, nurture for seven days, then calcine red-hot again. Cool, remove, pound into powder in a mortar, add another two and a half *liang* of mercury, seal as before, nurture with fire for three days, then place in the furnace with three *jin* of fire to calcine red-hot. Remove and break into chunks. Take seven *liang* of *mozhangzi* (grinding rod), melt in furnace smoke, and pour the previous medicine into it to form superior silver.

**Hundred-and-One Powder**
Grind one *liang* of lead powder finely, wrap in silk to form four balls, and boil in three *liang* of honey using a double boiler until the honey is exhausted. Wash the lead powder balls clean, then boil in a strong *zaojiao* (Chinese honey locust) decoction for one full day and night. Remove, then boil in one cup of *jichangcao* (chicken intestine herb) juice with half a *liang* of borax until adhering closely. Wrap externally with a piece of black gauze, tie securely, place in an iron pan, and stir-fry for three two-hour periods. Remove and grind finely. Add one *liang* of *sanqi* mother cinnabar, grind together, and wrap again. Then use equal parts of *baiyaojian* (myrobalan), lead white frost, and *madouling* (birthwort fruit) as *jin* powder. Stir-fry the lead powder balls for two two-hour periods, remove, and bury in the ground overnight. For each *qian* of powder, refine one *liang* of substance, dividing into three applications. Wrap the powder in silver foil when adding; use in proportions of three, seven, four, or six—excellent.

**Method for Calcining Arsenic Powder**
One *liang* of arsenic, half a *liang* of lead powder, three *qian* of borax, and one *qian* of *liu* (sulphur).
Grind the four ingredients into powder and wrap in *kunlun* paper to form a ball. Then take one *liang* each of *caowu* (wild aconite) and *nanxing* (arisaema), grind into powder, and mix with *wuyecao* (five-leaf herb)—if unavailable, substitute spinach—pounded into a paste to form a dough. Encase the previous medicine ball as a lining. Seal externally with salt-clay to a thickness of approximately one inch, and dry in silence. Apply six *jin* of fire, calcining in a spiral from the top; when smoke appears, withdraw the fire. Repeat this process twice, then calcine in a damp ash bed until cool. Grind finely to the size of millet grains. For each seven *qian* of substance, use three *qian* of mother material and one and a half *qian* of medicine, adding in three applications. Refine the substance, then boil in salt, alum, and plum juice for half a day.

**Four Spirits Alchemical Refinement**
One *liang* of *sanqi* mother cinnabar, one and a half *liang* of lead powder, one *liang* of arsenic, one *qian* of borax, one *qian* of *liu* (sulphur), *huayin xixin* (asarum from Huayin), *juanxiang* (costus root), *caowu* (wild aconite), and *bai’ai* (mugwort).
Grind the four herbal ingredients in equal parts into fine powder. Use a jar, placing half a *liang* of medicine on the top and bottom, with the previous medicine in the center. Apply half a *jin* of fire and three cups of water as the measure. For the second firing, use two *jin* of fire and five cups of water. For the third firing, use five cups of water and five *jin* of fire. Refine one *liang* and one *qian* of cinnabar per application.

**Golden Tripod Powder**

Lead powder, one *liang*, ground into fine powder and bound in silk.

Five倍子 (*wu bei zi*), *he che* (human placenta), and various tooth-ridge horns.
Place in a large bowl of water and boil until the powder is dry.

**Method for Forging the Golden Tripod Cinnabar**
Three *liang* of arsenic, four *liang* of lead.
Melt the lead in a crucible until liquefied, then add three or four drops of water to clarify the liquid. Add cinnabar.
Cut the cinnabar into dice-sized pieces and gradually introduce them into the crucible. Once complete, lift and open it in a cool place—the crucible will naturally separate, with lead settling at the bottom and golden cinnabar rising to the surface.
Next, pulverize the cinnabar finely, then grind the pre-boiled powder. Place one *qian* of silver foil in a silver dish, cut into pieces, with half inside and half layered above and below, sandwiching the powder in the center.
Add a small amount of mercury, seal it, then cover with nine *qian* of *Golden Tripod Cinnabar*. Place in a *jian* bowl, seal the bowl, and cover tightly with a lamp dish.
Fill the top with ash, shaping it into a cone. Surround with fire, using five *jin* for one firing, reducing by two-thirds.
Once cool, remove it. The bowl must be placed on a water vessel below before firing.
Refire as before, covering it, but without cinnabar—only a white-fired bowl cover weighing three *jin*.
When the furnace cools, remove and pulverize finely. Add one *qian* of bright raw arsenic, knead with sour juice into pills.
Dry them, wrap in silver foil, and mix with one *fen* each of *juan qiao* (withered lotus receptacle) and sour juice to form a body-adherent paste.
Also, prepare a paste from sour juice herb and purple duckweed (in any quantity) for external application as body-adherent spheres.
Seal with *liu yi* mud, fire with three *jin* for one firing, reducing by two-thirds.
Once cool, remove it—one *qian* will transmute one *liang* and three *qi* of *sanqi*.

**Lead-Refined Danyang Powder**
Six *liang* of powder, white poplar (washed), *tu zhu* (cinnabar substitute), *bai shan* (white clay), table salt, *yu zan* (jade hairpin), four *liang* each; *dai zhe* (hematite), three *liang*; *chi shi zhi* (red halloysite), two *liang*; *qing fan* (green vitriol), four *liang*; rock crystal, four *liang*.
Grind all ingredients evenly into powder, then pound with rice vinegar into a paste.
First, use yellow wax proportionate to the powder’s quantity, shaping it into small pills.
Seal with the prepared medicine, dry, then melt the wax spheres to empty them, refilling with powder.
Seal the box’s opening with medicine, dry, bind with iron wire, and place in an iron pot. Boil in lead liquid for three days and nights.
Remove when black—one *qian* transmutes one *liang* of material, without requiring *gou mu* (hook mother).

**Queen Mother’s Palace: One-Month Cycle Method**
One *liang* of *fen shuang* (calomel), half a *liang* of mercury.
Grind the two ingredients together until no specks remain.
Take a chicken egg, pierce one end, and remove the yolk and white. Grind *zhang nao* (camphor) in any quantity, place inside the eggshell, swirl, then pour out.
Add the calomel-mercury mixture, then cover with *huang qin* (scutellaria) powder in any quantity.
Use another half eggshell to seal the opening.
Secure the medicine, place in a *wu zhi kui* (ignorance-sealing vessel), tamp firmly, and seal the vessel’s opening with additional sealing medicine.
Externally, bind with iron wire, set on a tripod stand, and nurture the vessel with paper ash. The ash on the crucible should be one *cun* and a half thick. The firing schedule is as follows:
*Mao-you* fire.
One day, one *liang*.

On the second day, the same.
On the third day, two *liang*.
On the fourth day, three *liang*.
On the fifth day, four *liang*.
On the sixth day, five *liang*.
On the seventh day, six *liang*.
On the eighth day, remove and grind finely again, then reuse the medicine and nurture for another seven days with the following firing schedule:
On the first day, two *liang*.
On the second day, three *liang*.
On the third day, four *liang*.
On the fourth day, five *liang*.
On the fifth day, six *liang*.
On the sixth day, seven *liang*.
On the seventh day, seven *liang*.
On the eighth day, remove; use one *qian* to transmute one *liang* of red silver into the supreme treasure.

**Method for Subduing Sal Ammoniac**
One *liang* of sal ammoniac, half a *liang* of mulberry ash frost.
Grind together, place in a box, and cover with an additional layer for sealing. Nurture with two *liang* of fire for three days, then add three *jin* of fire to calcine until glowing red. Allow to cool and retrieve the subdued fire.

**Alternative Method**
For each *liang*, use one piece of frankincense ground to powder. First melt the borax, then add the frankincense, stir until uniform, and pour out. Each *zi* can transmute one *liang*.

**Method for Dead Borax**
Four *liang* of borax, one *liang* of aged tangerine peel, two *liang* of *zhi mu* (anemarrhena).
Grind the above into a fine powder, heat in a crucible, add the sal ammoniac, and fan vigorously until molten. Pour out.

**Divine Immortal’s Elixir for Refining White Divine Cinnabar**
Half a *liang* each of cinnabar and sulfur, one *liang* of *di ru xiang* (dripping frankincense).
Grind the three ingredients into a fine powder, add a small amount of walnut meat, and grind into a mass. Wrap first in two layers of damp paper, then one layer of dry paper. Bind with hemp strips. Next, take one *qian* each of gall and alum, and half a *liang* of good *meng shi* (chlorite schist). Grind into a fine powder, add half a *liang* of purslane, and grind evenly. Mix with one *sheng* of rice vinegar, simmer over a slow fire to form a paste, and shape into cakes. Place the previously prepared medicinal ball at the center, then wrap in three to five layers of paper. Place in a box, tamp the surrounding space with lime until full, and seal the opening with honey-mixed clam powder. Externally, seal with salt clay and allow to dry. Dig a pit one *chi* and two *cun* deep and wide, use three *dou* of *jin su* (golden millet) fire. First place the box in the pit, then cover with millet husks, filling evenly and tamping firmly. Ignite from above and continue until the fire is exhausted. Wait until the smoke has completely dissipated and the vessel has cooled before opening the box. Then, use five *jin* of hard, mature fire to calcine, reducing the fire by three *jin*. Retrieve the medicine without losing a single speck. Again, use a *gan wo* (sweet crucible) to calcine until molten, then pour into the pit. The weight remains unchanged. This medicine is a transmuter: for every ten *liang* of refined cinnabar, use one *liang* of White Divine Elixir. Place together in a *gan guo* (sweet crucible), melt into a liquid, and when the sound of cicadas is heard, stir vigorously with a willow branch. When the sound ceases, pour into the pit to form an ingot, ready for use as desired.

**Method for Refining Cinnabar**
Ten *liang* of cinnabar.
First melt in a new iron pan, then add two *liang* of antelope horn and two *liang* of *tai yin xuan jing shi* (selenite) powder, stirring immediately. If the cinnabar disappears, do not be alarmed—intensify the fire and stir until it reappears. Pour the cinnabar onto the ground; it will lose half its weight. The refined cinnabar will be as white as snow, and when broken, its texture will be finely serrated—ideal for transmutation.

*Collected Writings on the Dao of Metal, Scroll Six Concludes*
*Collected Writings on the Dao of Metal, Scroll Seven*

**Method for Making Iron Resemble Silver Using Lychee Pits**
Grind lychee pits into powder, then stir-fry the cinnabar. When the pit powder turns to ash, remove it and stir-fry again. Add to boiling water with oxhide glue three to five times; the cinnabar will become as lovely as silver, with a powdery pink hue, weighing three to five *fen*, and will not darken or tarnish.

**Alternative Method for Copper**
Use the roots of *gu chui cao* (drumstick grass) to fill a box and smoke a crucible until it is thoroughly blackened. Add borax and melt into a liquid. When cool, the borax will congeal into a solid mass. Melt copper in a separate crucible, then add the hardened borax. The copper will separate, with red above and white below. Stir with a new red-hot tile strip, removing all floating impurities until the liquid resembles clear water—this is the ideal state.

**Method for Purifying Blackened Objects to Restore Their True Luster**
- One *liang* of saltpeter
- Five tubes of calomel
- Thirty *wen* of green alum
- One piece of pumice the size of two *qian*
- One piece of borax the size of the pumice

Grind the above into powder. Place the object in a pot, covering the bottom and top with the powder. Heat with fire, and the impurities within the object will separate. Once the blackness is removed, the object will be pure, lustrous, and precious—most effective when placed at the bottom of the pot.

**Method for Softening Staffs**
Grind fifty parts frankincense with one *liang* of nitre. For each *liang* of staff material, add one *qian* of the mixture—adding more will make it too soft.

**Method for Drawing Blood**
- Five *wen* of *mu lü* (high-quality)
- Five *wen* of arsenic

Melt one *liang* of staff material into a liquid. Wrap the above ingredients in paper, stir evenly into the molten metal, and pour into a mold. Cover with damp paper, and it will turn white.

**Alternative Method**
- Five *wen* of dried scorpions
- Five *wen* of arsenic

Grind finely as before, add to the molten metal, stir evenly, and pour out—it will also turn white.

**Method for Transmuting with Dead Arsenic**
- Four *liang* of arsenic, finely ground
- Fifteen *chuan lian* seeds
- Two *liang* each of *gu jing cao* and *wu ye teng*

Chop each ingredient finely, stir-fry until black and charred (retaining their properties), then grind into powder. Mix with the previously prepared arsenic, adding one and a half *qian* of silver and one *qian* of frankincense. (These two may be omitted if desired.)

Use a porcelain white bottle as a water-fire vessel, filling it with four cups of water. Once cooled and opened, the result will resemble jade-like silver—most pleasing. The transmuting agent will settle at the bottom of the cup, with one and a half *qian* sufficient to transmute one *liang*. Adjust quantities as needed.

**Method for Rendering Dead Arsenic Safe**
Use any amount of arsenic, boiling it in mulberry wood ash lye for three full days. Then process it in a water-fire vessel to subdue its fire. If not fully subdued, boil and process again. This can be used with chalcanthite, lead powder, cinnabar, realgar, orpiment, and mother cinnabar—all will be effective.

**Alternative Method**
Use *mai men dong*, cockscomb flower, and *jin suo tian*.

Take the juice of these three ingredients, boil for one day, then discard the plant residue. This subdues the fire.

**Alternative Method**
Use *che qian zi* and camphorwood root.
Pound to extract the juice, mix with arsenic powder, and wrap together with the medicinal residue. Place in a container and nurture with slow fire for three days, then use a strong fire to subdue it.

**Alternative Method**
Take one *liang* each of *mu lü* and arsenic, grind finely, and kill. First heat a crucible until glowing red, then place the two ingredients inside. After a long while, apply a strong fire to subdue them.

**Alternative Method**
Spread a layer of *pi li zi* powder at the bottom of a crucible, add a layer of arsenic, then a layer of medicinal powder. Alternate layers of arsenic and medicinal powder three or four times. On top, place a layer of saltpeter, then a layer of *bai hu*, filling the mouth tightly. Seal firmly, allow to dry, then apply a strong fire until the contents turn dark. Once cooled, remove and grind to powder.

**Alternative Method**
Use *ku lian* tree bark and *qian niu zi*.
Grind these two ingredients into powder and spread at the bottom. Cover with arsenic, seal, and apply fire to render it inert.

**Alternative Method**
Take three *liang* each of arsenic and saltpeter, grind into fine powder, and wrap the arsenic-saltpeter mixture in *kun lun* paper. Then take three *liang* of *bai hu* powder, spread a layer at the bottom of the crucible, place the wrapped arsenic-saltpeter in the center, and cover with another three *liang* of *bai hu* powder, filling the mouth completely. Press tightly, seal, and allow to dry. Apply fire gradually from low to high, then use a strong fire to calcine. Once cooled, retrieve the product.

**Four White Ingredients Five-Fold Transmutation Method**
This may also be used in a vessel to subdue and render arsenic inert.
Two *liang* of arsenic, one *liang* of *fen shuang*, half a *liang* each of southern borax and *nao sha*.
Grind together into powder, wrap tightly in a silver strip, then wrap again in silk. Take one *liang* each of *bai you*, *bai lian*, *cao wu*, and *zhi mu*, grind into powder, and spread at the bottom of a new large earthen pot. Place the silk-wrapped packet on top, then cover with the herbal powder, pressing firmly. Fill the top with clean yellow earth. Use three *jin* of fire to calcine until slightly red, then remove. Cover with a pile of fresh earth and let sit briefly before reheating.
Repeat this process five times, each for one *ke*. On the fifth *ke*, cover with earth until fully cooled. Remove and form into small pieces. Use two *qian* to transmute one *liang* of base metal.

**Bone-Transforming Method**
Take equal parts of aged arsenic and *fen shuang*, grind together into fine powder.
Mix with the natural juice of fresh ginger to form a paste, wrap tightly in white silk, and coat the exterior thickly with a mixture of honey and powdered *da ji* and *juan xiang*. Place in a box, seal the opening with a paste of clam powder and oil.
Then seal the exterior with paper-fiber and mud, allow to dry, and calcine with fire until a fragrance is detected. Remove, grind into powder, and use one *qian* to transmute one *liang* of base metal.
For superior results, add mother cinnabar in a 50-50 ratio; for medium results, use a 40-60 ratio; for lower results, a 30-70 ratio.

**Method for Subduing *Fen Shuang***
Take one *liang* of *fen shuang* and three *qian* of silver filings, cut finely, and grind together into an extremely fine powder. Wrap tightly in boiled silk. Use the juice of fresh ginger, knotweed, or—if unavailable—scallion root juice or camphorwood root juice, and boil until the liquid is fully absorbed and dry. Remove, trim away the "umbilical cord," and wrap in a silver dish.
Take one cup each of the aforementioned juices, and grind *qiang hua*, *chen pi*, and *du zhong* into coarse powder. Place in a crucible and heat until smoke nearly dissipates. Quickly add half a *liang* of alum to the crucible, then place the wrapped *fen shuang* inside. Cover with more alum powder and fan with a bellows until dry. Remove once cooled and set aside for use.

**Alternative Method**
Take half a *liang* each of *zi shen*, *zhi mu*, and *tian men dong*, grind into fine powder, and mix with fresh ginger juice to form a paste. Coat the exterior of the medicinal ball.
Next, take three dried persimmons, chew thoroughly into a paste. Take thirty *Qingzhou* dates, remove the pits, and pound into a paste. Wrap the medicinal ball again.
Seal with paper-fiber and salt mud, then calcine with five *jin* of fire. Once the fire has diminished by more than half, turn the ball and calcine again. When the fire is exhausted, remove the ball and plunge into a water pit. After a long while, retrieve and allow to cool briefly. Test over fire—if not fully subdued, repeat the calcination until glowing red, no more than three times, to achieve fire resistance.
When transmuting, use a pinch of borax and *nao sha* for best results.

**Alternative Method**
Use camphorwood root (also called *dang lu*).
Dry in the sun, burn to ash, and leach to obtain the juice. Place in a porcelain bottle, then leach the ash again twice with the concentrated juice. Boil the ash juice until dry, place in a box, seal the opening, and calcine the powder to subdue the fire.

**Alternative Method**
Spread *tie jiao po luo men cao* at the bottom of a crucible, place the powder in the center, and cover the top with a paste made from *bi ma zi*. Secure a water cup on top of the crucible with iron wire and process in a water-fire vessel.
If not subdued, alternate fire above and water below three to five times to render the fire inert.
There are other methods, some for transmuting *mao* into *danyang*, which are extraordinarily effective.

**Method for White Calcination**
First, form the powder into pellets using *chu* juice, then dry in the sun. Next, wrap them in fine silk, then take one bowl each of *di lian*, *yan cao*, and *ji chang cao* juices. Enclose the wrapped medicine within a vessel, suspend it, and boil for one full day—slow heat is best. Then apply a concealing medicine to the body: grind equal parts *huang lian*, *huang xiang*, *huang qin*, *cao long dan*, and *ku zhang* into powder, mix with vinegar, and coat the wrapped medicine to a thickness of one inch. Cluster five *jin* of fire around it, reducing the fire by three-tenths. Remove the fire and cover the kiln with damp earth. This powder requires no clay pellets—this is the *Yuanwu* Master’s method.

**Four White Substances for Concealing Various Materials or *Danyang***
- Four *liang* of subdued *pi*
- Six *liang* of subdued *liu*
- Half a *liang* of subdued *fen shuang*
- Two and a half *qian* of subdued *xiao*

**Subduing *Pi***
Take a large *dang lu* root, cut a piece, hollow a cavity, place a small piece of *pi* inside, then boil in the root’s natural juice. When the large root turns black, the fire is subdued. If not subdued, replace with another root as the base, take fresh juice, and boil again—then the fire will be subdued. Repeatedly verified.

**Subduing *Sha***
Grind *di fu zi* into powder, mix evenly, and calcine in a sealed crucible. Alternatively, use *zi bei hu er cao* or *tian qie er* powder—both can subdue *liu*. Repeatedly verified.

**Subduing *Fen Shuang***
Boil in wild redflower root juice to subdue.

**Subduing *Xiao***
Pound *ce qiao* branches and leaves to extract juice, then stir-fry to subdue. Alternatively, pound *ce wu* leaves into a paste, spread half on the bottom, place *xiao* inside, cover with the remaining paste, and calcine with intense fire until it melts into a jade-like mass—ready for use. Repeatedly verified.

Once the four substances are subdued, place them in a water-fire vessel, add seven or eight cups of water, then calcine with intense fire until truly inert—ready for concealing. To make *Danyang*, add two and a half *qian* of *ru xiang* and two and a half *qian* of *huang dan* into the vessel, process, then remove to apply to materials.

**Mother Cinnabar Method**
Two *liang* of mother, eight *liang* of mercury.
Shape the mother into a dish and place it in the vessel. Add mercury onto the dish, then cover with medicinal powder as follows: *chuan jiao*, *xi xin*, *huang wu*, *gan lao*, tea leaves, and *jing jie*—each three *qian*, ground into powder, to cover the mother and mercury. Then calcine with one *cheng* of charcoal until complete. Remove the cinnabar, cut into dice-like blocks, boil in honey mixed with *mi tuo seng* powder, then place in a lead concealing vessel to nurture.

**Method for Making Dead Lead into a Concealing Vessel**
One *jin* of lead, half a *jin* of *yan xiao*.
First melt the *xiao* in a crucible, then add the lead and boil for one day. Remove, grind into powder, soak in boiling water, and dry in the sun to form the concealing vessel—use four *liang*.

Place the previous cinnabar into the vessel, apply four *liang* of *mao-you* fire, and nurture for three days. Remove and prepare the kiln medicine as follows:

**Treasure-Ruining Medicine**
Mix equal parts buckwheat ash and *xin* into powder, form into balls with water, calcine, and grind into powder. Add equal parts *dan fan*, *bai yao yu* powder, *ding tou*, and calcined *dai zhe shi*, along with one *liang* of *yan xiao*. Melt in fire, then add twenty *wen* of *shao fen* and twenty *wen* of *peng sha*. Grind into powder—use three *qian* each to line the bottom and top, then calcine one *liang* of cinnabar.

**Lead Calcination Method**
Half a *jin* of black lead.
Place in an iron pan and stir-fry with a large bamboo whisk. Add *yan xiao* powder and continue frying until the lead is dry. For each *liang* of lead, use half a *liang* of *xiao* powder.

Place the lead powder into a sand container, insert the mercury-cinnabar ball (remove the silk wrapping), cover with powder, and seal the concealing vessel with iron wire. Seal the outer seams with *shi zhi* mixed with vinegar. Place in the furnace, dry with paper ash, then sift and prepare the furnace. Position the container inside, place one *liang* of charcoal on top, and ignite for one day and night. Repeat for three days and nights. When the fire is sufficient, remove and place in a pit. Press down with the aforementioned medicinal herbs, then seal the surface with salt. Apply intense fire to melt into liquid.

**Method for Forming Mother Cinnabar**
Five *liang* of mercury.

Two *liang* of silver. Combine these two substances in a mortar. Then take two *liang* of *zhimu* (Anemarrhena asphodeloides), decoct finely, and pour the liquid into the previous ingredients. Grind together until thoroughly blended, stopping once the substance is formed. If not yet achieved, decoct again and continue grinding. Then strain through white paper to form pellets the size of bullets, securing them with thread. Next, take two *sheng* of sour vinegar water (or ginger juice if vinegar water is unavailable) and place in a clean jar. Suspend the cinnabar pellet by its thread into the jar and boil for one *fu* period. Remove and place in a basin of cold water, whereupon the substance will harden.

**Adhesive for Personal Use**
Equal parts *chuanjiao* (Zanthoxylum bungeanum), *chuanwu* (Aconitum carmichaelii), and *xixin* (Asarum heterotropoides). Use raw, grind into powder, mix with honey, and apply to the cinnabar pellet. Place in a clean area to dry, then store in a *guizi* (concealing vessel).

**Method for the Concealing Vessel**
Three *liang* of black lead, one *jin* of lime, and one and a half *liang* of *dansha* (sal ammoniac). First, melt the black lead in a wok until liquid. Add the lime and stir evenly. Then add the *dansha*, stirring with an iron spoon until it becomes a liquid. Pour onto the ground to cool, then remove. Place in an earthenware box, level the surface, and arrange the sand as in the lotus-nurturing method. Next, mix *gefen* (clam powder) and salt with water to form a paste, sealing the mouth of the box. Take a new tile basin, fill it with ash, and bury the box at its center, covering it with ash. Use one and a half *jin* of firewood, gradually adding more over one *fu* period. The next day, use another one and a half *jin* of firewood, following the same method. On the third day, use three *jin* of firewood, again adding gradually, for another *fu* period. Once cooled, remove and boil in *wumei* (Prunus mume) water for one *shi* period, then refine into a treasure.

**Method for Forming *Geng* Cinnabar**
One *qian* of *geng* (metallic essence) and three *qian* of mercury. Use half a cup of pure sesame oil, add one *gualouzi* (Trichosanthes kirilowii seed), and decoct until the medicinal pellet turns yellow. Add another seed, repeating until seven seeds have been used. Gradually add six to seven *fen* of *baijiaoxiang* (resin), decoct briefly, then pour and knead to form. Wash thoroughly with hot water to remove medicinal residue until the cinnabar pellet gleams. Fill with *wumei* pits, then apply cinnabar to the surface. Next, coat the exterior with *baimei* (Prunus mume) pulp, then mix *caowu* (Aconitum kusnezoffii) powder with vinegar and apply all over. Wrap entirely in paper and mud, then bake until dry. Cover the top with ash and surround with fire on all sides, nurturing for one night until the cinnabar emerges. Then mix *ziheche* (placenta) powder with honey and apply in a layer over silk. Next, mix equal parts *xixin* (Asarum heterotropoides), *caowu* (Aconitum kusnezoffii) powder, *baihe* (Lilium brownii), and *jiangzi* (Croton tiglium), blend with honey, and apply another layer. Seal externally with salt mud, allow to dry, then place in the furnace and nurture with starlight fire for one *hui* period.

**Method for Following the Mother with Three Essences**
One *qian* of *geng* and one *fen* of mercury. Combine these two to form cinnabar. Add one *qian* of cinnabar. Grind all three together evenly, mix with *yuxingcao* (Houttuynia cordata) juice to form pellets, then roll in *huangfan* (yellow vitriol) as an adhesive layer, with *jinfan* (potash alum) as the outer seal. When refining silver, use *jinfan* as the adhesive layer and *huangfan* as the outer seal. Wrap in paper and place on *yinshi* (mica or similar mineral) overnight. Then finely grind *yuxingcao*, apply as an adhesive layer one finger thick. Next, use *huanghua* (dayflower), *jichangcao* (Acalypha australis), and *shemao* (five-leaved snake grass), pound into a paste, and apply another layer one finger thick. Then mix one *liang* of charcoal ash and one *qian* of *qingyan* (green salt), decoct with water to form a concealing vessel called the "willow floss vessel." Use five to six *jin* of mature fire for one *hui* period. Once the medicine has passed through, remove and refine in the furnace.

Jade and mica: Take two *liang* of each, boil in one bowl of rice vinegar until fully absorbed, then dry by baking. Store in a porcelain box, using half a *liang* of the mixture to cover each *liang* of the substance. Refine by *hui*, dissolve in water, and reuse.

**Cinnabar Gold Method**
Use four *liang* of large cinnabar chunks, wrap in silk, and suspend for steeping as follows: Combine one *liang* each of *diyu* (burnet), *chushizi* (paper mulberry fruit), *baji* (morinda root), and *gansui* (kan-sui root). Grind these into fine powder, divide into four packets, and boil in good rice vinegar for one *fu* period. Add vinegar once and medicine once in four stages until fully boiled, then remove the cinnabar.

Take one *liang* of silver and four *qian* of *geng* (metal essence), melt together, hammer into foil, and cut into pieces. Wrap and stir-fry as in the lotus-seed method, placing the cinnabar inside. Mix honey with *mituoseng* (litharge) powder for an adhesive layer half a grain of rice thick. Then blend refined honey with *yuxingcao* root and *lizhicao* (lychee grass) powder, applying another adhesive layer one grain of rice thick. Place in a *qingyan* (green salt) vessel with four *liang* of fire, nurture for seven days. Remove when cool, place on a brick, refine with three *jin* of charcoal fire for one *hui*, then cool again. Transfer to a crucible for forging, then boil with *yan* (salt), *fan* (alum), and *dan* (chalcanthite) until fully processed. Pour repeatedly, refining dozens of times to form the treasure.

**Vessel-Making Method**
Take half a *jin* of *qingyan* (green salt), boil with two bowls of lotus root juice until dry, then bake. Place in a crucible, forge into liquid, pour out, and grind into fine powder after a short while. Store in a box, first placing dead white salt at the bottom, then *qingyan*, and finally dead white *yan* (salt) on top. Seal the seams with clam powder mixed with vinegar. Dead white *yan* is prepared by forging with *zhimu* (anemarrhena).

**Refining Divine Sand Method**
Take eight *liang* of mercury, first with one and a half *liang* of sulfur, half a *liang* of *dilei* sulfur, half a *liang* of realgar, and one *qian* of orpiment. Grind the three yellows into powder, stir-fry into "blue-gold head" according to the method, then place in an upper vessel with water below. Refine with fire to form divine sand, yielding one or two *qian* as a gift.

**Boiling Method**
Use equal parts of *qianghua* (wolfsbane), *wubei* (Chinese gall), *daji* (euphorbia), *chuanjiao* (Sichuan pepper), *langdu* (wolf’s-bane root), lotus leaf ash, two *qian* of *naosha* (sal ammoniac), and white alum. Grind into powder, boil with river water and vinegar for three days, then place in a silver vessel with four *liang* of *yan*. Nurture for one *liang* of time. Adhesive layer medicine: three *qian* of *danfan* (chalcanthite), half a *liang* of *xipeng* (borax), and one *qian* of cinnabar. Grind these three into powder, mix with honey, apply, and nurture with fire for seven days before removing to stir-fry.

**Herbal Vessel Method**
Use equal parts of *nanxing* (arisaema), *langdu*, *wujia pi* (acanthopanax bark), *jingjie* (schizonepeta), *huangqin* (skullcap), *huanglian* (coptis), *diyu*, *chuanjiao*, and *huangshukui* (yellow hollyhock). Grind into powder, mix with honey to form a paste, place in a box, and seal. Refine with three *liang* of fire, nurture for seven days. Then boil two *liang* of *momei* (dark plum), two *liang* each of white alum, white *yan*, and *wubei*. Grind these three into powder, boil for one *fu* period with river water, then remove to wash and stir-fry with four *liang* of fire. Pour mercury twice, nurture with two *liang* of fire for three days. Repeat this pouring process only twenty times, avoiding the sprouting stage.

**Furnace-Refining Method**
Place one *liang* of *huangdan* (lead oxide) in a pot first, with the sprout in the center, then cover with half a *liang* of *huangdan*. Place in the furnace, fan into liquid, remove, break the crucible, and form a single treasure.

**Ge the Immortal’s Nine-Turn Divine Sand Gold Elixir**
**Shell-Shedding, Womb-Changing Divine Sand Method**
Take five *liang* of cinnabar, two *liang* each of sulfur and *qingyan*, two and a half *liang* of *wubei*, and three and a half *qian* of *naosha*. Combine with cinnabar, boil in rice vinegar for one period. If the liquid evaporates, add more vinegar and continue boiling. Remove the cinnabar and use *danfan* as the adhesive layer.

**Boiling Chalcanthite Method**
Take two *liang* of duck-beak *danfan*, one *fen* of *poxiao* (mirabilite), two *liang* of edible *yan*, and two *liang* of mercury. Grind these four ingredients together, steam overnight, then place in a raw iron pan. Boil with river water over a charcoal fire until bubbling. If the liquid reduces, replenish with hot water—never use cold water. Boil continuously for a day or half a day, then use an iron spoon to scoop mercury from the pan’s bottom. When it forms sand, stop. Discard the remaining medicine, retaining only the mercury sand. Wash with water, dry with paper, and reuse. Wrap the sand in two layers of paper to absorb excess mercury, then separate the sand into individual pieces. Place the sand in a clean iron pan, cover with a *jian* bowl, seal the bowl’s edges with paper, and place over a slow fire. After a long while, remove from heat and retrieve the sand. The truly dead sand will settle as purple chunks at the pan’s bottom, while the undead will fly onto the bowl. Grind the dead sand into powder, mix with honey-boiled cinnabar, and coat the mercury sand evenly. Then wrap with three-seven mother sand.

**Forming Three-Seven Mother Sand Method**
Take three *qian* of *shanzeyin* (mountain-marsh silver) powder and seven *qian* of mercury. Grind these two together to form sand, then thinly and evenly coat the honey-treated cinnabar pieces. If the summer heat prevents solidification, repeat the process. Spread cinnabar in an iron pan as before, cover with a purple bowl, seal the edges with damp paper, and place over a slow fire to expel excess mercury. Once fully expelled, add five *liang* of *shanzeyin* powder to cover the cinnabar, then top with one *liang* of *huangdan*. Alternatively, use eight *liang* of silver powder and two *liang* of *huangdan*, seal the edges with salt-clay, dry, place in an ash pit, and nurture with four *liang* of mature charcoal fire from the *yin* hour for three days and nights.

Once the nurturing period is complete, remove the cinnabar, discarding the silver powder. This marks the first cycle, wherein the common matrix is purged, and the Mother is no longer used.

**Method for Adding Mercury, Nurturing with Fire, and Harvesting Yellow Sprouts**
Take three *liang* of Mother Sand refined into cinnabar and place it back into the vessel. Add two *liang* of mercury, pouring it over the cinnabar, then seal and allow to dry. Place in the ash pit, using five *liang* of charcoal, with four *liang* of mature fire arranged atop the vessel, and cover with ash. After noon, replenish with another four *liang*. By the end of the first watch, add more. Replenish at three intervals—morning, evening, and night—for three days and nights. Open the vessel to inspect: if yellow sprouts have formed atop the cinnabar, add one *liang* of mercury, reseal, and nurture with fire for another three days and nights. Examine again for yellow sprouts. Once sprouts appear around the vessel’s rim, pour an additional twenty-four *liang* of mercury, nurture, and harvest. Collect these for the Great Elixir, transforming them into the elixir.

**Method for Transforming the Great Elixir**
Do not remove the sprouts that have formed within the vessel. Instead, pour four *liang* of mercury into it and seal the seams with red halloysite. First, place a water jar beneath the vessel, positioning the vessel over its mouth. Fill the space with paper ash, ensuring a two-inch layer atop the vessel. Arrange four *liang* of mature fire on top. Replenish the fire at the *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours, using no more than four *liang* each time. Nurture thus for two and a half days, then remove the water jar and refill it. Continue this process for a total of five days and nights. Open the vessel and pour in another four *liang* of mercury, maintaining the same fire regimen. Nurture for one month, repeating this six times, each with four *liang* of mercury—totaling twenty-four *liang*. Upon opening the vessel, harvest the yellow sprouts that have ascended to the top, collecting eight *liang*, ten *liang*, or even one *jin*, and store them separately for the Great Elixir’s nurturing, where they will transform through the surging spring. The remaining sprouts at the vessel’s base, which have not ascended, are unusable; combine them with the original cinnabar and refine them with herbal decoctions to form a usable product.

**Method for Refining the Nine-Turn Golden Elixir and Its Consumption**
**First, Pass the Yellow Sprouts Through the Flowery Pool to Transform the Great Elixir’s Fire Regimen**

**Secret of the Flowery Pool**
To transmute dry mercury into silver,
Rely on salt and acid as the master.
With fierce flames of saltpeter and alum,
Swiftly transcend the mortal to attain the sacred truth.

Borax, saltpeter, white alum, and table salt—one *liang* each.
Grind these four ingredients finely and place them in a crucible, layering them evenly above and below. Position the previously harvested yellow sprouts in the center. Mix half a bowl of paper mulberry juice with one *sheng* of rice vinegar, then gradually drip the mixture onto the medicine until the mercury permeates the base. Cover with a purple bowl and wait until all the vinegar is exhausted. Apply intense fire to drive off moisture, then seal tightly and continue heating until the contents are thoroughly dried and charred. Reduce the fire, allow to cool, and remove for washing.

**Second Washing Secret**
The purple robe and silver belt gleam bright,
Seal the vessel’s mouth—do not disclose this lightly.
With *hanfangji* as aid,
Grind the sprouts together in water.

Purple grass, lime, *hekou* pepper, and *hanfangji*—one *liang* each.
Combine these four ingredients and decoct them in a strong infusion of *shanglu* root in a clay pot, yielding three bowls of liquid. Strain and use this medicinal water to wash the sprouts that have already passed through the Flowery Pool. Do not use plain water. Place the sprouts in a purple bowl and gently heat to dry them, ensuring all moisture is expelled. Then, cleanse them thoroughly and expose them to the open air for one night to absorb the harmonious *qi* of Heaven and Earth before returning them to the furnace.

**Secret of the Surging Spring’s Longevity Fire**
After the yellow sprouts have undergone the Flowery Pool and one washing, expose them to the open air for one night to receive the harmonious *qi* of Heaven and Earth. Then place them back in the vessel, seal as before, and nurture them. Every five days, pour in four *liang* of mercury. The regimen requires two and a half days with water below and fire above, followed by two and a half days with water above and fire below, completing the five-day cycle of water and fire.

When water is below, fill a jar with water, place the vessel over its mouth, and bury it in a ceramic container filled with paper ash. Apply fire above. When fire is below, use an iron tripod to support the vessel, placing the fire beneath and a water jar atop the vessel. This alternates water and fire above and below.

When applying fire at the *yin* hour, use one *liang* of mature fire and observe for three hours. The next day, use two *liang*. Gradually increase to sixteen *liang*, then reduce the fire back to one *liang*—this is the method of accelerating the fire. If a day is missed, compensate accordingly. After a full month of nurturing, use only one *liang* of fire daily—this is the gradual progression of fire. By adjusting the fire thus, the mercury will never be exhausted. Additionally, invert the sprouts.

When inverted sprouts manifest as five-colored purple powder, harvest the purple powder that forms atop the vessel upon each opening and store it in a silver container. Place it in a sacred chamber’s crucible to transform into the Great Elixir. Collect the remaining sprouts as treasures. After fifteen days, perform another Flowery Pool washing—this is also beneficial.

Master Bao Zhenren said:
Without the Flowery Pool, the result will not be refined;
Even if powder forms, it will scatter when burned.
This aligns with the principle.

For all fire-nurturing methods, follow this secret without deviation, and transformation will naturally occur, attaining spiritual communion with the Dao of creation.
As the *Book of Changes* states: *"The waxing and waning of the sun and moon follow the celestial course."*
This is the hidden secret of the Surging Spring’s fire regimen, preserved within Wei Boyang’s *Triple Concordance*.

When the Five Colors enter the Purple River Cart, follow the regimen of nurturing the Surging Spring—each time you water the open-and-close, suddenly the entire vessel sprouts buds: some purple, some jade-green, some like tea-dust, some purple-red, some white-glowing, or their original hue. If you encounter the yellow-earth color or golden hue in the process of attaining immortality, these are the true auspicious colors. Without fail, after each watering, transfer them to the crucible. If the purple powder has not yet been collected, verify the secret of the Five Colors.

The *Golden Elixir Formula of Lord Yin the True* states:
Cinnabar is called "lush green,"
Yet without the elixir, one cannot consume it.
The celestial and terrestrial patterns form,
The yin-yang numbers are then complete.
Above coils the Yellow Dragon,
Below crouches the White Tiger.
One substance bears five colors,
Eternally serving as the immortal’s bounty.

Master Purple Radiance also said:
The Purple Dragon coils atop,
The White Tiger contains essence and qi.
Those who close their doors to study
Do not stray from the *Triple Concordance*.

In general, when cultivating the elixir, if you see the Five Colors manifesting as "dust in a bright window," this is the numinous transformation of the elixir. When the open-and-close vessel reveals the Five Colors, take refined silver and hammer it into a thin sheet—one, two, or three pieces—matching the size of the vessel containing the Yellow Sprout. Make the edges thick and the center thin, then press it onto the cinnabar vessel as a lid. Continue the daily fire-nurturing as before, and naturally, purple powder will form on the silver sheet. Every five days, open the vessel and use a goose-feather brush to gather the powder into a silver container. When you have collected two taels, transfer it to the sacred chamber for further transformation. The purple powder will naturally ascend in qi and coalesce—not as cinnabar or mercury in substance, but as their quintessence.

**Method for Transforming Purple Powder in the Sacred Chamber**
Fashion a vessel from fine silver and place the purple powder inside—two, three, or four taels. First, take three qian of fine gold, hammer it into foil, and cut it into pieces. Place them in a small crucible, heat the gold until slightly red, then remove the crucible. Quickly pour in seven qian of mercury, immediately stirring with an iron rod to form cinnabar. Wash the cinnabar-mercury with hot water, dry it with paper, and shape it into three pellets. Steep them in a strong solution of wood-ash lye mixed with dew-water, boiling for half a day or a full day until firm, then remove. Bury the pellets within the powder in the silver vessel, then place the vessel in an ash bath. Nurture with civil and martial fire for seven days. Remove the cinnabar pellets, refine them in a qi furnace to form a treasure—without the slightest loss. This powder is numinous.

The sacred chamber is none other than the silver vessel. It must be encased in a sand vessel, sealing the silver vessel within, before being nurtured with civil and martial fire—six taels each morning and evening.

If the purple powder is not further transformed to nurture the golden cinnabar, this treasure may be consumed directly. Grind the purple powder into a fine powder, mix it with paper-mulberry juice to form pills the size of sesame seeds, and let them dry. Coat them in yellow wax, wrap them in silk, and soak them in flowing water for forty-nine days—or in fresh well water. Only after soaking may they be taken: one pill on an empty stomach, washed down with well-flower water. Consuming this elixir repels all malevolent influences, bestows longevity and bliss, and grants the status of an earthly immortal. Your bones and marrow will become as unyielding as metal and stone, and your numinous transformations will be indestructible.

If the purple powder, resembling "dust in a bright window," is not yet ready for consumption, subject it to nine further transformations of the Golden Elixir to nurture the Great Medicine into spiritual communion.

**First Transformation: Golden Liquid Returning Elixir**
How many refine lead and mercury?
The numinous path grows ever more subtle.
Cold forests deepen with green waters,
Red powder flows with the waves.
Refined into true gold’s hue,
Its radiance gleams like autumn moonlight.
Guard it well with you,
Lest it slip away to the mundane.

Master Purple Blossom said: Harvest the Yellow Sprout finely, wash it with water, and let the particles that float with the water enter the crucible to nurture the Great Medicine. Follow the previous method of fire-nurturing, advancing and retreating with water and fire—there is another transformation for the water-washed portion. The particles that do not float with the water become white cinnabar, which can be refined into treasure. The portion that floats with the water is gold—the golden essence of the Yellow Sprout.

**Second Transformation: Method for Adding Mercury to the Yellow Sprout to Produce Medicine**
Cold springs flow with white snow,
Adding mercury, sprouts anew.
Honey-sealed in the golden crucible,
Burned into purple chrysanthemums.
Fragrant leaves take flight,
Gradually coalescing into blossoms.
Few know this path,
Forgetting worldly cares, one must not boast.

Master Leaf said: First, wash five taels of white cinnabar Yellow Sprout with water, then place it in the Flowery Pool and add five taels of mercury. Rest it upon water to form cinnabar pellets. Arrange them in the crucible, seal it tightly, and place it in the furnace. Nurture with civil and martial fire for one day and night. Then add another five taels of mercury, following the previous fire regimen, and nurture for seven days—all will become treasure, further attaining spiritual communion.

**Third Transformation: Refining the "Dust in a Bright Window" to Cultivate the Six Qi**
How many numinous transformations?
The true adept acts as the supreme matchmaker.
Cold clouds stretch to the earth’s axis,
The yin tiger spurs the yang thunder.
Two qi surge as blue radiance,
Three peaks pile with jade snow.
Harmonizing the true wondrous principle
Requires the催 of the Great Yang.

Take two taels of "dust in a bright window" and one tael of raw sulfur. Grind both finely, place them in a crucible, with the "dust in a bright window" lining the bottom and top, and the sulfur-dust mixture in between. Cover with more "dust in a bright window," seal it tightly, and place it in the furnace. Nurture with fire for five days. Remove and grind everything into a fine powder. Then add five taels of raw sulfur, grind it finely, mix with paper-mulberry juice to form pills the size of mung beans. Each pill can transmute one tael of mercury into treasure. If it lacks numinosity, nurture it for another twenty-one days.

**Fourth Transformation: Refining the "Dust in a Bright Window" to Cultivate the Purple River Cart**
Gather the sun’s essence,
Purify the heart to refine the purple sprout.
The Jade True One is not far,
Abide in the Dao, and the Dao has no bounds.

The jade laughter piles into treasure,
Yellow gold fills my home.
Yet it is the inner treasure of the heart,
How could it be used for arrogance or extravagance?

To the right: Take five taels of "dust in a bright window" and place it within the divine chamber—the Chamber of the Great One. Use five taels of mercury, shaped like lotus seeds, nestled within the "dust in a bright window." Seal tightly with honey, then place it in the furnace as before. Nurture with fire for seven days until all becomes true sprouts, forming strands. When melted, it becomes gold of the finest hue; that which flies to the top of the crucible is the powder of the Purple River Cart.

**Fifth Transformation: The Purple River Cart Transmutes into Yellow Ascension**
Yellow Ascension is the true Dao,
Its transformations flow like a river’s ford.
Do not speak of it to the common folk,
Keep its mysteries hidden, do not reveal them.
Refine the essence, temper the gold ten thousandfold,
Consumed, it dispels the three spirits.
The true congeals in the wondrous source of the Dao,
Only then may one approach the Celestial Lord.

To the right: Take five taels of the Purple River Cart, grind it finely into powder, and place it within the divine chamber. Seal as before, then nurture with fire in the furnace for forty-nine days. Remove, and it will have transformed into Yellow Ascension. Grind it into powder, mix with paper-mulberry juice to form pills the size of hemp seeds, coat them with yellow wax, and soak in water for forty-nine days to dispel the fire toxin. Take one pill on an empty stomach with weak wine. This elixir can restore the hun and po, reviving the dead.

**Sixth**
Grind the Yellow Ascension into powder and place it within the divine chamber’s crucible. Nurture with fire for twenty-one days, then remove and grind finely. Mix with jujube pulp to form pills the size of soybeans. Take one pill daily on an empty stomach with wine or well-flower water. For those with yang decline, qi exhaustion, or spirit disarray, it fortifies yang, restores vitality, and redoubles strength, reversing aging and restoring youth—its efficacy is unfathomable.

**Seventh: The Divine Transformation of the Purple Gold Elixir**
Place the powder of the Purple River Cart back into the divine chamber and nurture with fire for forty-nine days.

**Eighth**
Nurture for one year, then open the furnace to separate and gather the five elixirs. Return them to the golden crucible and nurture with fire for consumption.
First named the Great Dragon-Tiger Elixir,
Second named the Divine Talisman White Snow,
Third named the Purple Tenuity Elixir,
Fourth named the Gold-Purple Elixir,
Fifth named the Golden Liquid Minor Numinous Elixir,
The ninth transformation is called the Golden Liquid Minor Return Elixir.

**Ninth**
The golden body arises naturally,
Hun and po unite in nature’s bond.
Open the furnace, the white snow takes flight,
The crucible brims, the red lotus unfolds.
Once a wandering traveler,
Now an immortal ascending with one’s abode.
The whole household roams the Purple Palace,
Rising to heaven in broad daylight.

To the right: Follow the steps in order, return to the golden crucible, and nurture with fire for one year. Purify body and mind, perform rites to thank heaven and earth, then open the furnace and remove the crucible. Gather the various elixirs—those that congeal into a true crimson hue are called the Great Dragon-Tiger Return Elixir. Consumed, it allows one to ascend to heaven in daylight, spiritually roam the Purple Palace, transforms chickens into phoenixes and dogs into dragons. This elixir revives the desiccated, restoring life to the dead. If the crucible’s contents all congeal into a red hue resembling lotus flowers, it is called the Purple Tenuity Elixir. If it remains purple without changing into other colors, it is called the Purple Gold Elixir. If the crucible’s contents all gleam with a golden radiance, it is called the Golden Liquid Minor Return Elixir.

**Celestial Treasure Longevity Divine Talisman Repository**
Take one catty of fine northern stone rouge as the standard. Remove stone debris, then use the roots, leaves, and flowers of *Orostachys fimbriatus* pounded into natural juice. Place the rouge in a silk bag, suspend it within a porcelain jar, and simmer over a slow fire for five days and nights—do not let the fire grow too strong. Avoid all iron implements. Once the time is complete, remove and place it in a jar, lining the bottom and top with the original herb dregs. Seal tightly and nurture with fire for seven days: three days with four taels of fire, three days with six taels, and one day with eight taels. Test the fire’s submission by placing a probe at the bottom. Remove, then calcine in a water-and-fire crucible until it melts into liquid. Remove, skim off the surface ash, and purify. Place in a sand jar and nurture for fourteen days, covering the top with the original dregs’ ash. For the first seven days, use three taels of fire; for the next seven days, four taels. Once complete, remove to form the repository.

**Divine Transformation White Snow**
Take four taels of frost powder from two crucibles as the standard. Boil in ginger juice for half a day, then shape into five-mace pieces, splitting them into thin slices. Lightly coat with honey, mix with raw yin, and for each tael, wrap in mother foil. Place in the repository and nurture for twenty-one days. The nurturing method requires observing the divine talisman’s essence and potency. Test on the fourteenth day—if the surface blackens, it is not yet complete. After twenty-one days, if the hun does not perish, extend the time and carefully monitor the fire’s timing. Use one tael of bone and one and a half mace of white snow to achieve the full treasure’s hue. If the fire’s power is sufficient, one mace can transmute one tael. If transmutation is desired, use the repository as the Longevity Repository to nurture the frost powder. If transmutation is not desired, employ another method to nurture the frost powder into a repository, extracting the frost powder as "dust in a bright window."

**White Snow Repository**
Take one catty of nurtured frost powder as the standard and place it in a sand jar with four taels of cinnabar. Boil with *Orostachys fimbriatus* for seven days, then place in the repository and nurture for seven days. Each day at dawn and dusk, monitor the fire: three days with three taels, three days with three and a half taels, and one day with four taels—until the cinnabar is truly dead. If mercury frost is not desired, follow the previous method for fourteen days; one mace can transmute one tael of silver.

**Congealing Frost**
Grind four taels of cinnabar into powder, then boil one tael of cinnabar with *Orostachys fimbriatus* for five days. Place in the repository, securing the ball with silk, and cover the top and bottom. Nurture for eight days: two days with two taels of fire, three days with three taels, and three days with four taels. Extract the cinnabar and use one tael of female mercury, boiling it with *Akebia quinata* for one day—replace when it turns black. Repeat this process ten times, then finely grind the female mercury and nurture together for seven days: two days with two taels of fire, three days with three taels, and two days with four taels. Again, finely grind the cinnabar and female mercury, then nurture for seven days. Once the fire nurturing is complete, extract one tael of the male’s refined essence, boil it with radish juice for one day, grind evenly, and combine all three substances. Nurture for seven days with the same fire regimen as before.

Again take one tael of refined sulfur, broken into pea-sized pieces, and boil it with *Tiankujia* for one day. Combine with the previous four substances and nurture for seven days with four taels of fire. These four substances will then become full-color gold.

For the transformation, take four taels of the Four Spirits as the standard measure, use six mace of thin mother sheets, and one tael four mace of mercury. Soak them together overnight, then grind into granules and form eight pills. Place them into the previous vessel, seal tightly, and set in an ash pool. Nurture for ten days with five taels of fire each day. Retrieve to obtain the most refined red gold.

For the communion with the Dao, take four taels of the extracted gold and hammer it into a single box. Take two taels of cinnabar, boil it with *Akebia quinata* for five days, then nurture it within the box for seven days with four taels of fire each day. Repeat this process to extract eight taels. Retrieve and for every tael of mercury, use one mace of cinnabar to form the supreme treasure.

**Method for Sprinkling:**
Mix tea powder with vinegar to a smooth paste, shape into small crucibles, and place mercury inside. Use one mace of elixir powder as the base, covering above and below. Seal with salt and place in a *jianzhan* bowl. Apply two catties of fire in one firing to produce full-color purple gold. This is the inner attainment of those who possess the Dao, capable of transmuting and refining the Great Elixir—an ability beyond ordinary men. Yet the utmost sincerity and dedication to aiding the poor are paramount.

**Infant and Womb of the Eight Perfected:**
Take two taels of high-quality cinnabar and one tael of raw sulfur, wrapping them separately. Boil in the pure juice of *Akebia quinata* for seven days. If unavailable, substitute with *Xuangong*, which is also highly effective. Retrieve and place the sulfur in an iron pan to stir-fry, then stir-fry the cinnabar with plant residue until the sulfur is exhausted. Use four mace of mother metal to form pearls, mix evenly, then take a black hen’s egg, hollow it out, and place the cinnabar and pearls inside. If the egg is insufficient, use additional eggshells to cover. Seal with egg white and *Kunlun* paper, wrapping seven layers, then secure with yellow mud to seal all seams. Crush eight catties of raw lead and place it above and below the egg, using an iron fork to hold the egg in place to prevent it from rising. Seal the vessel with tiles and cover with ash fire, applying gentle fire on all sides until the lead and tin melt. Maintain this fire regimen for seven days, then retrieve and remove the mother metal. Use half a tael of cinnabar powder placed inside a goose egg as a lining. Combine with ten taels of qi from the union of nine and one, place inside the goose egg, and nurture in a lead vessel for seven days as before. Retrieve, and the sprouts will emerge—a treasure of boundless creation. If no goose egg is available, take two taels of cinnabar and place it in a fifty-tael crucible or iron pot, then pour four taels of mercury inside. Follow the seven-day counter-pouring method to refine the mature substance into treasure, yielding endless creation and the sprouts of longevity. Even when mature, it may be divided into vessels. Those who possess the Dao will surely comprehend its transmutation.

**Plum-Nucleus White Silver Method:**
First, take one tael of black lead and one tael of mercury, place them together in a crucible, and stir-fry into granules. Next, wash and pound *Huanghua Diding* grass to extract its natural juice. Take one tael of cinnabar, purify it with lodestone to draw out iron-like impurities, then boil in the grass juice for a full day and night. Retrieve, dry in the sun, and bake until finely powdered. When using, take a *wubeizi* gall, measure its capacity, and if it holds two mace, first place one mace of cinnabar powder inside, then add half a portion of silver mother, followed by one mace of mercury granules. Seal the opening with pitch, then secure with *guanni* mud and red halloysite. Mark the opening of the *wubeizi* with a brush, dry in the sun, and place it in an iron incense burner. First, fill half the burner with powdered incense, place the *wubeizi* inside, then fill the rest with powdered incense and press firmly. Burn it at nightfall, and by dawn, retrieve the cooled ash. Break it open to reveal the treasure within.

**Collected Writings on the Metal Dao, Scroll Seven, Completed**

**The Nine-Turned Divine Cinnabar Elixir of Ascension to Immortality, Formula of the Perfected Lord Xu**

The Formula states:
Take four taels of transparent sulfur and first boil it with the juice of *Shuitian Gongzi* grass (the large floating duckweed on water, with round leaves and a cross-shaped vein pattern) for three full days. If unavailable, use *Qumai* powder boiled in river water, which is also effective. For the mercury, take one tael of *Guan Zhong*, one tael of *Wubei*, and one *fen* of transparent pine resin. Grind these three ingredients into a fine powder, then boil with strong vinegar over a slow fire for half a day until it congeals into a paste. Remove the coagulated mercury, then take an iron pan, pound fresh ginger to extract its natural juice, and boil the mercury for another half day. Once dry, place the sulfur over a gentle and strong fire to melt it into liquid. Remove from the fire, pour into the coagulated mercury, and stir slowly with an iron spoon until it forms a blue-gold head. Next, grind finely with a willow wood mallet, then stir-fry over a slow fire, ensuring no ghostly flames arise. Continuously sprinkle with a willow branch dipped in sour vinegar for seven *shi* (twelve-hour periods) before stopping. For example, begin stir-frying at the *yin* hour and alternate workers until the *shen* hour. Once the cinnabar granules are mature, place them in a water-and-fire vessel for forging. At this time, it is crucial to eliminate any stray mercury to obtain firm and solid divine cinnabar.

A poem says:
Two eights unite yin and yang,
The noble man examines them in detail.

The harmonious blending transforms myriad changes,
The old woman weds Liu Lang.

**Method for Forging the Ding-Crucible**
The crucible should be fourteen inches deep, with three mountains protruding externally. The water basin at the bottom must not be too thick—only about one grain of rice in thickness is standard.

**Method for Constructing the Furnace**
Use wide bricks to first build a base one foot high, then apply a layer of clay on top, with height and width adjusted as needed. The third tier should be approximately three feet high. At the base, create a wind gate measuring one foot six inches in both length and width. The lowest tier of the furnace holds the iron crucible. The two tiers above are where the fire is applied. Leave one foot of empty space at the bottom. On the left, make a square door; on the right, a round door—these correspond to the sun and moon. The doors should be eight inches wide, aligning with the *mao* and *you* hours of the second eight. The main passage is built with two doors on the left and right, for winds are stronger from the east and west and weaker from the south and north.

**Method for Loading Refined Cinnabar into the Crucible**
Take the previously stir-fried cinnabar with the blue-gold head, grind it two to three thousand turns, then place it into the crucible. Mix red halloysite with sour vinegar and apply it to the three mountains of the crucible. Next, place the water basin of the crucible below, uniting heaven and earth, and seal the seams securely. After one night, place it into the furnace’s basin, then into the water furnace, adding water and fire. Ensure the water does not overflow, and the fire should not be too high. Initially, apply three *jin* of fire. When the water reduces by one or two shallow measures, add hot water. Then apply one to two more *jin* of fire, and when the water reduces by about three shallow measures, continuously replenish it until five *shi* (twelve-hour periods) have passed. Next, increase the fire to five *jin* and forge once. When the fire reaches fifteen *jin* and is fully applied, cease forging. Remove from the cold furnace and proceed with the subsequent methods.

Generally, if the refined cinnabar is not firm and solid, or if stray mercury remains, it will not become a treasure. If the nurturing is not continuous, the cinnabar’s color will not stabilize, and the cinnabar will "swallow its mother." All these flaws arise from the blue-gold head not being sufficiently stir-fried. If sulfur is not properly controlled, mercury will not form. If mercury is not coagulated, the work will not succeed. If the water and fire are too intense, the fire’s power is insufficient, or the thickness of the crucible’s bottom is unknown, all will fail. The water-and-fire crucible must be made of iron to avoid the risk of damage.

Lord Laozi said: "The primal essence of *jia* and *geng* is called blue-gold. When placed in the furnace and crucible, if fifteen *jin* of fire are used, and the *jiji* (water-fire balance) is maintained for one *fu* (twelve-hour period), heaven and earth will be fully united, and refined cinnabar will form. It must be firm and solid—this is the way. The fifteen *jin* of fire correspond to nine hundred years, fifteen cycles of the great yang, and the number of the *jiazi* cycle. In one day and night, there is the transformation of nine hundred years, and mercury becomes cinnabar. Within it lies the union of *li* (fire) and *kan* (water). The innate red color of mercury belongs to yang. Thus it is said: When *kan* and *li* unite, the *jiji* refining is complete. Water, fire, metal, and earth merge into one transformation. This distinction is made to reveal the true Dao."

A poem says:
Five *jin* of *jiji* in the palace of *kan* and *li*,
The work of unity is complete, the body firm and red.
Within, observe the power of yin and yang’s union,
Ninety days of *jiazi* complete one cycle.
When forging, the great fire’s spirit penetrates,
Stored for a thousand years, it does not decay.
If consumed, longevity and extended life are attained,
Knowing one method, all things become clear.

**Recipe for Boiling Refined Cinnabar**
Take the refined cinnabar forged in the crucible, cut it into pieces the size of pearls with a knife, and place them in a bamboo basket. Suspend it in a solution of mulberry ash and boil for three days and nights—use a new iron pot. Add the following ingredients:

- One *liang* of alum
- One *liang* of Sichuan pepper (remove the seeds)
- One *liang* of refined salt
- Two *qian* of chalcanthite
- Two *qian* of realgar

Grind the above five ingredients in order, add strong vinegar, and boil the refined cinnabar for three days and nights—longer is even better. Bathe in Sichuan pepper decoction, remove the medicinal residue, and dry thoroughly before use.

Lord Laozi said: "Why boil it? Because the sulfur and mercury must be rendered inert. Only then is boiling applied. These five numinous medicines correspond to the true five phases—this is the medicine that renders sulfur and mercury inert, hence called the five numinous ones. Boiling with mulberry ash controls sulfur. When sulfur is inert, mercury dies. Thus, by rendering sulfur inert, mercury can then be rendered inert. Once inert, what use is sulfur? Yet sulfur can be made and refined, possessing this great merit."

A poem says:
Yin and yang restrain each other to form gold,
Relying entirely on the mulberry lord to aid the poor.
Refined through nine works, it gains transformative power,
All by the cinnabar’s virtue, one meets the immortal lords.

**Method for Making the Receptacle**
Take one *jin* of *shanze* (mountain and marsh) ore, boil it into a liquid, add powdered lotus leaves, and stir. Remove from the fire and stir until it forms fine beads, then pour into water. Wash away the ash and sift to collect the finest original grains. If larger grains are used, the receptacle will not be numinous. Grains the size of millet should allow for breath—this also depends on a good "mother." If the mother is not good, the work will be difficult to complete.

A poem says:
When child and mother are truly numinous, they commune with transformation,
If the child is numinous but does not bond with the mother,
The great medicine, once made, must be cherished,
Lest one wander lost paths and suffer hardship.

Use four *liang* of mother to nurture one *liang* of child as the standard. The refined cinnabar must be separated by a "body-adhering medicine," layered within the receptacle, ensuring full coverage. Seal the opening, place it in an ash pit, and apply fire to nurture it, allowing it to receive numinous *qi*.

**Body-Adhering Medicine**
- Four *qian* of transparent flake chalcanthite, ground
- One *qian* of foreign sulfur, ground, boiled in water-field grass juice for seven *fu*

Stir-fry the two ingredients in a new pan until the color turns purple, then stop. Once cool, grind into a fine powder. Mix the refined cinnabar with strong vinegar until moistened, then roll it in the medicinal powder until fully coated. Next, wrap each piece tightly with silver foil and place it into the receptacle using the lotus-layering method.

Lord Laozi said: "Why use minerals like sulfur and chalcanthite as the body-adhering medicine? These two medicines are the root origin of rendering mercury inert. Mercury, upon seeing chalcanthite, can become powder; upon seeing sulfur, it can become cinnabar. Thus, both are used without losing their principle."

A poem says:
When Metal and Wood intermingle in the Fire Palace,
One must seek the *mao-you* hours to harmonize their union.
After seven cycles beyond the Heartless Maiden’s realm,
Invite Master Liu to ascend the azure void.

**Method for Nurturing in the Ash Pool and Fire Timing**
Once placed in the receptacle and sealed, bury the vessel in an ash pool filled with five *dou* of paper ash. Position the medicinal container at the center, supported by an iron tripod to elevate it. Cover the vessel, leaving a three-*cun* opening at the top. At the *mao* and *you* hours each day, add two *liang* of fresh fire through the opening, removing the old fire. Nurture it thus for one full day and night.

On the second day, increase the fire to four *liang*. Continue in this manner for three or four seven-day cycles until the process is complete. Once cooled, remove a single piece and test it: wrap it in the flesh of a long-aged white plum, steam for the duration of a meal, then quench it in strong vinegar. If the resulting color is snowy white and the piece feels light, the sulfur has departed, leaving only inert mercury, with no loss to the "mother."

If the transformation is incomplete and the adhering medicine still shows the color of chalcanthite, it indicates the fire was too high, not that the ash’s power was insufficient. Boil sour vinegar, add the "mother" powder to the receptacle, and mix in two *qian* of white alum. Rub it vigorously in the palm, wash clean, and dry. Return it to the vessel, add five *liang* of fire, and nurture it for three days at the *mao* and *you* hours, replenishing as before. Success will be assured.

The receptacle must be cast iron, weighing approximately five *jin*, and the fire should be matured fire.

Lord Laozi said: "Why use the *mao* and *you* hours to apply fire?"
He replied: "These are the gates of the sun and moon’s rising and setting, embodying the unbroken cycle of yin and yang. When water, fire, and earth are combined with the *mao* and *you* hours, the Five Phases are complete."

A poem says:
Without essence and radiance, the child lacks spirit;
Feeding on the mother’s flesh, the child paradoxically thrives.
If one fails to grasp the subtle mechanism and its essential point,
When will the ninefold work of creation be achieved?

Lord Laozi said: "Bathe the mother in vinegar and nurture it anew. For the mother, having been assailed by the qi of mercury, sulfur, and the adhering medicine, loses its luminous essence, becoming dull and obstructed, unable to effect transformation."

After nurturing the mother to produce the child three to five times, if any loss occurs, simply replenish it in a four-to-one ratio. If one has the means, the previously nurtured cinnabar may be combined with cinnabar from other mountains and marshes, refined anew according to the prior method, with fire added and replenished at the proper times. Nurture it for seven days, and the substance will become incomparably firm. If multiple cycles are performed, its power will be vast. Once twenty or more *liang* are gathered, bathe them twice—this is called "transcending the mundane to enter the sacred."

A poem says:
The fox and hare do not nurse the horse,
Nor do the hawk and crane hatch the sparrow’s eggs.
The Golden Elixir does not depart from lead,
Yet ultimately, it does not rely on lead’s foundation.

**First Cycle**
Remove the adhering medicine and residual sulfur, along with any that has been "stolen" (i.e., lost). Use this method to refine it, and nothing will be lost. When refining *lingsha* (spiritual cinnabar) to this stage, one gradually enters the sacred realm.

A poem says:
Break and refine it again to strengthen it,
Stealing away the mysterious essence, the body returns to its natural state.
Once the countenance is perfected,
The secret of immortality is passed down from mouth to mouth.

Use lead yet do not use lead;
One must work within lead.
But when it comes time to use lead,
Using lead is still a mistake.

Take the nurtured *lingsha*, pound it in an iron mortar, and wrap it in *kun* arrow paper to form a ball. Gather whole roots and leaves of *diding* (Chinese violet), *bima* (castor bean), and *badou* (croton) in equal parts, pound them into a paste, and coat the *lingsha* ball.
