Place it in a large sand vessel, surround it with silver foil, and pack *shengwuzhi* (a sacred substance) tightly around it. Drill twenty-three holes in the *lingsha* ball, position it at the center of the vessel, seal the mouth tightly, and place it in the furnace. Apply half a *cheng* of fire and nurture it overnight.

Remove and open the vessel: if a single piece remains at the center like a silver furnace, take it out and refine it. Crush it into pearls as before.

A poem says:
The Elixir Turtle completes seven returns and nine cycles,
The Mercury Furnace’s secrets must be clearly understood.
Once black and white can effect transformation,
Bathing in the Flowery Pond, one ascends of itself.

Bathe the *lingsha*, then boil it for a day in a pot with one *sheng* of strong vinegar, half a *liang* of green vitriol, and three *qian* of nitre. Ensure it becomes tightly compacted, transforming into a new and true treasure—this is the method for the first cycle’s work.

Good has no head, the cauldron has no ears;
No medicine is used, yet it is directly controlled.
Grasp the principle of Heaven and Earth,
And carefully consider this meaning.

**Method for the Second Cycle: Transmuting Lingsha into True Essence**
Take the *lingsha* that has been separated from its mother and bathed, and prepare one *jin* of receptacle. As before, place it in the vessel, using the two-to-eight ratio. Refine the *lingsha* as previously described, then apply the adhering medicine for the white-body *lingsha*:

- Three *qian* of *fenshuang* (calomel)
- Three *qian* of *liu* (sulfur)
- Four *qian* of *eguanshi* (stalactite)
- Four *qian* of *peng* (borax)
- Two *liang* of *baijiaoxiang* (white benzoin)

Grind these five ingredients into a fine powder, mix with sour vinegar to form the adhering medicine, then wrap the *lingsha* in two layers of *kunlun* paper, securing it tightly with hemp thread. Trim the excess, place it in the first-cycle silver receptacle using the lotus-layering method, seal the mouth tightly, and bury it in the ash pool. Apply and replenish the fire according to the prior method for a full seven days.

Once cooled and the vessel opened, the *lingsha* will appear in clusters like lychee, with the sulfur, mercury, and adhering medicine fused into a single white-body silver. There is no need to pass it through the lead pool. If four *liang* of the adhering medicine are gathered, it can be used to create a "Longevity Receptacle" for *mu sha* (mother cinnabar), which may then be employed as *lingsha*.

Lord Laozi said: "This removes the mundane embryo and sheds the mortal frame. The receptacle need not use sour vinegar, nor will the mother suffer any loss. It is called the Longevity Receptacle. Thus is the *lingsha* nurtured."

If sixteen *liang* are gathered, there is no further need for the furnace; one may proceed with the method for "seed gold" and "shell removal."

The white-body silver, when two *qian* are used to transmute one *liang* of red copper, yields the supreme treasure, called *Danyang*. No further boiling or refining with *an*-type furnaces is required.

A poem says:
No mundane medium forms the white-body,
Yet it awakens, freed from its womb’s qi.
My numinous power commands creation—
*Danyang* thus ascends in merit.

**Third Transformation: Seed Gold and Shell-Removal Method**
Simply take sixteen *liang* of green gold, add half a *qian* of *que*, half a *liang* of cinnabar, grind finely, then remove and wrap one *liang* in Kunlun paper to form a block, binding it tightly with hemp thread. Encase it in the juice of paper mulberry and *wu* donkey’s milk. This is the adhering medicine from the second transformation. Apply it to a thickness of one grain of rice, place it in the white-body silver sand receptacle, seal it with lotus-patterned mud, and close the seams as before. Set it in the ash pool, replenish and advance the fire as before, and nurture it for a full three days. Upon retrieval, the gold will naturally shed its shell. Remove the dead mercury pellets, crush them, and sow in the morning to reap by evening. One *liang* of the receptacle medicine can transmute one *liang* of silver into *geng*. One *qian* of the white-body silver can transmute one *liang* of red copper into the supreme treasure.

Lord Laozi said: "Why is it called the seed gold and shell-removal method? Because it employs green gold." A poem says:
The sulfur shell parts from its skin,
The green head peers forth in sunlight.
All directions transform and shift—
Drawing the sage to shatter mortal delusion.
Though the morning sowing is seen,
The workings of creation remain unseen.
If dogs and parrots were to consume it,
They would transform into phoenixes and dragon-children.

**Fourth Transformation: Morning Sowing and Evening Reaping with Pouring Method**
Simply take the nurtured, shell-removed dead green gold pellets, crush them with an iron hammer into pieces the size of *ying* seeds, weigh out half a *jin*, and place them in a sand receptacle. Each time, pour two *liang* of mercury over them, seal the seams at the *yin* hour, and set it in the ash pool. Add five *liang* of fire, then withdraw at the *shen* hour. By the next day, upon opening, the mercury will all be dead at the bottom of the receptacle. Pour mercury once daily—this is the method for endless longevity. If half a *jin* of dead mercury is accumulated, it can be transformed into *jade laughter* and *linlang*, with wondrous transmutations.

Lord Laozi said: "What is meant by morning sowing and evening reaping? It refers to subduing two *liang* of mercury with fire, pouring in the morning and completing by evening." He further said: "How does the medicine attain such potency? By combining herbal and mineral medicines, it naturally undergoes numinous transformation—hence it is called *lingsha*. Entry into sagehood is unknowable, thus it is said to be difficult at first but easy later. If ordinary people do not grasp this principle, how can they ever gain such insight?" One *qian* of the remaining receptacle medicine can transmute one *liang* of *he* into the supreme treasure. It possesses the power of a thousand transformations and ten thousand changes.

A poem says:
Behold the merit accumulated to numinous might—
Base metals, once rebellious, now follow the true path.
Thus I transform the deviant to restore the right,
Abandoning gain and loss—truly a steadfast man.

**Fifth Transformation: Jade Laughter and Linlang Method**
Simply take five *liang* of the previously inverted green gold dead mercury, without any additional processing, place it in a receptacle, and sprinkle five *liang* of mercury over it. Set it at the bottom of an ash pool jar and advance five *liang* of fire. Each day at the *yin* and *mao* hours, replenish and advance the fire. Then use an iron tripod to elevate the medicine receptacle and nurture it with top-fire. Invert it every three days—the mercury will surge upward like *jade laughter* and *linlang*, resembling a forest of jade trees or pearl-tipped buds, faintly tinged with red, like coral. It is a true treasure to behold.

Lord Laozi said: "*Jade laughter* refers to mercury surging and coiling, congealing like a jade forest." One *qian* of the dead mercury can transmute one *liang* of *zheng* lead into the supreme treasure instantly. It possesses wondrous, numinous powers of transformation.

A poem says:

The mercury coils and congeals, intertwining of its own accord,
A solitary alchemy of divine power—how lofty the endeavor!
A hall filled with wintry snow, like *jade laughter*,
The Golden Lord, upon witnessing it, bows his divine brush.

**Sixth Transmutation: The Method for Conceiving the Five Metals, Subduing Yin-Yang, and Transmuting the False into the True**
Simply take one *liang* each of the Three Yellows, grind them, and refine for one *fu* period. Then add one *liang* of *jade laughter* powder, grind them together thoroughly, and place in a large crucible. Cover with half a *liang* of pre-refined *liu sha*, then sprinkle half a *qian* of *jade laughter* powder on top. Seal the opening and advance nine *jin* of fire, applying it in three stages until fully calcined. Cool the furnace, remove the medicine—it should appear cinnabar-red. Whether copper, iron, tin, or lead, melt five *liang* in the crucible, then add one *qian* of the Three Yellows powder. It will transmute into the supreme, purple-refined *zheng* metal.

**Method for Refining *Liu Sha* with Fire**
Take half a *liang* of *liu sha*, crush it, and place in a sand crucible. Sprinkle one *qian* of *tian qie* powder on top, seal the crucible, and wait for it to dry. Advance one *jin* of fire, calcine until glowing red, then remove with tongs and let cool. Grind into fine powder and store in a sand crucible for use.

Lord Laozi said: "Why are the Three Yellows called 'dead'? Because they transmute the false into the true. Mercury, being the essence of water, reverts to pure yang, thus it can restrain yang and transform the false into the true."

A poem says:
For love of the yellow sprout turning to white snow,
What difficulty could there be for me to ponder deeply?

The Three Primordials cherish and guard the crucible’s contents—
foolish men are not permitted to recklessly measure.

**Seventh Transmutation: Method for Congealing Mercury into Silver through Sevenfold Reversion of Sulfur**
Take eight *liang* of sulfur and two *liang* of mercury. Grind them together until black—this is the Dao of reversion and restraint. Next, add one *liang* of the previously refined Three Yellows, grind them together, and place in an amber crucible. Then, use three *liang* of Three Yellows powder to cover and seal it as prescribed. Place in an ash pit, adjust the fire daily at dawn and dusk, and advance four *liang* of fire. Nurture for seven full days. Remove and grind into powder. For each use, take one *zi* of the powder, place in a raw iron crucible, and sprinkle three *liang* of mercury over it. Apply civil and martial fire, nurture for three days, and wait for the mercury to die. Then advance three *jin* of fire, and with one firing, it will transmute into silver.

Lord Laozi said: "What is meant by the Sevenfold Reverted *Ling Sha*? Originally, eight *liang* of mercury were used, but here only two *liang* of mercury and eight *liang* of sulfur are employed—the meaning of reversion and repetition is the 'seven reversions,' which is the sevenfold transmutation."

A poem says:
The forked horns and the maiden’s form await their tryst,
Reversion and repetition, leisurely and fitting.

When the elixir matures, it undergoes wondrous inversion—mother and child unite without doubt. The eighth transmutation yields a white body that, when mixed with mercury, becomes *geng*, known as the *Eight Trigrams Geng Method*. Simply take five *liang* of the sevenfold reverted sulfur-mercury, add half a *liang* each of the finest three yellows, and one *liang* of southern borax. Grind them together until extremely fine, place in a crucible, seal the seams tightly, and set it in the ash pool. Nurture with two *liang* of fire, adjusting at dawn and dusk daily, for a full twenty-one days. Remove, grind into fine powder, and for each *qian* of the powder, mix with five *liang* of mercury to form true *geng*.

Lord Laozi said: "Why does mixing mercury yield *geng*? Because the number of the Eight Trigrams is complete, and the utmost balance of yin and yang is achieved."

A poem says:
Thus the elixir ripens in full display,
No effort spared in its toil.
A single spark of absolute yin transforms—
Who shall be my kindred soul?
If one can refine to this stage,
One shall instantly ascend in flight.

**Ninth Transmutation: The Great Method of the Immortal Elixir for Eternal Life and Ascension**
Simply take the previous *Ling Sha* elixir at each transmutation, refine it with honey into pills, and consume one pill with flowing water. Illness will be cured upon ingestion. The divine transformations of these transmutations have been described earlier—from ancient times to the present, no alchemical elixir surpasses this. The achievement of the ninth transmutation is beyond the reach of mere human effort.

Lord Laozi said: "If one can refine to this stage, a single touch can induce ascension, replacing mortal bones with those of a perfected being. Form and visage shall enter the realm of the wondrous and unfathomable. Choose a blessed highland, build an abode and altar, and prepare with fine azure silk. Daily, pay homage to the true, forge the furnace and cauldron, and use three *jin* of *Ling Sha* from the two-eight preparation, ground finely. Then take two *jin* of the eighth transmutation’s sulfur-mercury with the three yellows, combine for a total of five *jin*, and grind into dust. Place in the cauldron, calling it *Mingchuang Chen* (Dust of the Bright Window). This can be used to nurture the golden silkworm and achieve the wondrous Dao."

A poem says:
From mortal to sage, the sun and moon are probed,
Divine work rejoices in silent competence.
What are gold and jade, rank and wealth, compared to this?
The bright moon and clear breeze belong to my heart.

Lord Laozi said:
Take one *jin* each of yellow lead, malachite, mica powder, golden earth, and rock crystal. Grind these five ingredients into powder, refine with water, and mix with black donkey’s milk to coat the inner walls of the cauldron. Once dry, add the elixir, then seal the upper plate, uniting heaven and earth within the furnace. Adjust daily, nurturing with five *jin* of fire. After a full hundred days, remove and bury three *chi* underground for one year. Then suspend it in a well for another year, followed by soaking in water for a year. Retrieve and bury it underground again for one year to prevent the emanation of radiant light. Form the elixir into pills the size of a chicken’s head with sweet dew juice, then return them to the crucible to nurture with fire, adjusting for seven full days. Remove and feed one pill to a pure black dog, then cast it into a vat of freshly drawn water—the water shall boil intensely. Replace the water and soak again, repeating this with nine vats. The dog shall transform into a dragon and ascend. How much more so for a human who consumes it? After soaking in nine vats of water, one shall likewise ascend, hence the name *Ninefold Great Immortal Elixir*. Yet how can the common folk recklessly attempt such refinement? Even achieving a single transmutation allows one to consume the elixir and preserve health for extended years. No one who fails to follow heaven’s way can succeed in refining the great elixir. In the great elixir’s refinement, only three conditions ensure success:
First, innate impurities are purged, and wisdom naturally awakens.
Second, one seeks a master and the Dao, nurturing tranquility.
Third, the method aligns with the meeting of the green dragon, and actions become effortless, attracting the divine treasure’s radiance, which naturally guards and enlightens.

Of old, the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning taught Lord Laozi to comprehend heaven and earth’s creation, refine water and fire into form, unify metal and wood, and universally harmonize the myriad transformations with the Dao. Thus, all creation was established, culminating in the secret method of the great elixir. It was then transmitted to the Lord of Eastern Florescence, who passed it to the Queen Mother of the West. Thereafter, immortals transmitted it orally, without written record, through heart-to-heart instruction thrice daily. Success was achieved in nine stages. Today’s *Scripture of Purity* expounds Lord Laozi’s intent in elixir refinement—medicine is without emotion, and the world calls it formless. Thus, he taught the people to establish the *yin* startle, embodying boundless transformation.

Moreover, a verse says:
Silent and natural, rooted in origin,
Rising and falling, advancing and retreating, paired and drawn.
If it enters the belly,
One ascends to the nine heavens.
Test one or two transmutations—effects shall be seen.
But at the third transmutation,
One must act without speech.
Alas, heaven and earth’s spirits will not tolerate carelessness—beware!

In elixir texts, when "nurturing in emptiness for five to seven days" is mentioned, it refers to opening and resealing after the initial firing if the elixir is not yet mature. Then, use the empty nurturing method: reseal, wait for dryness, place in the ash pool, and suspend half an inch of ash above. Cover with a single piece of ash, using no more than two *liang* of fire, and nurture gently for five to seven days—this is empty nurturing.

**Fire Regimen**
(Not for the previous nine transmutations, but for the ninefold method of refining arsenic powder into the elixir head.)
From the first to the fourth transmutation, apply fire twice daily, two *liang* each morning and evening. On the third day, add one *liang*, making three *liang*. From the third to the sixth day, increase by one *liang*, making four *liang*.

When the fire’s intensity reaches maturity, adjust accordingly. If the heat is excessive, proceed gradually—this is optimal; the height of the ash poses no hindrance. From the fifth to the seventh transmutation, follow the standard method. After seven days, replace with four *liang* of mature fire daily, ensuring no deficiency. Do not exceed five *liang* per day until reaching the seventyfold measure of the Great Medicine, at which point proceed gently without haste; thereafter, five *liang* suffices.

**Qingxia Zi’s Sixteenfold Great Elixir**

**Boiling Cinnabar (Section Jia)**
*Sulfur, green salt:* one *liang* each
*Gallnut:* break open, remove worm-eaten fragments, wipe clean with dry cloth (avoid fire), take one and a half *liang* of powder

Grind the three ingredients together in a mortar until even, place in a sand pot, and fill to eight-tenths with sour aged rice vinegar. Suspend three *liang* of cinnabar and boil for one *fu* period. Maintain a gentle simmer like fish eyes; replenish with hot vinegar as it reduces—avoid cold vinegar. Upon completion, wash with warm water to purify.

**Forming Chalcanthite-Cinnabar Coating (Section Yi)**
*Refined chalcanthite:* five *liang*
*White lead, mercury:* one *liang* each
*Crude nitre:* one *fen*

Grind the four ingredients together until fine, with no visible specks or sound. Place in a silk bag, suspend in a porcelain vessel, and boil in river water for one day. Use an iron spoon to stir within the vessel; when the mercury has transformed into cinnabar grains, cease. Discard the remaining solution, wash the grains clean, dry, and form into a single pellet. Place in a crucible, cover with a bowl, and apply gentle fire to expel all residual mercury. Grind finely, moisten with honey, and boil with cinnabar. Wrap the pellet evenly with a layer of the mixture to form a uniform coating.

**Mercury Seal (Section Bing)**
*Mercury:* seven *qian*
*Mother (mercury residue):* three *qian*
*Pepper:* three *qian*

Grind together finely, then gently heat in pepper-infused water until the mixture becomes mud-like—this is ideal. Wash away the residue with water, dry, and press between layers of paper to remove excess mercury before applying as a body seal.

For cinnabar applied to the body or heavy-head cinnabar grains, arrange the pieces loosely in a flatiron, cover with a bowl, and apply prolonged gentle fire to expel all residual mercury until the grains solidify into firm cinnabar.

**Enclosure (Section Ding)**
*Silver pearls:* five *liang*
Wrap the cinnabar from the mercury seal in yellow wrapping, place in a yellow crucible, and mix with two *liang* of yellow lead and the juice of yellow ox hide. Seal with refined clay, allow to dry, then fire intensely until red-hot for an extended period. Remove from heat, allow to cool, grind finely, and nurture with yellow powder, covering the top with one *liang*. Seal the opening, allow to dry, place in the furnace, and cover the top with two *cun* of ash.

**Fire Regimen (Section Wu)**
Apply three *liang* of top fire, replacing at *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours. Nurture for three *sui* periods, then cease the fire. Allow to cool, remove, and peel away the cinnabar-coated silver—the cinnabar must not melt. Use for subsequent washing and rinsing.

**Testing (Section Ji)**
Arrange the fire-tamed cinnabar in a yellow crucible (or an unglazed vessel). Pour two *liang* of mercury, seal the opening, place in the furnace, and apply four *liang* of top fire, replacing at *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours. Nurture for three *mou* periods. Upon opening, if no sprouts appear, add another two *liang* of mercury and repeat the process. If still no sprouts, add another two *liang* and repeat. Sprouts will inevitably form. Then, use twenty-four *liang* of mercury for further nurturing.

**Washing and Rinsing (Section Geng)**
Do not remove the cinnabar or yellow sprouts; instead, pour four *liang* of mercury. Place the water tripod securely, position the yellow crucible atop it, cover the top with two *cun* of ash, and apply four *liang* of top fire, replacing at *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours. Nurture for five *pan* periods, removing half the ash every two *pan* periods. Lift the yellow crucible, pour cold water (or hot water) into the water tripod until full. Open the yellow crucible, add another four *liang* of mercury, and repeat the process six times. Then collect the yellow sprouts, yielding perhaps one *jin*, ten *liang*, or half a *jin*. Accumulate these for the Great Elixir, nurturing with fire to stimulate the wellspring of transformation for the Sixteenfold Great Elixir. The remaining residue that does not ascend may be combined with the earlier cinnabar. Form into a grass-sealed vessel, and with one refinement, it becomes treasure.

**Hua Chi Xin (Transformative Pool Preparation):**
*Borax, sal ammoniac, saltpeter, alum, white numinous powder, and yellow sprouts—* each one *liang*. Weigh the ingredients in equal parts, grind with milk to a fine uniformity, and layer above and below with wheat-bran paste. Mix half a *sheng* of grain juice with one *sheng* of rice vinegar, stir evenly, and pour to moisten. Apply fire to reduce by half, then pour again, repeating until the liquid is exhausted. Cover with a *jian* bowl, apply gentle fire for one *shi* period until scorched, then move to a shaded place to cool. Wash thoroughly.

**Mu Yu Ren (Bathing Preparation):**
*Sichuan pepper, white lime, purple grass,* and *Stephania tetrandra*—or, in some versions, *Dioscorea bulbifera*—weigh in equal parts. Crush coarsely, decoct in a stone vessel with flowing water to a thick liquid, then strain through layered silk. Use this to wash the yellow sprouts from the *Hua Chi* until thoroughly cleansed, avoiding raw water. Place in a *jian* bowl, apply gentle fire to dry, stir, and expose to the open air for one night to absorb the harmonious darkness of heaven and earth—this is called *Jing Lu Huang Ya* (Dew-Refined Yellow Sprouts).

**Cao Gui Kui (Herbal Seal Preparation):**
*Sichuan pepper, anemarrhena, fritillaria, scrophularia, sophora, coptis, phellodendron, rhubarb, licorice, apricot kernel, arisaema, gentian, gallnut,* and *gardenia*—pound into powder, mix with rice vinegar to form a paste, and apply to cinnabar and mercury that failed to sprout. Roll into a ball about one finger’s thickness, wrap in *Kunlun* paper, seal with refined clay, and allow to dry. Patch any leaks in the crucible. Fire with five *jin* of fuel—or three *jin*—until glowing red, then quench in water. Pound into powder, mix with rice vinegar to form a paste, and apply again to cinnabar and mercury that failed to sprout. Roll into a ball of the same thickness, wrap in *Kunlun* paper, seal with refined clay, and dry. Patch crucible leaks. Fire with five *jin*—or three *jin*—until glowing red, quench in water, and extract the molten silver.

**Dan Tou (Elixir Foundation):**
Place *Jing Lu Huang Ya* into a yellow crucible, pour four *liang* of mercury, and apply once daily. Nurture with fire for two and a half days, using *upper fire and lower water*. For another two and a half days, use *upper water and lower fire*.

After nurturing for a full five days, the cycle of water and fire is complete. For instance, when fire is above and water below, ensure the water does not dry up. If water is above and fire below, use an iron tripod: place fire beneath the base and water atop the opening (A). This is the method for harmonizing water and fire.

On chamber days, apply fire. For the first two days, use two *liang* of fire. Each day, increase by one *liang*, gradually reaching sixteen days. Then reduce the fire incrementally back to one *liang*. This completes one month’s firing regimen.

After chamber days, apply one *liang* of fire and nurture for a month—this is the method of gradual progression, ensuring the mercury never depletes.

To invert the sprouts and halt their growth, observe the five-colored purple powder. When the lid is opened, it will rise and condense into purple powder. Sweep this into a silver container to gather the Great Elixir. The remaining sprouts are stored in the *shen shi* (Spirit Chamber).

Every fifteen days, perform a "bathing" ritual to activate the transformative process. As Master Bao Zhenjun said: *"Without the Flowery Pond, it will never be refined; even if powder forms, it will scatter lightly. Only after firing will you truly understand."* Thus, the immortals guarded this secret, never revealing the firing regimen—it is the hidden art of the Golden Elixir’s transformations. Once mastered, success is assured.

The *Book of Changes* states: *"Waxing and waning, ebb and flow—such is the creation of Heaven and Earth."* As the *Cantong Qi* says: *"Within lies the gushing spring; the firing regimen nurtures the five colors into purple. Enter the Purple River Chariot’s system, and the gushing spring is cultivated."*

Each day, apply the elixir. When the lid is suddenly opened, sprouts may appear inside the container—some jade-green, some tea-colored, some purple-red, some with a white radiance—these are their natural hues. If the container is filled with yellow earth or gold, these are the true five colors. After one or two applications, transfer them to a crucible to collect the purple powder, confirming the five colors.

At this stage of refinement, the purple powder from the opened container is called *"Mingchuang Chen"* (Dust of the Bright Window)—the foundation of the Great Elixir. Upon seeing the five colors, take one or two *liang* of silver foil, hammer it thin at the edges and even thinner at the center, then embed it atop the sand container. Next, place *Huang Ya* (Yellow Sprout) inside, seal it, and apply the same firing regimen. Naturally, the powder will ascend and adhere to the foil atop the container. Every five days, open the container and sweep the powder with a goose feather into a silver vessel, collecting one, two, or four *liang*. Store it in the *shen shi* (Spirit Chamber) for further transformation. It will spontaneously ascend in spirit, coalescing into a substance of unrefined cinnabar and mercury—the essence of cinnabar and mercury.

**Method for Transforming Purple Powder into the Great Elixir in the Spirit Chamber:**
Take three parts *Geng Sha* (cinnabar), press out the free mercury, leaving exactly one *liang*. Divide this into three pills, then boil them for a day in *bing yao* (cake medicine)—or charcoal ash infusion—along with dew water until firm. Place them in a container, cover with four *liang* of purple powder, and set it in an ash jar. Apply balanced fire atop with one *liang* of fire, nurturing it during the *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours for seven cycles. It will melt into *Zimo Jin* (Purple-Ground Gold), with no loss in weight—proof of the powder’s efficacy.

The *shen shi* (Spirit Chamber) is a silver container, which must first be sealed with a sand container before placing it in the ash jar. Nurture it with one *liang* of balanced fire. If no further transformation is needed, grind it finely, mix with paper mulberry juice to form pills, and let dry. Coat them in yellow wax, then submerge in flowing water or a well for forty-nine days. Retrieve them, and take one pill with well-bloom water to ward off all malevolent influences, turning the five viscera golden—thus achieving the state of an Earth Immortal.

The Way of Transformation is too profound to describe fully.

**If the Mingchuang Chen (Dust of the Bright Window) is not yet ready for consumption, proceed with further refinement to nurture the Golden Elixir:**

**First Transformation: Refining Huang Ya into White Snow and Golden Essence**
Master Zihua said: Crush *Huang Ya* (Yellow Sprout), levigate it with water, and nurture in a crucible whatever follows the water. It will transform into the Great Medicine, with the same advancing and retreating fire regimen. Whatever does not follow the water can be melted with white gold to instantly form a treasure. What follows the water is called *Huang Ya Jin Jing* (Golden Essence of the Yellow Sprout).

**Second Transformation: Adding Mercury to Huang Ya to Produce Medicine**
Take five *liang* of *Huang Ya*, place it in the *Hua Chi* (Flowery Pond), and add five *liang* of mercury. Set it over fire to form cinnabar grains. Return it to the crucible, seal with paper, place in the furnace, and nurture with balanced fire for one *fu* (a period of time). Remove it, add five *liang* of mercury, seal, and apply the same firing regimen to produce a treasure.

**Third Transformation: Verifying and Using Huang Ya to Complete the Medicine**
Take half a *jin* each of *Huang Ya*, silver powder, and mercury, place them together in the *Hua Chi*, and temper fifty times. Remove, place in a container, seal, and apply the same firing regimen. Upon removal, one firing will produce a treasure. Every five days, apply the elixir, harvesting and refining until the mercury is inexhaustible—this is called the *Yongquan* (Gushing Spring).

**Fourth Transformation: Refining Mingchuang Chen into the Original Source of Vermilion Mercury**
Take one *liang* of *Mingchuang Chen*, place it in a crucible, then add one *liang* of coarse cinnabar. Cover above and below with *Mingchuang Chen*, then pour one *liang* of mercury over it. Seal as before, place in the furnace, and nurture with fire for forty-nine days to form a treasure. Alternatively, melt it for seven days to instantly produce gold. What ascends to the top of the crucible is called *Zihe Che* (Purple River Chariot).

**Fifth Transformation: Refining Mingchuang Chen into the Two Blacks**
Grind one *liang* each of sulfur and mercury finely, place them in a crucible, then cover with two *liang* of *Mingchuang Chen*. Seal as before, place in the furnace, and nurture with fire for five days until it turns golden or purple. Remove, grind finely, then mix with five *liang* of raw sulfur and paper mulberry juice to form pills the size of mung beans. Use one pill per *liang* of mercury to transmute it into gold.

**Sixth Transformation: Refining Mingchuang Chen into the Purple River Chariot**
Take five *liang* of *Mingchuang Chen* and place it in the *shen shi*—the *Taiyi Shen Shi* (Chamber of the Great One).

**Sixth Transformation: Refining Mercury into the Purple River Chariot**
Take five *liang* of mercury, prepare it in the manner of the *Zai Lian* method, place it within *Mingchuang Chen*, seal as before, and nurture with fire in the furnace for seven days until it forms *Huangya* (Yellow Sprout). When melted, it becomes true gold, and what ascends to the top is called *Zihe Che* (Purple River Chariot).

**Seventh Transformation: Transmuting the Purple River Chariot into Gold Liquid**
Take five *liang* of *Zihe Che*, mix with vinegar to form a paste, spread it within the vessel, bore holes, and allow to dry. Place five *liang* of mercury inside, seal as before, and nurture for seven days until it forms *Geng* (Metal Essence).

**Eighth Transformation: Transmuting the Purple River Chariot into Huangju**
Take five *liang* of *Zihe Che* and one *liang* of cinnabar, grind finely into powder, place in the *shen shi*, seal as before, and nurture with fire for forty-nine days. Remove, grind finely, and mix with paper mulberry juice to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Take one pill on an empty stomach with ash-free wine.
This elixir revives the dead and restores life, reanimates the body and revives the soul. After consuming ten pills, the *Three Corpses* depart the body. In cases of sudden death, administer half a *qian* of the elixir mixed with cold water, and the person will revive immediately. Such rebirth is no ordinary feat—how could it be achieved without divine power?

**Ninth Transformation: Refining Huangju with Xiong to Alter Substance**
Take one *liang* each of *Huangju*, cinnabar, and mercury, and four *liang* of *xiong* (realgar), grind finely, place in the *shen shi*, seal, and nurture for seven days. Remove, grind finely, and mix with jujube pulp to form pills the size of mung beans. Take one pill on an empty stomach with well-water drawn at dawn. For those suffering from *yang* depletion, blackened complexion, or mental confusion, this elixir restores youth, revives the soul, and raises the dead. Its divine efficacy is unfathomable.

**Tenth Transformation: Transmuting Iron into Gold with Xionghuang**
Place *xionghuang* in the crucible, cover with one *liang* of *Huangju* powder, seal, and nurture with fire as before for one hundred days. One pill may transmute one *liang* of iron into gold.

**Eleventh Transformation: Refining Mercury into Treasure with Zihe Che Powder**
Take one *liang* each of *Huangju* and *Huangya*, and four *liang* of cinnabar, spread them in the *shen shi*, seal, and nurture in the furnace for thirty days. Remove and use only the cinnabar, mixing it with paper mulberry juice to form pills the size of mung beans. One pill transmutes one *liang* of copper into *Huangu Dan Yang* (Bone-Transforming Yang Elixir). When sprinkled over one *liang* of mercury, it instantly becomes treasure.
One *liang* of this copper medicine may transmute one *jin* of mercury, or one *liang* into ten *liang*.

**Twelfth Transformation: Refining Huangju into the Purple Gold Elixir**
Take two *liang* of *fen shuang* (calomel), grind finely, and mix with glue to form pills the size of mung beans. Use one *liang* of *Huangju* powder to evenly cover above and below, seal as before, and nurture with fire for fourteen days. Remove. One pill, when sprinkled over one *liang* of mercury, transmutes it into treasure.
Alternatively, it may be accomplished in a single night.

**Thirteenth Transformation: Refining Purple River Chariot to Transmute the Five Metals**
Take five *liang* of *Ziheche* (Purple River Chariot), place it in the divine chamber, seal as before, and nurture with fire in the furnace for one year. The fire’s power is equal to that of the Great Elixir. Form pills with paper mulberry juice, the size of soybeans. Each pill may transmute the five metals into treasure.

**Fourteenth Transformation: Divine Alchemy of the Purple Gold Elixir**
Take *Ziheche* powder, place it in the divine chamber, seal tightly, and nurture with fire in the furnace for one year. Remove. Form pills with paper mulberry juice, the size of sesame seeds, then return them to the divine chamber, seal tightly, and nurture with fire for forty-nine days. Remove. Wrap them and place in east-flowing water. Soak for forty-nine days, then take one pill with wine free of sediment.

**Fifteenth Transformation: Verification of the River Chariot**
Take four *liang* or half a *jin* of *Ziheche*, place it in the crucible. Then cover evenly with *Huangju*, seal tightly, and nurture with fire in the furnace for a full year. Open the crucible to reveal five kinds of elixirs, then gather them. Return them to the crucible and nurture with fire for seven days before consuming the elixirs. These five are named as follows: first, *Longhu* (Dragon-Tiger); second, *Shenfu* (Divine Talisman); third, *Ziyou* (Purple Wanderer); fourth, *Zijin Dan* (Purple Gold Elixir); fifth, *Jinye Xiaohuan Dan* (Golden Liquid Lesser Return Elixir).

**Sixteenth Transformation: Differentiating the Five Elixirs**
After nurturing with fire in stages for one year, once all elixirs are complete, fast and bathe in purification, offer libations to heaven and earth, then open the crucible to retrieve the elixirs. That which congeals atop the crucible in a true crimson hue is called *Longhu Dan* (Dragon-Tiger Elixir). Consuming it allows one to ascend in broad daylight, wander the Purple Palace in spirit, transforms chicken feed into phoenixes, and turns dog food into dragons. That which forms within the crucible in flakes like fish scales with a white radiance is called *Shenfu Dan* (Divine Talisman Elixir). Consuming it revives the dead, restoring withered bones to life. That which appears pale red like the color of lotus blossoms is called *Ziyou Dan* (Purple Wanderer Elixir), or if it remains purple without changing through various hues, it is called *Zijin Dan* (Purple Gold Elixir). That which forms with a golden radiance along all edges is called *Jinye Xiaohuan Dan* (Golden Liquid Lesser Return Elixir). For all the above elixirs, form pills with paper mulberry juice, the size of sesame seeds. Once dry, wrap them in silk and soak in east-flowing water for one hundred days. Remove. Take one pill with well-flower water, then two, then three, up to four pills, to complete the dosage. With focused intent and utmost care, one will swiftly attain spiritual communion. Consuming a single pill transforms the five viscera and bone marrow into golden hues. One becomes impervious to water or fire, while tigers, wolves, snakes, and insects all flee in terror. All malevolent spirits and demons keep their distance, and through spiritual transfiguration, one ascends in broad daylight—this is the supreme and most wondrous Dao of the perfected.

*Geng Dao Ji*, Scroll Eight, concludes. #1 (Text following this point appears to be missing.)

**Geng Dao Ji, Scroll Nine**

**Western Shu Jade Cauldron Perfected One’s Nine-Cycle Great Elixir**
**First Cycle**
Take ten taels of fine cinnabar. Chop red peony root and steep it in sour rice vinegar, then boil the cinnabar for five *fu*-periods. Mix with powdered straw and honey to bind—do not overmoisten—layering and covering the cinnabar as it cooks. Seal the vessel and nurture with fire for a full seven days. Cool the furnace, remove the cinnabar, and discard the straw ash. Next, boil *qianghua* in sour vinegar for three *fu*-periods until it is subdued by fire. If it remains unyielding to the flame, prepare a receptacle for nurturing the cinnabar. Should any vapor arise, take ten taels of *shanze gen*, pound it into pearls, and layer it with the cinnabar. Seal the vessel, press salt over the lid, and bury it in an ash pit. Nurture for seven days, and the cinnabar will truly die and become treasure.

**Second Cycle**
Use the cinnabar nurtured in the previous receptacle. Boil five taels of cinnabar with the same herbs until dry, then grind it finely with three *qian* of water-borne gold powder. Knead with pure rock honey into a single cake, bind tightly with silk, and wrap in three taels of silver foil, ensuring complete tightness. Place it in the previous receptacle and nurture for seven days. Upon removal, if the cinnabar retains its unborn hue, it is ready for further refinement into the great medicine. If used in a pearl furnace, it will reveal its treasure; when applied to *danyang*, it transforms bone into supreme treasure. When poured, it sprouts buds—this water-borne gold is the mother of silver.

**Third Cycle**
Use the cinnabar nurtured in the first cycle as the receptacle. Forge a small vessel from *shanze gen* to serve as the divine chamber, leaving fine holes on all sides. Place the previous receptacle’s mother cinnabar inside the vessel. For the outer receptacle, use the cinnabar from the first cycle. Inside the vessel, add two taels of cinnabar and mercury, bury the vessel at the center of the receptacle, and nurture for seven days. Upon opening, if no mercury vapor remains and it has congealed, pour in another two taels and nurture for another seven days. The mercury will sprout buds; remove them without disturbing the vessel. Pour in another two taels of cinnabar and mercury, nurture again, and accumulate over ten taels of buds. Then bathe them.

**Bathing Method (Flower Pool):**
Grind equal parts borax, saltpeter, *pao*, green salt, and alum into powder. Line the bottom of a bamboo basket, place the buds on the powder, and cover with more powder. Mix one bowl of paper mulberry juice with one *sheng* of rice vinegar, pour over the medicine, and cover with a small dish. Simmer over low heat until dry, then seal the dish’s seams and slightly increase the fire. Nurture for about one hour, then cool before opening to complete the bath.

**Bathing Method (Herbal Wash):**
Grind one tael each of purple grass, *huangyaozi*, *hanfangji*, and *baiyou* into powder. Boil in three bowls of water to make a thick decoction, strain, and simmer the buds in the liquid for several rolls. Wash and purify them, then place in the basket. Dry over low heat and expose to the open air overnight.

**Fourth Cycle**
Crush the bathed buds to form a receptacle. Place the previous silver vessel inside, pour in five taels of cinnabar and mercury, and nurture for three days. Upon removal, the mercury will have congealed. Open the vessel, add another three taels of cinnabar and mercury, seal, and nurture for another three days. The mercury will sprout a white jade smile. Accumulate over ten taels of poured mercury to form the receptacle—this white bud smile is the raw material of supreme treasure.

**Fifth Cycle**
Use the bud sieve as the receptacle. Grind two taels of realgar and two taels of cinnabar and mercury into powder, place in the previous divine chamber, and nurture for three days. Add one tael of mercury each time, increasing to ten taels over twenty-eight days. Grind and nurture repeatedly, without counting days, until it gradually transforms into light dust. This substance cannot be drowned by water nor burned by fire. At high noon, cast a small amount into the blue sky—it will dissolve into white snow, ascending beyond measure. Accumulate this to form the receptacle.

**Sixth Cycle**
Use the dust from a bright window as the receptacle. Grind four taels of gold with half a *jin* of cinnabar and mercury, place in the divine chamber, and nurture for forty-nine days. Upon removal, it will all become gold powder.

**Seventh Cycle**
Use the gold powder as the receptacle. Grind four taels of cinnabar with half a *jin* of cinnabar and mercury, place in the previous divine chamber, and nurture for a full forty-nine days. The cinnabar and mercury will entirely transform into purple gold powder.

**Eighth Cycle**
Use the nurtured purple gold powder as the receptacle. Grind eight taels of cinnabar and mercury with four taels of realgar, place in the divine chamber, and nurture for a full forty-nine days. It will all become purple-ground gold powder. Mix with paper mulberry juice to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Each two pills can transmute one *jin* of mercury into purple-ground refined gold.

**Ninth Cycle**
Use the previous receptacle’s purple gold returning elixir. Melt one *jin* of raw iron into liquid, add one pill of the elixir, and it will resonate in the crucible, transforming entirely into purple gold. From beginning to end, mercury must be extracted from cinnabar, and realgar must be refined to its essence. For the fire timing, use two taels of mature fire at *mao* and *you*, with the fire’s separation and union maintained at roughly three *cun* from the top fire.

**Ge Immortal’s Nine-Cycle Spirit Sand Great Elixir**
**First Cycle**
Take eight taels of mercury and two taels of sulfur. Stir-fry until the sulfur’s head turns green, then place in a water-and-fire crucible to refine and ascend. Cut into blocks for use. Boil with saltpeter, *liu*, green-black alum, *huangyaozi*, thunder pill, *langdu*, *mulu*, *nanxing*, and *wujia* bark in rice vinegar for three days and nights. Bathe thoroughly, then boil in aged leaf juice for two days. Place in the mother cinnabar receptacle and nurture with fire until the color turns pure white—only then can it serve as the sacred receptacle. If not yet white, nurture for another seven-day cycle until it truly dies.

**Second Cycle**
Grind sixteen taels of truly dead spirit sand into powder, and mix with four taels of raw spirit sand. Use *jianhuang*, *yadan* alum, green spirit, white snow, and flying talismans affixed to the body. Blend with honey, coat each piece evenly, then roll in spirit sand powder. Nurture for seven days, then apply a great fire in one firing to complete the treasure.

**Third Cycle**
Take the spirit sand from the second cycle, without firing, and use it to infuse *danyang*. Each two *qian* can infuse one tael of red matter until it turns purely white. Pour into the trough, cover with damp paper—it will turn snow-white, this being the method to test the *gen* of spirit sand. If proceeding to later cycles, this step is omitted.

**Fourth Cycle**
Use only the head of the spirit sand receptacle to nurture the mother sand, following the previous method to refine spirit sand; it likewise becomes treasure after seven days.

**Fifth Cycle**
Take sixteen taels of spirit sand from the second cycle to form a receptacle, nurture four taels of cinnabar within, wrapping each piece in gold leaf. Nurture for three seven-day periods, then remove. Use one tael each of salt essence and chalcanthite, half a tael of *liuxu* alum, and a large bowl of medicinal paste. Boil the previous ingredients until dry, then place together in a crucible. In another crucible, take one tael of nurtured cinnabar and one tael of *geng* to form a liquid. Then place the previous crucible into the furnace to melt, using tongs to extract the cinnabar-*geng* liquid and pour it into the medicinal crucible. Once clarified, pour into the trough to form treasure—yielding two taels of fine, superior *geng*.

**Sixth Cycle**
Take the cinnabar nurtured within the spirit sand receptacle, free of smoke, and blend evenly with two taels each of male and female [ingredients]. Place in a sealed vessel and nurture with fire for forty-nine days, then remove. Form into pills with yellow wax, the size of a chicken’s head. Each pill can infuse one tael of *gen* from mountains and marshes into *geng*.

**Seventh Cycle**
Take sixteen taels of spirit sand nurtured within the truly dead spirit receptacle to form a receptacle, pour four taels of mercury over it, and nurture for seven days—upon opening, it has already become supreme treasure. Wait until sprouts fill the vessel before harvesting, then fire to form treasure. With prolonged nurturing, it becomes a cold forest of jade trees.

**Eighth Cycle**
Take twenty-four taels of cold forest powder and twelve taels of previously nurtured cinnabar, grind evenly with one *jin* of raw sulfur, place in a sealed vessel, and nurture for seven days before removing. Pour four taels of mercury over it, nurture with fire for three seven-day periods—its sprouts will all turn yellow. Fire to form *geng*.

**Ninth Cycle**
In preparing the medicine, choose an auspicious day. Take the spirit sand from the eighth cycle to form a sealed vessel, with a fire regimen of one tael per day. Two taels on the second day. Three taels on the third day.

Continue the fifteenth day, then remove. Use a cold furnace, bathe for sixteen days, and store one tael. On the first day of the next month, resume nurturing—after three years, the Great Elixir will be complete. Once the elixir is formed, dried mercury becomes a golden figure. If consumed, one ascends in flight. Mix one pearl with honey and take with frankincense decoction; even chickens and dogs that ingest it instantly transform into dragons and phoenixes.

**Secret Method of Precious Niter by Immortal Ge**
Take niter in any quantity, boil it with rehmannia juice and oilseed rape juice, then place it inside a phoenix embryo. Use Kunlun paper pasted to a thickness of one grain of rice, cover the embryo shell with talcum powder, then seal the top with several sheets of mica. Cover with white tiger, seal tightly, and calcine with one *cheng* of fire until it turns five colors with patterns—marvelous beyond words. This niter serves as a crucible to nurture spirit sand and cinnabar powder into treasure, even more wondrous than other crucibles. It is called the **Crucible of Grand Yang** or the **Crucible of Pure Yang**.

**Method for Parting the Embryo to Reveal Treasure**
Take eight taels of fire-tamed niter, crush and grind into coarse powder, place in a crucible to nurture various mineral medicines. For two taels of cinnabar, wrap it in silver foil, then cover with one layer of Kunlun paper, place in the crucible, and nurture with half a *jin* of *mao-you* fire for three days—it will truly die, its color unchanged, the silver foil unbroken, allowing it to be mixed with mercury to form treasure. For two taels of realgar, wrap it in *geng* foil, place in the crucible as before, nurture with six taels of fire for five days—it will truly die, its color unchanged, and can transmute silver into ten-tenths *geng*. For two taels of orpiment, nurture with fire as before to transmute silver into *geng*. For two taels of seven-tenths yang candidate, first wrap it in Kunlun paper, then coat with stone-center yellow mixed with rice vinegar, dry in shade overnight, place in the crucible the next day, nurture with six taels of fire for three days—it will truly die, its color like cinnabar, with a radiant red flame, dazzling to behold. Black sand and grass sand do not retreat from the furnace. For two taels of powdery frost, wrap it in silver foil, then cover with one layer of Kunlun paper, place in the crucible, nurture with four taels of fire for three days—it will truly die, becoming even harder, the silver foil unbroken, able to transmute red stubborn metal into white, with a thousand transformations. For two taels of arsenic, wrap it in one or two layers of Kunlun paper, place in the crucible—nurture with fire for one day and it will die, its embryonic color unchanged, and can transmute copper. For two taels of chalcanthite, wrap it in gold foil as before, then cover with Kunlun paper, nurture with six taels of fire for three days—it will naturally truly die, its color like red gold, able to transmute silver into eight-tenths *geng*. For borax, niter, and alum, wrap them in foil and nurture to death, using only one layer of Kunlun paper, place in the crucible, nurture with fire for five days as appropriate—they will naturally truly die, their embryonic color unchanged.

**Nine Cycles and Sixteen Transformations of Spirit Sand Great Elixir**

**First Cycle**
Take half a *jin* of imported sulfur, shape into lumps, and boil with half a *jin* each of *ma-ti* fragrance and *hu-er* grass in two *dou* of river water for seven *fu* periods. Take half a *jin* of mercury, boil with four taels each of Sichuan pepper and *qiang-hua* root for seven *fu* periods. Use a new iron pan, first melt two taels of sulfur, then add eight taels of mercury, stir-fry into sand, grind evenly, place in a water-fire crucible, seal tightly, and fire with five *jin* of fire for three days and nights.

**Second Cycle**
Take the spirit sand from the first cycle, add two taels of sulfur, melt in the pan, add the first-cycle sand, stir-fry, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with three *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with two *jin* of fire for one day.

**Third Cycle**
Take the sand from the second cycle, add one tael of sulfur, melt in the pan, add the sand, stir-fry, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with three *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day.

**Fourth Cycle**
Take the sand from the third cycle, add one tael of sulfur, stir-fry, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with two *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day.

**Fifth Cycle**
Take the sand from the fourth cycle, add seven *qian* and a half of sulfur, stir-fry, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with half a *jin* of fire for one day.

**Sixth Cycle**
Take the sand from the fifth cycle, add half a tael of sulfur, stir-fry, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with half a *jin* of fire for one day.

**Seventh Cycle**
Grind the sand from the sixth cycle, add one tael of raw cinnabar, grind and stir-fry together, place in the crucible, and fire with three *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with half a *jin* of fire for one day.

**Eighth Cycle**
Take the sand from the seventh cycle, add one tael of raw cinnabar, grind and stir-fry together, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with one *jin* of fire for one day. Then fire with half a *jin* of fire for one day.

**Ninth Cycle**
Take the previously completed sand, melt one *jin* of fine silver into beads, nurture the sand within, place in a sealed vessel, set in an ash pool, and fire with three taels of fire for seven days. Remove and bathe. Then use this sand to nurture new sand into treasure—its transformations are boundless. Strike a crane’s crown with one grain of the elixir, and even a skilled archer will miss it for days, hence it is called spirit sand. In healing, it is as swift as the wind sweeping away floating clouds, with the wondrous power to revive the dead, restore youth, and reverse aging—its efficacy cannot be fully described.

**First Transformation**
Take one *jin* of mercury, mix with three taels each of green vitriol, chalcanthite, and white alum, two taels each of green *guan* and white *guan*, and one tael of niter, grind together, boil in one *dou* of rice vinegar for three days, then bathe clean. Boil imported sulfur with *ma-ti* fragrance and *yu-xing* grass for three days, melt two taels of sulfur in an iron pan, add eight taels of mercury, stir-fry into sand, place in the crucible, and fire with five *jin* of fire for one day.

**Second Transformation**
Fire with two *jin* for one day. Fire with half a *jin* for one day. Remove and form into blocks, boil in pine-yellow ash liquid for one *fu* period. Wash clean, then coat with honey and apply silver foil to the surface. Place in the former silver-pearl chamber and nurture for seven days. On the first day, two taels of fire. From the second to the fourth day, three taels. From the fifth to the seventh day, four taels of fire to completion.

**Third Transformation**
Take the former nine-cycle Great Elixir Mother and break into small pieces. First place half into the vessel, then spread the newly nurtured sand within, and cover with the remaining half of the Elixir Mother. Seal firmly in the ash pool and nurture for seven days. First two taels, then three, then four, then five taels to completion. Remove. Nurture the sand in this manner seven times to obtain fourteen taels of Elixir Head. Store each separately, then boil with *chao-sheng* grass for one day.

**Fourth Transformation**
Use the newly nurtured sand from the third cycle. Pound to powder in an iron mortar, wrap in a layer of Kunlun paper, then coat the sand with a paste made from *di-ding* flower, croton seeds, and castor beans. Place in the vessel, seal tightly, and set in the furnace. Fire with half a *cheng* for one night. Cool and remove—a piece like jade. This is the supreme treasure. Crush again to form a chamber.

**Fourth Transformation**
Take the previously fired jade-like sand pieces and form them into lumps. Grind *fen-shuang* (powdered frost), *liu-sha* (sal ammoniac), and *peng-sha* (borax) into equal parts of powder. Roll the sand lumps in honey, then coat them thoroughly with this powder. Wrap in Kunlun paper, place a lotus before them, and set within the *Sheng Wu Zhi* chamber. Nurture in the ash pool for seven days with four taels of fire. The white body becomes a treasure. This elixir must undergo seven cycles before completion and storage.

**Fifth Transformation**
Take the previously nurtured white-body chamber and place it within the crucible. Pour two taels of mercury over it, seal tightly, and set in the ash pool. Nurture with two to three taels of fire for seven days. Open, then pour another two taels of mercury, and nurture for another seven days. Repeat this process twice more, each time adding two taels of mercury and nurturing for seven days—twenty-eight days in total. Then add three taels of mercury, and nurture with yin fire four times over twenty-eight days. For the fourth cycle, add four taels of mercury and six taels of yin fire, another twenty-eight days. Finally, pour five taels of mercury with six taels of fire, completing four cycles of twenty-eight days each.

**Sixth Transformation**
Take the previously nurtured *yu-xiao* (jade laughter) without damaging it, and place it in a silver-inlaid box. Set upon a fire furnace with five taels of yin fire, and pour five taels of mercury. Replenish every three days, repeating this process endlessly. When removed, it will resemble a forest of jade trees, its form like a head, red as coral. Break it to reveal the treasure.

**Seventh Transformation**
Grind two taels of the previous *yu-xiao* into fine powder. First place half in the crucible, then add one tael each of realgar, orpiment, sulfur, and *liu-sha*, all ground together, into the crucible. Cover with the remaining half of *yu-xiao* powder, seal tightly, and subdue with one jin of yin fire for three days. Remove—a lump like gold. Crush four taels, add one tael of cinnabar, and warm for seven days with four taels of fire. Remove and refine by smoke to achieve the finest purple *mo-jin* (polished gold). For the second cycle, nurture two taels of cinnabar for seven days with four taels of fire.

**Eighth Transformation**
Take the previously nurtured eight taels of cinnabar, pour two taels of mercury, and nurture with four taels of yin fire and four taels of *zheng* fire for seven days to form the treasure. Replenish with mercury every seven days, cycling endlessly. At this stage, proceed according to one’s karmic capacity.

**Ninth Transformation**
Take half a jin of sulfur, melt it in a jumping vessel, add two taels of mercury, and stir-fry until black. Grind into powder. Layer the powder from the seventh transformation’s Three Yellows over it, seal tightly, and nurture with four taels of fire for three days, then six taels of fire for four days. Pour four taels of mercury to form the finest mountain-and-marsh white treasure. Continue this process in seven-day cycles with fire, completing forty-nine days in total.

**Tenth Transformation**
Grind the elixir head from the ninth transformation into powder. Place an iron jumping vessel with five taels of mercury beneath, and apply half a jin of fire. Sprinkle three qian of the elixir powder over it, seal with a lid, and reinforce with damp paper. When the cicada’s song ceases, cease firing—a single firing yields five taels of mountain-and-marsh supreme treasure.

**Eleventh Transformation**
Take one tael of the ninth transformation’s jade powder and one tael of mercury refined in the tenth transformation, grind them together into powder. Melt one jin of red silver, add one tael of this powder, and it will transform into a white-body supreme treasure.

**Twelfth Transformation**
Combine one tael of the Three Yellows from the seventh transformation, one tael of cinnabar from the sixth transformation, and one tael of mercury from the tenth transformation into a cake. Place in the crucible and nurture for seven days before storage. Then, within the *yao* vessel, add five taels of mercury to the previous mixture, nurturing to produce four *shen* and two qian. Cover with a lid, apply half a jin of fire below, and when the cicada’s song begins, increase the fire for one firing to form the finest purple *chang* supreme treasure.

**Thirteenth Transformation**
Take five taels of mercury-sulfur from the ninth transformation, add one tael each of the finest realgar, orpiment, sulfur, and *peng-sha*, grind together, and place in a sealed vessel. Nurture in the furnace for twenty-one days, using two taels of fire by day and four taels by night. Remove to transmute the Five Metals and Eight Stones into supreme treasure.

**Fourteenth Transformation**
Form the Three Yellows from the previous refinement into a chamber, nurture two taels of the finest cinnabar within for twenty-one days—first with two taels of fire, then three, then four to completion. Remove the cinnabar, grind it with the Three Yellows into powder, and shape into pellets the size of soybeans with dew water. Ingest with flowing water to prolong life by a hundred years, attain immortality, and move as swiftly as a galloping horse.

**Fifteenth Transformation**
Take the previously nurtured cinnabar, refine it into gold, and cast a divine crucible large enough to hold the ingredients. Also cast an iron crucible, lining its interior with a paste of mica, *zeng-qing* (azurite), rock crystal, *hu-zhong-ying* stone, and lead dan, mixed with paper mulberry juice. Place the divine chamber within, then select a high and auspicious site to construct a hut and altar for the refinement of the Great Elixir.

**Sixteenth Transformation**
First, take two jin of mercury from the fourteenth transformation’s Three Yellows and three jin of *er-ba* divine cinnabar, mix and grind evenly, then pound thirty thousand times. Place in the divine crucible and seal tightly. Then set within the large iron crucible, sealing all seams securely. Reinforce with *liu-yi* mud, place in the ash pool or Heaven-and-Earth furnace. Align the upper water and lower fire crucibles, and nurture with five jin of fire for one month, three jin for another month, one jin for another month, and five jin for ten days—one hundred days in total. Remove and bury in the earth to dispel fire qi for one year. Then suspend in well water for one hundred days. Remove, grind thirty thousand times into powder, and form into pellets the size of mung beans with sweet dew water. Return to the divine chamber and nurture with four taels of fire for seven days. When complete, remove. Feed one pellet to a chicken, and it will transform into a phoenix and fly away; feed one to a dog, and it will become a dragon and soar.

With this elixir, offer thanks to Heaven and Earth and the Northern Dipper. Discard one portion in renowned mountains and great rivers, then it may be ingested to attain true immortality. Without sufficient virtue and power, one cannot reach this stage—proceed with caution. Once a person has taken it, soak it in golden sweet-dew juice, grind it thoroughly three times a month, and dispel the fire toxin before consumption, ascending directly to the ranks of immortals. The practice must prioritize aiding the poor and delivering all beings—this is proper. During refinement, each transformation may be ingested in stages, yet nothing compares to completing nine cycles and sixteen transformations, where success reveals its wondrous efficacy, truly the stuff of immortals. The key lies in unwavering resolve and diligent practice; none who persist shall fail to achieve it.

**External Elixir: Method for Preparing a Silver Receptacle**
Pound silver into thin sheets, dip in vinegar, and sprinkle with sulfur powder. Cover with five to seven leaves of paddy-field grass, seal all seams, and heat until glowing red. Allow to cool, then grind into powder.

**Cinnabar Method**
Take one tael of fine cinnabar, one *fen* each of native sulfur and *que* sulfur, and half a *fen* of borax. Mix with vinegar and fermented water in a porcelain vessel, and boil for three days and nights. If the vinegar evaporates, keep a separate vessel of warm vinegar by the fire to replenish it gradually, ensuring it lasts a full day. Remove, wash with warm water, and measure the quantity of the substance. Seal in a vessel of appropriate size: first spread a layer of silver powder, then fill with cinnabar. Seal the seams with honey-mixed clamshell powder, let dry, and place in an ash pool, covering the top with ash to the thickness of a finger.

Begin with one and a half taels of fire, nurturing for three days. Then add two taels of fire, nurturing for seven days. Next, add three taels of fire, nurturing until twenty days. Then increase by one tael of fire up to forty taels, nurturing for forty-nine days. Remove and heat over fire until subdued, then it may be used. To refine silver, melt it in a lead crucible. To enhance the receptacle, do not grind the final product; instead, layer and nurture as before, increasing the fire by one day. Apply fire at midnight and noon, strictly adhering to the schedule.

**Three Sages Method (also called Minor Ninefold Dryness)**
Take ten taels of fine cinnabar, one tael of sulfur, and one tael of mercury. Grind the three ingredients together for a full day until extremely fine, with no visible mercury. Press firmly into a vessel, then add one tael of fresh *fo’er* grass (i.e., *yunjiang*) pounded with one *qian* of salt. Grind further into a paste and spread over the vessel’s lid as sealing medicine. Outside the vessel, mix stone fat, *shengwuzhi*, sacred ash, and vinegar-charcoal ash into a mud, and seal the vessel’s opening securely.

Select an auspicious site and dig a pit one *chi* and two *cun* deep and wide. Drive a nail to secure the fire gate, then purify the pit inside and out with hot vinegar mixed with two *qian* of charcoal ash. Place the vessel inside, stabilize it, and sift fine charcoal ash over it until covered to the thickness of a finger. Add another layer of charcoal ash five *cun* thick on top, then apply fire as follows:
- First day: one *jin* of fire.
- Second day: two *jin* of fire.

On the third day, apply three *jin* of fire. On the fourth day, apply one *cheng*. Calcine with charcoal fire for a full day, then cease. Wait until completely cooled before opening the sixth vent to retrieve the vessel. Upon inspection, the cinnabar will appear as blood-red specks, resembling a mirror’s surface.

For the right-hand ingredient: take one *liang* of cinnabar, grind it to an extremely fine powder, and affix it to the vessel’s lid with paper. Replace the leaves and proceed as before, sealing the vessel securely. The firing process may be repeated three, five, six, or seven times, each following the initial method. The sealing and firing for the eighth iteration remain identical.

Remove the vessel’s contents, grind finely, and add the following ingredients: one *qian* each of saltpeter, sal ammoniac, alum, green vitriol, willow vitriol, and borax. Grind these together with the aforementioned powder, pack tightly into the vessel, and spread one *liang* of finely ground sulfur on top. Seal the vessel securely. The sealing medicine and firing method remain as previously described.

Apply four *liang* of fire and nurture for seven days. Then apply half a *jin* of fire and nurture for another seven days. Finally, apply one *jin* of fire and nurture for seven days. Afterward, use one *cheng* of fire to refine the contents fully. Once cooled, retrieve the vessel—the sulfur will have risen to the top, separate from the other ingredients. Gently scoop it out with a spoon and set it aside; do not mix it with the cinnabar powder.

Grind the previously calcined base powder finely, add one *liang* of the refined cinnabar, and grind them together. Place the mixture into the vessel, seal it securely, and apply fire as in the eighth iteration, using one *cheng* of fire until fully refined. Retrieve the contents, grind finely, and divide into three portions.

For one portion: mix with red rice paste to form pills, each weighing one *qian*. When used in shade, one *qian* of this pill can dry ten *liang* of mercury. Place the mercury in a crucible, apply half a *jin* of mature fire to heat it until a faint smoke rises, then sprinkle one crushed pill on top. Immediately place a lit stick of mature fire across the crucible’s mouth; the mercury will scatter with a hissing sound. Once the sound ceases, heap three *jin* of fire around it and calcine until glowing red. Carefully pour the contents into a quenching pit, cover with damp paper, and retrieve the product without loss.

For another portion: add one *liang* each of high-quality orpiment and fine blue vitriol, grind together, and place into the vessel. Seal as before, bury in the ash pit, and apply three *jin* of fire, nurturing for three days. Then apply two *cheng* of fire to refine fully. Once cooled, retrieve and grind the contents. One *liang* of this powder, divided into ten parts, can dry ten *liang* of mercury each, producing a superior *gengxin* substance.

For the final portion: add one *liang* of *fen shuang*, grind thoroughly, place into the vessel, and seal as before. Apply two *cheng* of fire to calcine until red, then cool and retrieve. Grind finely; one *liang* of this powder, divided into ten parts, can condense ten *liang* of mercury into treasure. *Textual variants noted.*

**Embryo-Shedding Sprout**
Take one *liang* of mercury-subduing cinnabar, add one *liang* of mercury refined with yellow *ken*, and apply three *liang* of top-fire. Alternate the fire at *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours, nurturing for three *mou* periods until the mercury is subdued, resembling jade laughter. Repeat the refining and nurturing as before; select only the firm and mature portions for use, calling this the *Embryo-Shedding Sprout*. Perform this four times over twelve days, after which transmutation refining may begin.

**Mother-Detached Sprout**
For transmutation refining, use five *liang* of *Embryo-Shedding Sprout* and four *liang* of refined mercury, applying four *liang* of top-fire. Nurture for three *mou* periods, using a water cauldron below. Repeat this six times over eighteen days to obtain twenty-four *liang*. The substance will naturally form into flakes and lumps, with no adhesion between earlier and later stages—this is called the *Mother-Detached Sprout*. Bathe it in the *Flowery Pond*, expose it to the dew for one night, and the *Embryo-Shedding Sprout* will become azure-green and hard as stone.

**Flowery Pond Method**
Use sulfur, sal ammoniac, borax, and green vitriol, adding one *sheng* of pure wine; all else remains the same.

**Heaven-Produced Yellow Sprout**
Cinnabar, chalcanthite, and Chinese gall—grind these three ingredients together and sift into a fine powder. Moisten the cinnabar with rice vinegar, then coat it evenly and thickly in the center. Wrap it tightly in *Head Gold Sand*, using the *finger-wrapping method*, with one *dou* of rice vinegar and one *liang* of green salt. Suspend and boil until dry. For each *liang* of cinnabar, mix in three *liang* of finely ground *Embryo-Shedding Sprout* powder, then place in a yellow *ken* for subduing fire. Seal the opening with salt, apply one *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *yin*, *wu*, and *xu* hours, and nurture for seven *mou* periods. When complete, the salt will have dissolved entirely. Retrieve the cinnabar, peel away the *Head Gold Sand*, wash the cinnabar clean—it will be uniformly red as gold, but do not melt it. For each *liang*, add five *liang* of mercury, grind evenly, and place in the *Spirit Chamber*. Set it within the yellow *ken*, seal the opening, and apply half a *jin* of fire to calcine until half dry. Add another *jin* of fire, and when the fire has fully subsided, retrieve it cold. The mercury will have dried, resembling gold—this is called *Heaven-Produced Yellow Sprout*, also known as *White Horse Sprout* or *True Lead*. The cinnabar will have ascended to the top of the *Spirit Chamber*, light as a wasp’s nest—this is the *True Purple River Chariot*, ready for use.

For each *liang* of *Heaven-Produced Yellow Sprout*, add three *liang* of mercury. Apply four *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, and nurture for one *pan* period until the mercury is dry. For every three *liang* of dried mercury, mix in cinnabar or *Spirit Sand*, grind evenly, and place in an iron vessel to refine the mercury—the mercury will not be exhausted.

**Purple Gold and White Snow**
Grind two *liang* of purple powder, one *liang* of mercury, and one *liang* of sulfur together until no specks remain and no sound is heard. Place in the *Great One’s Heavenly Palace*, set within a yellow *ken*, and apply two *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, nurturing for five *sui* periods. Add one *liang* of mercury and nurture again, increasing the mercury to ten *liang* as before. When retrieved, the elixir body will disperse, its color like gold. Each *qian* can refine five *liang* of mercury into purple gold. Its power is equal to the Great Elixir. When a small amount is tossed into the air, it transforms into white snow, rising higher and farther until its bounds are unknowable. Melt and shape it into spoons or chopsticks for use—if poison is encountered, the poison will scatter and disperse.

Refine five *liang* of purple powder with rice vinegar, fashion it into a vessel, and let it dry. Place three *liang* of mercury inside, set it in a yellow *ken*, seal the opening, and apply fire to nurture for one *mou* period—the mercury will dry. Grind one *liang* each of cinnabar, realgar, and orpiment evenly, then mix with two *liang* of hardened purple powder. Seal the opening, apply two *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, and nurture for ten *pan* periods. Retrieve, grind finely, and form into pills the size of *mung beans* with paper mulberry juice. Each pill can instantly dry five *liang* of mercury. Cover three *liang* of cinnabar with four *liang* of *Four Spirits*, apply two *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for seven *mou* periods. Retrieve, grind finely, and form into pills the size of *soybeans* with paper mulberry juice—these can revive the dead.

Grind half a *jin* of purple powder and one *jin* of mercury together until no specks remain, place in a yellow *ken*, seal the opening, and apply four *liang* of top-fire to nurture for one *mou* period—this can transmute the Five Metals into treasure. Grind one *liang* each of *Purple River Chariot* and cinnabar with four *liang* of realgar evenly, place in an iron vessel, seal tightly, and apply two *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, nurturing for forty-nine days. Add one *liang* of mercury, grind evenly, apply five *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, and nurture for five *pan* periods. Refine five *liang* of mercury as before—the mercury will dry and transform entirely into gold, its refining and nurturing inexhaustible. This is called the *Immortal’s Golden Valley and Jade-Field Transmutation Method*.

Grind one *liang* each of *Purple River Chariot* and cinnabar with four *liang* of realgar evenly, place in an iron vessel, seal tightly, and apply two *liang* of top-fire, alternating at *mao* and *you* hours, nurturing for forty-nine *pan* periods. Add one *liang* of mercury, grind until no specks remain, apply two *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for seven *mou* periods. Add mercury and nurture again, following the previous method until the mercury reaches one *jin*. When retrieved, its color will be like radiant purple gold. Grind finely and form into pills the size of sesame seeds with paper mulberry juice—each pill can refine one *jin* of mercury into purple gold.

Cover one *liang* of *Purple River Chariot* with one *liang* of realgar, place in the *Great One’s Heavenly Palace*, set within a yellow *ken*, and apply two *liang* of top-fire to nurture for three *mou* periods before retrieving. Grind the realgar finely, and for each half-*liang*, stir in ten *liang* of mercury in an iron pan. Follow the usual method until the sound ceases, then nurture for one *mou* period, gradually intensifying the heat until it glows red throughout, forming purple gold.

Grind four *liang* of *Purple River Chariot* with half a *jin* of mercury until no specks remain, place in an iron vessel, seal tightly, and apply two *liang* of top-fire to nurture for forty-nine *pan* periods.

Grind finely, then nurture for another year, mix with grain juice, and form into pills the size of sesame seeds—each pill can refine one *jin* of mercury into purple gold.

Take five *liang* each of *White Gold Sand* and mercury, and congeal them into granules. Cover with *Yellow-White Gold Essence*, place in a yellow *ken*, apply one and a half *liang* of top-fire, and alternate between *mao* and *you* periods to nurture for seven *pan* periods until complete, naming it *Precious Shoot*. Divide into two portions: use one portion to congeal mercury into granules, following the previous method in every step. Divide, congeal, and nurture again—after nine transformations, it can transmute the Five Metals.

Nurture *Precious Shoot* with mercury, regulating the fire, furnace, and crucible as in the method for nurturing the *Elixir Head*. After ten infusions, the *Precious Shoot*’s power is exhausted; it may then be smelted into silver, also called *Immortal’s Golden Grain* or *Jade-Field Guard*.

Grind the sprouts of *Precious Shoot* finely, cover with five *liang* of cinnabar, place in a yellow *jian*, apply five *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for five *mou* periods. Retrieve without altering its innate color, then mix with raw cinnabar in equal measure, grind evenly, place in the *Great One’s Heavenly Palace*, set within a yellow *zheng*, and nurture with gentle fire for twenty-one *mou* periods. When the cinnabar’s body disperses into a golden hue, it is called *Red-Stone Cinnabar*. Used to make *Bright Window Dust*, it is a most wondrous thing.

**White Horse Tooth Transformation Method**
Melt eight *liang* of yellow gold in a crucible with *qi*-fire and saltpeter, stirring until fully dissolved. Grind *White Horse Tooth* finely, and add one *daorui* at a time to the molten liquid until completely dissolved. Once settled, place the crucible in ash, chill thoroughly, and break it open to naturally separate the embryo, naming it *Yellow Sprout*.

Grind equal parts *Yellow Sprout* and cinnabar finely, place in a crucible (filling no more than seven-tenths), cover with a tile shard leaving a vent, and melt with fire. Place in ash, chill thoroughly, and break open to reveal the cinnabar subdued, its color like molten silver. Cut into dice, wrap in fine silk, and suspend in a sand pot. Add equal parts *green salt*, *sal ammoniac*, *pomegranate rind*, and *oil-acid*, then boil in fermented water for one *pan* period. Rinse with boiling water forty-five times to remove all medicinal residue, then dry by baking.

For each *jin*, grind with four *liang* of mercury until no specks remain. Place in a yellow *ken*, seal tightly, and once dry, set upon a level ash mound. Surround with five *jin* of charcoal (half raw, half cooked), and fire until spent.
