When cold, retrieve the mercury—it will have fully merged with the cinnabar, its essence and marrow transformed without the slightest loss, called *True Subdued-Fire Silver-Colored Cinnabar*.

Grind twenty *liang* of *Silver-Colored Cinnabar* finely. Spread eight *liang* on the bottom of a yellow *zheng*, place ten *liang* of cinnabar in the center coated with silver powder, then cover with twelve *liang* of *Silver-Colored Cinnabar*, pressing firmly. Seal tightly, apply four to five *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for seven *pan* periods. Fire with three to two *jin* of charcoal until spent, then retrieve when cold. The cinnabar that enters the vessel grants longevity; the longer it endures, the more potent it becomes. If the cinnabar turns black as iron, after a thousand refinements it will still yield golden liquid, its essence unshaken and without the slightest loss—this is called *Iron-Colored Cinnabar*. Hammered into pellets the size of rabbit droppings, it can transmute the Five Metals.

Melt one *liang* each of *Copper Snail Stone*, black lead, and *White Iron* into liquid, then add seven *qian* of *Iron-Colored Cinnabar* and stir over a blazing fire until clear. Pour into ash, chill thoroughly, and break open—the cinnabar will remain intact on top, while the Five Metals below will have transformed into *Snowflake Mercury Silver*. If the cinnabar’s transmutative power weakens, grind it finely to make the outer vessel for *Red Lychee Silver*.

For cinnabar the size of imperial pearls, wrap it in *Three-Seven Sand* granules, then encase in two layers of *Kunlun* paper and silk. Boil with *white alum* (which blooms at dawn and withers by dusk) in flowing water for a day, then trim evenly. After transmuting with *Iron-Colored Cinnabar*, grind seven *qian* finely, knead with honey into a paste, wrap again in two layers of *Kunlun* paper, seal with refined mud, and dry. Surround with four *jin* of charcoal on the ground, then heap three *jin* of cooked fire to heat until thoroughly red. Turn the ball and add the remaining fire, then remove the heat when eight-tenths spent. When cold, retrieve the granules and cinnabar—both will have become supreme treasures, called *Red Lychee Iron-Colored Cinnabar*. Though unaltered and without loss, its power is further diminished.

If gathered to one *jin*, grind with four *liang* of mercury until no specks remain, place in a yellow *zheng*, seal tightly, and once dry, set steadily on level ground. Encase in a damp ash mound, surround with five *jin* of charcoal (half raw, half cooked), and fire until spent. When cold, retrieve without the slightest loss, forming *Longevity Granules* for the vessel.

Divide ten *liang* of *Three-Seven Sand* into ten pills, wrap loosely in palm fiber with *white alum* (which blooms at dawn and withers by dusk), and boil in flowing water for a day. Spread eight *liang* of *Longevity Vessel* on the bottom of a yellow *zheng*, arrange the granules evenly atop, then cover with twelve *liang* and press firmly. Seal tightly, apply four *liang* of top-fire, and nurture for seven *mou* periods. Fire with three *jin* of charcoal until thoroughly red, then remove the heat and retrieve when cold—the granules will be fully subdued and unshaken. With prolonged refinement, the vessel’s color gradually yellows, progressing through *Two-Eight* and *One-Nine*, until it reaches *My Lotus*. Through mercury infusions and controlled grinding, the vessel’s hue deepens. Only then can one truly appreciate the cinnabar’s efficacy, distinct from the Eight Stones.

**Longevity Vessel**
Twenty *liang* of cinnabar, two *liang* each of realgar and orpiment. Half a *liang* each of *yellow alum*, *chalcanthite*, *willow-floss alum*, and *grape green*. Weigh the seven ingredients, grind evenly, and wrap in two layers of fine silk. Measure portions of *sal ammoniac*, realgar, orpiment, *yellow alum*, *black alum*, *malachite*, *green salt*, *hematite*, and *willow-floss alum*.

Weigh the nine ingredients, grind evenly to a fine powder, and place them in rice vinegar. Suspend and boil for the duration of two watches. Remove and dry over a slow fire, then place in a yellow vessel, seal tightly, and wait until dry. Use five *jin* of firewood, allowing the fire to extinguish naturally on the ground. Once cooled, remove the light and floating particles, grind finely to form a vessel, and nurture the golden cinnabar granules—every step follows the method for nurturing silver cinnabar. With prolonged refinement, the vessel may nurture cinnabar as well, just as cinnabar is nurtured, each granule penetrating to the core. This is called *Golden Elixir Embracing Gold*, which, when smelted, becomes gold. However, both golden cinnabar and cinnabar must first be boiled in the nine-flavor vinegar for the duration of one watch before they can be nurtured. The nine-flavor vinegar may be stored for prolonged use; if depleted, more vinegar may be added.

**Medicine for Treating Severe Leprosy: Divine Response Great Wind Pill**
Size of *tung* seeds. For severe cases, take twenty pills; for mild cases, ten or five.
- *Danggui* (Chinese angelica) one *liang*
- *Quanxie* (scorpion) one *liang*
- *Dafengzi* (chaulmoogra) one *jin*
- *Zhangnao* (camphor) one *liang*
- Mercury
- *Fangfeng* (saposhnikovia)
- *Heshouwu* (fleeceflower root)
- *Qianghuo* (notopterygium) each five *qian*
- *Baiyou* (white mustard)
- *Baizhi* (angelica dahurica)
- *Ruxiang* (frankincense)
- *Cangzhu* (atractylodes) each three *qian*
- *Dahuang* (rhubarb) two *liang* (processed with heated wine)
- *Gancao* (licorice)
- *Chenpi* (tangerine peel) each one *liang*
- *Shexiang* (musk) one or two *qian* as available

A poem says:
*Danggui, Quanxie, Dafengzi, camphor—each the same,*
*Mercury, Fangfeng, Heshouwu, Qianghuo—five qian dry.*
*Baiyou, Baizhi, Ruxiang, Cangzhu—three parts complete,*
*Dahuang, Gancao, Chenpi, musk—none may rest easy.*

Form the above ingredients into pills using glutinous rice paste, each the size of a *tung* seed. Take twenty pills on an empty stomach with plain hot water, followed by congee. Avoid the following: soot from the bottom of pots, radish heads, Chinese yam, jujubes, persimmons (remove the frost), cucumbers, watermelons, winter melons, raw melons, lotus roots, water caltrops, sugarcane, eggplants, sugar, white fish, saltwater fish, yellow and white foods, sea snails, and *qiongzhi*. No other foods may be consumed, or the condition may relapse and become untreatable. Good wine may be consumed, but sexual activity must be avoided.

*Geng Dao Ji*, Scroll Nine—conclusion.
